Harris-Walsh, Inc. v. Dickson City


No. 55, January Term, 1966


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


420 Pa. 259; 216 A.2d 329; 1966 Pa. LEXIS 761


October 1, 1965, Argued  
January 17, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, March T., 1964, No. 1, in case of Harris-Walsh, Inc., Parmoff Corporation and Moffat Coal Company v. Borough of Dickson City.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania) entered a decree nisi in favor of plaintiff strip miner and held defendant borough's ordinance that regulated the future mining of anthracite coal invalid and permanently enjoined the borough from its enforcement. The borough appealed the decree.


OVERVIEW: The borough passed an ordinance that regulated the mining of anthracite coal by the strip mine method within its territorial limits. The strip miner argued that the ordinance was invalid because the commonwealth had preempted the regulation of strip mining. The court affirmed the decree and held the ordinance invalid and enjoined the borough from its enforcement. The court first determined that the lower court had equity jurisdiction because the strip miner's only remedy at law would have subjected it to criminal prosecution, and thus it was not an adequate remedy at law to divest the lower court of equity jurisdiction. The commonwealth's Anthracite Strip Mining Law, 52 P.S. § 681.1 et seq., which provided for the improvement and conservation of lands affected by the strip mining of anthracite coal, vested exclusive jurisdiction over coal stripping operations in a state agency. The use of the words "exclusive jurisdiction" showed the legislature's intent that only the commonwealth was to regulate the anthracite strip mining industry. Thus, legislative action in the same field by any political subdivision, such as the borough, was precluded.


OUTCOME: The decree in favor of the strip miner that enjoined the borough from enforcing its ordinance regulating the future mining of anthracite coal was affirmed.

Faranda Appeal


No. 307, January Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


420 Pa. 295; 216 A.2d 769; 1966 Pa. LEXIS 765


October 11, 1965, Argued  
January 17, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Refused February 28, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, April T., 1965, No. 15, in re matter of condemnation of certain parcels of land in First Ward of City of Lancaster condemned by Redevelopment Authority, being property formerly of Tony Faranda.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his preliminary objection to a declaration of taking filed by appellee redevelopment authority.


OVERVIEW: The authority filed a declaration of taking of certain properties in order to carry out a redevelopment plan of an area that had been certified as a blighted area. The owner's property was affected by the plan, and he filed preliminary objections to the declaration of taking. The lower court dismissed the owner's objections. The court vacated the order and remanded. The court held that the lower court erred in dismissing the owner's objection to the authority's power and right to condemn the property because he asserted that it was not blighted. Section 406(a)(1) of the Eminent Domain Code provided that preliminary objections were the exclusive method of challenging the power or right of the condemnor to appropriate the condemned property unless the same had been previously adjudicated. The authority declared that the area was blighted, thereby making the thrust of the owner's attack directly to the authority's power, not to its wisdom. Preliminary objections constituted the exclusive method of challenging the power of the authority to take private property.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order dismissing the owner's preliminary objection to the authority's declaration of taking and remanded the case with directions to the lower court to take testimony on the question of whether the area was in fact blighted.

 

246 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Robinson v. Myers


No. 16, May Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


420 Pa. 72; 215 A.2d 637; 1966 Pa. LEXIS 739


May 24, 1965, Submitted  
January 4, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of York County, Aug. T., 1964, No. 372, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Harvey Robinson v. David N. Myers, Superintendent.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated and record remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a habeas corpus proceeding, appellant inmate sought review of from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his petition without a hearing following his conviction for manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged a number of trial errors, which the trial court below refused to entertain. The inmate contended that his trial counsel declined to undertake an appeal and that while imprisoned he was without funds or knowledge to perfect an appeal absent such assistance. Thus, the inmate contended, although entitled to appellate review as of right, the refusal of his appointed counsel to undertake the appeal effectively prevented him from exercising that right. The court held that where a state provided appellate review of criminal convictions as of right, it might not afford such review to indigents on terms less favorable than those afforded non-indigents. Furthermore, absence of a waiver, a state might not refuse to provide an indigent defendant with assistance of counsel on appeal as of right. The court held that the right to the assistance of counsel on appeal necessarily included the right to such assistance in the critical task of taking and perfecting an appeal. Therefore, the inmate might not be foreclosed from exercising his right to appellate review if his failure to assert the right was the result of an unconstitutional deprivation of the assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order and remanded the record.

Philadelphia v. Price


No. 316, January Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 564; 215 A.2d 661; 1966 Pa. LEXIS 841


October 7, 1965, Argued  
January 4, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 8 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1964, No. 4667, in case of City of Philadelphia v. Eli Kirk Price, III, Howard W. Hanson, Jr., Charles J. Ansel et al.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a housing discrimination action, plaintiff city challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 8 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted defendant homeowner's and real estate agent's (homeowner) motion for nonsuit and denied the city's subsequent motion to take off the nonsuit.


OVERVIEW: Complainant, a person of Chinese descent, filed a petition with the Philadelphia Commission on Human Relations (the Commission), charging that the homeowner and his real estate agent had refused to sell to him a home, in violation of the Fair Practices Ordinance, § 9-1104(A)(1) of the Philadelphia Code. The Commission determined that the homeowner did discriminate against the complainant and thereafter, the city brought a suit in equity against the homeowner. On appeal, the city argued that the failure of homeowner to appeal from the order of the Commission prevented him from attacking collaterally that order in an enforcement proceeding. Moreover, the city contended that the Fair Practices Ordinance (Ordinance) did not provide for a trial de novo in an enforcement proceeding. The court held that the homeowner did not have a right of direct appeal and therefore, he could not have waived, by failing to exercise a nonexistent right, the opportunity to attack the order of the Commission. The court further held that the Ordinance did provide for a trial de novo in an enforcement proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision which granted the homeowner's motion for non suit and denied the city's subsequent motion to take off the nonsuit.

Commonwealth ex rel. Thomas v. Myers


No. 334, January Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 577; 215 A.2d 617; 1966 Pa. LEXIS 842


November 12, 1965, Submitted  
January 4, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1965, No. 5857, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Phillip Clark Thomas v. David N. Myers, Superintendent.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging that he was illegally confined beyond the maximum expiration date of his original sentence on a voluntary manslaughter charge and was incarcerated as a "convicted parole violator" without having a hearing.


OVERVIEW: It was beyond question that, after having served the minimum term of his original sentence, the inmate, while on release as a parolee, was convicted of the crime of aggravated robbery and that, after having been released from confinement on the sentence imposed on the charge of aggravated robbery, he was returned to the custody of the Pennsylvania Parole Board and recommitted as a violator of his parole. In the exercise of its discretion, the Board recommitted the inmate and such recommitment extended the date of his maximum term on the original sentence. The court held that such action did not offend any constitutional right belonging to the inmate, because where a prisoner on parole was convicted of another crime, the Board had the authority to recommit the prisoner to serve the balance of the term which he would have been compelled to serve had he not been paroled and to forfeit any credit for the time he was at liberty on parole. The court further held that the inmate was not entitled to a trial on his parole violation, because Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 331.21(a) (1951) only required a hearing before the Board, which the inmate was granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Allen v. West Mifflin


No. 231, March Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 394; 214 A.2d 502; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 521


October 7, 1965, Argued  
November 23, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1964, No. 3856, in case of John E. Allen v. Borough of West Mifflin, Council of West Mifflin, John A. Benyak et al.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of mandamus affirmed; judgment of damages vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Borough of West Mifflin Council (Pennsylvania), challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee employee a writ of mandamus and a judgment for damages.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a Borough police officer and was "retired" pursuant to Borough of West Mifflin, Pa., Ordinance Number 507. The court held that since the ordinance permitted termination of employment as a policeman on grounds which were both not specified within the civil service statutes and not uniform, it was violative of such statutes, and thus invalid. The court also held that as to a delay involved in filing the complaint and adjudicating the case, while there was not enough delay and induced reliance to raise the defense of laches to the writ of mandamus, the trial court had to determine whether the delay was justified by some action which reasonably delayed the filing of a complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of mandamus, vacated the judgment for damages vacated, and remanded the case for further action consistent with the court's opinion in the assessment of damages.

Commonwealth v. Life Assurance Co.


No. 33, May Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 370; 214 A.2d 209; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 518


May 26, 1965, Argued  
November 9, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 65 Commonwealth Docket 1963, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Life Assurance Company of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company challenged a judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) that sustained the imposition of a gross premiums tax under 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2270.1-2270.10.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged, on constitutional and statutory grounds, the imposition of a gross premiums tax on domestic life insurance companies and foreign insurance companies pursuant to 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2270.1 - 2270.10. The trial court sustained the tax, and appellant again challenged, contending that: the tax denied due process and equal protection of the laws based on inequities in taxation of foreign insurers and domestic non-life insurance companies; only life insurance premiums, not those collected from accident and health contracts, were subject to the tax; and premiums collected on policies issued prior to the 1961 enactment were exempt from the tax. The court found that the legislature could reasonably classify taxpayers and impose taxes based on those classifications. Appellant did not meet its burden of establishing that the classification made clearly, palpably and plainly violated the state and federal constitutions. As such, the tax was neither arbitrary nor capricious.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; imposition of a gross premiums tax on domestic life insurance companies did not violate the due process or equal protection guarantees of the United States or Pennsylvania constitutions, because the Legislature could impose a tax based on distinct classifications of taxpayers for the reasonable purpose of collecting revenues.

 

251 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


National Land & Inv. Co. v. Easttown Twp. Bd. of Adjustment


Nos. 183, 186, January Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 504; 215 A.2d 597; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 540


April 29, 1965, Argued  
November 9, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Refused January 17, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Jan. T., 1963, No. 21, and Feb. T., 1964, No. 43, in case of National Land and Investment Company and Dorothy M. Ennis v. Board of Adjustment of Easttown Township, Harold E. Kohn and Edith Kohn, his wife.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania) which held unconstitutional a provision of the township's zoning ordinance, which appellee applicant challenged after its request for a building permit was denied by the township.


OVERVIEW: A township passed a zoning ordinance which required a minimum area of four acres per building lot in certain residential districts in the township. An applicant for a building permit challenged the ordinance as unconstitutional after its request was denied. During a hearing the board of adjustment granted the township's motion to quash the appeal. The lower court reversed that ruling, and the township then appealed. Procedurally, the court determined that lower court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the applicant had filed its appeal within a reasonable time in part because some of the delay was not due to any action or inaction on the part of the applicant. As to the merits of the action, the court held that the four acre minimum requirement in the context of the case was unconstitutional because the particular zoning action was designed to be exclusive and exclusionary and thus did not foster or promote the general welfare. Therefore, the adjustment board committed an error of law in upholding the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order which determined that the township's ordinance was unconstitutional.

 

252 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Reznor Estate


No. 44, March Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 188; 213 A.2d 791; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 489


March 19, 1965, Argued  
October 13, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from decree of Orphans' Court of Mercer County, Sept. T., 1964, No. 1, in the matter of estate of Claud L. Reznor, deceased.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executrix challenged the decision of the Orphans' Court of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed her exceptions to the final account of respondent trustee and directed distribution according to the proposed schedule.


OVERVIEW: Decedent had bequeathed shares of stock, the dividends from which were to be paid by the trustee to decedent's widow and, at her death, were to be divided equally between decedent's children. The trial court approved the trustee's plan to divide the stock into three equal portions, but on review, the court reversed. The court found that certain transactions of 1928 and 1938 represented apportionable events, the mathematical determination of which had to be decided upon remand. The court also found that the executrix was not estopped from receiving the dividends after the widow's death and that no hardship resulted to the trustee if the provisions of the trust were enforced. The court determined that the widow had a vested property right in 1918, when the decedent died, to all property that legally belonged to her under the existing rules of law. The court determined further that those rights to the "income", as represented by the distributions, became vested in each respective year, and the retroactive application of a future statute did not constitutionally extinguish them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree that dismissed the exceptions of the executrix.

 

253 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rieck Inv. Corp.


No. 31, May Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


419 Pa. 52; 213 A.2d 277; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 469


May 25, 1965, Argued  
September 29, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 342 Commonwealth Docket, 1962, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Rieck Investment Corporation.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, (Pennsylvania) that resettled appellee corporation's franchise tax liability to the Commonwealth. The Board of Finance and Review refused the corporation's petition for a review of the resettlement and the trial court had set aside the resettlement.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was a Delaware corporation registered and authorized to do business in Pennsylvania. The corporation conducted business in Florida and its certificate of authority to do business in Florida had been cancelled for nonpayment of corporate taxes. On its franchise tax report in Pennsylvania, it included the value of its two Florida lots. The Commonwealth made resettlement that excluded from the denominator of the tangible property fraction the value of the Florida lots. The issue presented was whether tangible property of the foreign corporation located in a state other than Pennsylvania and that was unrelated to the business done by the corporation in Pennsylvania, should be included in the denominator of the tangible property fraction of the Franchise Tax Act. The court held that the corporation was entitled to include in the denominator of the tangible property fraction the value of its Florida lots, even though such lots were unrelated to the business it conducted in Pennsylvania.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's decision in favor of the corporation that permitted it to include the value of its out-of-state lots in the tangible property fraction denominator.

Bliss Excavating Co. v. Luzerne County


No. 220, January Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


418 Pa. 446; 211 A.2d 532; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 619


April 20, 1965, Argued  
June 30, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, Jan. T., 1965, No. 3, in case of Bliss Excavating Company, Brook Contracting Corporation, Capone Coal Company et al. v. Luzerne County.



DISPOSITION: Decree vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed from a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), which continued a preliminary injunction in favor of plaintiffs, owners of anthracite coal lands and strip mines (strip mine owners), restraining the county from enforcing a zoning ordinance that purported to regulate anthracite strip mining.


OVERVIEW: The county passed a zoning ordinance to regulate the use of land for the excavation of sand, gravel, coal or other minerals, and peat moss for sale. The strip mine owners sought to enjoin the county from enforcing the ordinance, alleging that the ordinance was invalid. They also alleged irreparable harm and the absence of an adequate remedy at law. The court of common pleas granted a preliminary injunction, denied a petition by the county to dissolve the injunction, and continued the injunction. The court vacated and remanded the judgment with directions to dismiss the strip mine owners' complaint as premature. The strip mine owners had not sought, nor had they been denied, the right to engage in any activities on their land, and there had been no indication or threat of enforcement. The court noted that the injunction improperly restrained enforcement of the provisions regulating use of land for quarries, sand and gravel pits, and peat moss bogs, which were in no way involved in the proceedings. Finally, the court noted that the statutory procedures for challenging zoning ordinances provided an adequate remedy at law and were not so cumbersome as to result in irreparable harm.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decree that enjoined the county from enforcing a zoning ordinance and remanded the matter to the court of common pleas with directions to dismiss the strip mine owners' complaint as premature.

Crawford v. Redevelopment Authority of County


No. 146, March Term, 1964


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


418 Pa. 549; 211 A.2d 866; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 626


October 9, 1964, Argued  
June 30, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Granted January 15, 1965. Reargued March 19, 1965. Reargument Refused August 6, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, No. 2360 in Equity, in case of Edith L. Crawford v. Redevelopment Authority of the County of Fayette and City of Uniontown.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant redevelopment authority (authority) sought review of a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which enjoined a taking of the property of plaintiff landowner in the landowner's action in equity against the authority to enjoin the authority from taking her property pursuant to a redevelopment plan.


OVERVIEW: The county approved the authority's plan to redevelop an area that was deemed blighted by the Urban Renewal Board (board). The landowner's property, which was not blighted, was included in the area, which the authority sought to take for its project. The landowner brought an action against the authority to enjoin the authority from taking her property. The chancellor concluded that the area of the landowner's property was not blighted and entered a decree which forbade the taking of her property. The authority appealed. The court reversed, holding that the courts could not substitute their discretion for that of the board on the question of blight unless the board's actions were arbitrary, made in bad faith, or not in conformance with the procedures ordained by statute. The court found that the landowner had not demonstrated circumstances, which would have permitted the courts to interfere with the board's discretion. The court held that it could not construe the board's actions as arbitrary merely because one small part of the entire blighted area was free from blight. Comprehensive planning required that areas be considered in their entirety and not in their unseverable parts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decree which enjoined a taking of the property of the landowner in the landowner's action in equity against the authority to enjoin the authority from taking her property pursuant to a redevelopment plan.

Beauty Hall, Inc. v. State Board of Cosmetology


No. 9, May Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


418 Pa. 225; 210 A.2d 495; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 588


March 22, 1965, Argued  
May 25, 1965, Decided

State Board of Cosmetology, Alan L. Emlen, Commissioner of Professional and Occupational Affairs, Laverta Harper et al.



DISPOSITION: Decree vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee beauty school filed an action against appellant state board of cosmetology to challenge the constitutionality of an amendment to include an educational requirement to a licensing statute. The Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) entered judgment in favor of the beauty school. The commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature amended a cosmetology licensing statute to include a 10th grade education as a requirement for licensure. The beauty school protested, asserting that the amendment deprived or interfered with its property rights without due process of law in violation of § 1 of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Article I, § 1, of the Pennsylvania Constitution. The beauty school contended that the educational requirement decreased the number of students enrolling in its classes. The trial court granted a decree enjoining enforcement of the statute. On appeal, the court vacated the decree, finding that the financial loss allegedly suffered by the beauty school did not constitute a deprivation of or interference with property by the state within the meaning of the constitutional provisions asserted by it and did not provide the requisite standing to attack the constitutionality of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decree in favor of the beauty school enjoining enforcement of the amendment was vacated.

DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this consolidated appeal, appellant patient challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee hospital's motions for judgment on the pleadings in an action by the patient alleging negligence on the part of two hospital employees which caused her to fall and break her right ankle.


OVERVIEW: The patient was hospitalized for an unrelated matter when she fell and broke her ankle in the hospital. She alleged that the broken ankle caused her to require further hospital and medical care, subjecting her husband to great medical expense and inflicting upon her pain and suffering as well as impairment of earning power. The lower court held in favor of the hospital, and the patient alleged on appeal that the lower court's grant of judgment on the pleadings was improper because the doctrine of charitable immunity should not have applied to the hospital. The patient contended that because the hospital received payments for its services, it therefore could not truly be called a charity hospital. The court agreed and held that the hospital's liability had to be governed by the same principles of law as applied to other employers.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower court were reversed.

Amalgamated Transit Union v. Port Authority of Allegheny County


No. 80, March Term, 1965


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


417 Pa. 299; 208 A.2d 271; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 415; 59 L.R.R.M. 2760; 51 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P51,277


January 13, 1965, Argued  
March 16, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Jan. T., 1965, No. 2708, in case of Division 85, Amalgamated Transit Union v. Port Authority of Allegheny County.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant port authority sought review of a decree from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which directed it to comply with the arbitration provisions of § 13.2 of the Second Class County Port Authority Act (Act), 55 P.S. § 563.2, in its labor dispute with appellee union.


OVERVIEW: The port authority and the union were parties to a collective bargaining agreement, which provided that a party that desired change had to notify the other party in writing before a certain date. They complied with this provision, but the meetings did not result in an agreement. The port authority refused to submit the dispute to arbitration, and the union sought mandamus. The part authority alleged that § 13.2 of the Act gave it sole discretion to decide whether to submit a dispute to arbitration. Upon review, the court found the word "shall" in § 13.2 was an imperative, and the port authority was required to submit the dispute to mandatory binding arbitration upon the failure of the negotiations. The court observed that § 13.2 was not contrary to Pa. Const. art. III, § 20 because the port authority had no power to levy taxes or pledge credit of the commonwealth or any political subdivision. The court found the arbitration provision of the Act did not constitute an illegal delegation of legislative power under Pa. Const. art. II, § 1 because the Act provided appropriate standards for the board of arbitrators to follow in making its determinations. The court affirmed the decree.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree that directed the port authority to comply with the arbitration provisions of the Act in its labor dispute with the union.

Commonwealth ex rel. Fox v. Maroney


No. 311, March Term, 1964


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


417 Pa. 308; 207 A.2d 810; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 416


October 5, 1964, Submitted  
March 16, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1964, No. 1515, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. George E. Fox v. James F. Maroney, Superintendent.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an application for a writ of habeas corpus, petitioner sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the petition for the writ.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. Petitioner did not make a motion for a new trial, did not make a motion in arrest of judgment, and did not file a direct appeal. Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus and argued that the Commonwealth failed to hold a preliminary hearing immediately after his arrest, that he was not represented by counsel at the preliminary hearing, that the trial court did not investigate his educational, military and social background, and that his confession was coerced. The trial dismissed the petition and the court affirmed. It found that the 13-hour delay between surrender and the preliminary hearing did not constitute a per se constitutional violation. Lack of counsel at the preliminary hearing did not constitute a deprivation of due process because defendant failed to show that the preliminary hearing was critical. Petitioner failed to show that he was prejudiced by a lack of investigation into his educational, military, and social background. As for petitioner's argument that his confession was coerced, petitioner did not attack the voluntariness at trial and, therefore, waived his argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Smith


No. 404, January Term, 1962


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


417 Pa. 321; 208 A.2d 219; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 418

March 16, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Refused April 14, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from order of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1962, No. 75, affirming judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Chester County, June T., 1960, No. 210-A, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. E. Newbold Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for assault and battery, which was affirmed by the Superior Court, (Pennsylvania), claiming that it was error to allow the commonwealth to deny him access to witness statements held by the Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over in his car by a police officer for a traffic violation. The police officer asked to see his driver's license and when defendant reached in his pocket to get it, the police chief struck him over the head with a blackjack. A fight then ensued and defendant was later charged with assault and battery. Defendant was denied access to witness statements taken in conjunction with the incident, which were held by the FBI, on the grounds that they pertained to a confidential investigation undertaken by the United States Department of Justice. Defendant was convicted at trial and sought review. The court held that defendant had the right to, and great need for, the statements he requested. The court opined that it would be unfair to allow a state prosecutor to block access to FBI statements by asserting that the defendant could get the information elsewhere. The court held that denying defendant the FBI reports constituted a denial of due process and ordered a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court ruled against the commonwealth, reversed defendant's conviction and ordered a new trial.

Deitch Co. v. Board of Property Assessment, etc.


No. 270, March Term, 1964


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


417 Pa. 213; 209 A.2d 397; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 404


October 7, 1964, Argued  
February 25, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Refused March 24, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1960 B, No. 2258, in case of The Deitch Company v. Board of Property Assessment, Appeals and Review of Allegheny County.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action where appellant company sought review of an assessment by appellee, the Board of Property Assessment, Appeals and Review of property owned by the company, the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) dismissed the company's claim. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company brought a trial court action to challenge the property value assessment made by the Board. The company challenged only the real property portion of the assessment, which the trial court found inappropriate. On appeal, the court also found a "partial" challenge improper, even where done pursuant to a stipulation by both parties. Nevertheless, the court vacated the trial court ruling and remanded the matter. The court found that the proper procedure for a property tax assessment dispute was not followed by the trial court. On remand, the trial court was to first decide on the basis of the evidence what the fair market value of the property involved was. Of course, if the assessment was in excess of that value, it must be reduced. Secondly, the trial court was to determine the appropriate ratio of assessed value to market value which existed in Allegheny County. The trial court would then apply the ratio thus found to the market value of the property in order to arrive at the proper assessment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's dismissal of the company's action against the Board and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Meyer v. Joint Council, I. B. T., C., W. & H.


Nos. 269, 272, January Term, 1964

January 5, 1965, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1963, No. 2479, in case of Charles Meyer et al. v. Joint Council 53, International Brotherhood of Teamsters, Chauffeurs, Warehousemen and Helpers of America et al.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, seven individuals and five unincorporated labor organizations, sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their jurisdictional objections in a libel action filed by plaintiffs, six individuals.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a complaint in trespass against defendants, seeking damages for libel. The alleged defamation appeared in a printed tabloid that was specifically issued during a campaign preceding a National Labor Relations Board representation election. Defendants filed preliminary objections challenging jurisdiction. The trial court dismissed the objections. The court further found that plaintiffs' action for defamation was subject to, and controllable by, the courts rather than the constitution or the laws of the union.

Meyers Estate


No. 367, January Term, 1964


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


416 Pa. 516; 206 A.2d 37; 1965 Pa. LEXIS 714


November 11, 1964, Argued  
January 5, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Orphans' Court of Luzerne County, No. 327 of 1963, in re estate of Elizabeth Hileman Meyers, or Elizabeth A. Meyers, deceased.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, executors and offeror, sought review of the order of Orphans' Court of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee co-executor's petition for a citation against the executors and offeror to show cause why a deed was not executed to the co-executor upon payment by the co-executor of a sum of money for certain real property of a decedent.


OVERVIEW: The executors and offeror had answered the co-executor's petition by averring that the price offered by the co-executor was inadequate in view of the receipt by the executors of other offers. The executors and offeror also contended that the exercise of the co-executor's option to purchase the property, as provided for in the testator's will, constituted improper self-dealing by a fiduciary and was a violation of the fiduciary duty as an executor to the other residuary legatees to obtain the highest price available for an asset of the estate. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court holding that in the absence of fraud, accident, or mistake, neither the executors nor the court was able to disregard or void the decedent's clearly expressed intent as delineated in the will. The court held that it was unable to rewrite a testator's will or distort the language in order to attain what was believed to be more beneficial and wise, or what the testator would have provided if he had possessed a knowledge of existing circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court which granted the co-executor's petition and permitted the co-executor to exercise an option to purchase certain real property from an estate, which was opposed by the executors and offeror.

In re Palmer Twp. Annexation Case


No. 15, January Term, 1964


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


416 Pa. 163; 204 A.2d 760; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 398


March 17, 1964, Argued  
November 24, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Northampton County, June T., 1961, No. 145A-145B, in re annexation ordinance No. 38 of Township of Palmer.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On two complaints, appellants, an acquiring township and its school district, municipal authority, and residents, challenged an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Northampton County (Pennsylvania) that approved Palmer, Pa., Ordinance No. 38, which provided for the annexation of appellee township. The proceedings were governed by the provisions of the Act of July 20, 1953, P. L. 550, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, §§ 67501- 67508 (Act).


OVERVIEW: The trial court referred the matter to a board of commissioners. Appellants questioned the constitutionality of the Act. They also asserted that the trial court erred in placing the burden of proof on appellants, in ruling that the motives of the proponents of annexation were irrelevant, and in making findings of fact unsupported by evidence. Third, they contended the trial court's reliance on the belief that a majority of persons in the area to be annexed favored the annexation was improper. On appeal, the court held that the power given to the trial court to inquire into the propriety of an annexation under the Act did not involve an unlawful allocation of legislative power to the judiciary. After a complaint was filed asking for the appointment of a fact-finding body, the trial court should have made determinations as to its legality and propriety. It was error to place the burden of proof upon appellants. The board went beyond usual procedures, for it stated in its report that it made inquiry by conferring with interested counsel and by considering certain unsolicited communications and verbal advice, which were improper methods of finding facts.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated and the case remanded for further proceedings based upon the proper factors.

 

267 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. N. Metal Co.


Nos. 31, 32, May Term, 1964


Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


416 Pa. 75; 204 A.2d 467; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 382


May 26, 1964, Argued  
November 10, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Nos. 367 and 368 Commonwealth Docket, 1962, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Board of Finance and Revenue, v. Northern Metal Company.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant metal company challenged the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the final resettlement of the company's state taxes that was approved by respondent Board of Finance and Revenue (board). The company argued that the state should have computed the tax by applying the allocation fractions set forth in the Corporate Net Income Tax Act, 72 P.S. §§ 3420a - 3420 (1935).


OVERVIEW: The metal company was a Pennsylvania corporation with its sole place of business in Philadelphia. In 1957 if filed its Pennsylvania corporate net income tax report showing net income in the amount of $ 52,901.02. The state settled the tax by determining net income to be $ 676,140.18 (the amount of taxable income reported to the federal government). The state then computed the tax without resort to the allocation fractions set forth in the Corporate Net Income Tax Act, it simply applied the six percent tax rate to all of the company's net income. The state then resettled the company's tax, which the board and lower court upheld. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment upholding the resettlement, finding that the company transacted all of its business in state; thus under the Act it was not entitled to apportion any part of its net income outside of the state. The court held that the state could impose a tax or excise on the privilege of doing business within the state and require such a tax to be measured by the net income of the corporation derived from all of its activities as long as that income was fairly apportioned to the taxing state by reference to in-state factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment affirming the board's approval of the state's final resettlement of the company's state taxes.

 

268 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Goodfellow v. Rundle


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


415 Pa. 528; 204 A.2d 446; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 477


Submitted October 2, 1964  
November 10, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 31, Jan. T., 1965, from order of Superior Court, October T., 1963, No. 340, affirming order of Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Miscellaneous No. 12114, 1963, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Thomas F. Goodfellow v. Alfred T. Rundle, Superintendent. Orders reversed and new trial ordered.

Same case in Superior Court: 203 Pa.Super.Ct. 419.

Habeas corpus.

Petition dismissed, opinion by GAWTHROP, P.J. Relator appealed to Superior Court which certified case to Supreme Court, opinion by WOODSIDE, J., concurring opinion by FLOOD, J., in which WATKINS and MONTGOMERY, JJ., joined, concurring and dissenting opinion by WRIGHT, J.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County is reversed and the record is remanded to that court with directions to issue the writ and to grant new trials.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, who, without counsel, was sentenced to imprisonment, appealed to the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which certified the case under the appropriate statute, the Act of June 24, 1895, P.L. 212, § 10, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 17, § 197. Along with the certification, the Superior Court appended an opinion that sought to lay down broad guidelines for the courts in reviewing habeas corpus petitions grounded on lack of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Although the objective of a guideline opinion for the assistance of trial courts might be generally commendable, that mission in this complex and developing area was not achieved. The court's recent decisions indicated that much of what was said in the guideline opinion filed in the Superior Court did not express the permissible constitutional doctrines to be applied to habeas corpus proceedings. The proper disposition of the matter before the court did not require as broad a discussion as that attempted below. In its view, the order of the court of common pleas should not be affirmed. Relator was denied his constitutional right to counsel unless he understandingly and intelligently waived that privilege. Such waiver was, of course, possible. Here, however, the transcript of the hearing at which the pleas were taken and the sentences imposed was absolutely devoid of any reference to counsel. Additionally, the record was utterly without suggestion or a single element of waiver. Because there was no allegation of waiver and because the record did not, in any way, sustain a finding of waiver, the court held that relator was unconstitutionally denied the assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court held that the order of the court of common pleas should not be affirmed. The disposition was without prejudice to relator's right to withdraw his petition in the court of common pleas should he have desired to do so.

Norvell Estate


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


415 Pa. 427; 203 A.2d 538; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 468


Argued March 23, 1964  
October 7, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 88, 89 and 90, March T., 1964, from decree of Orphans' Court of Allegheny County, No. 4403-A5 of 1940, in re estate of Florence Tack Norvell, deceased. Decree affirmed.

Audit of fifth account.

Decree nisi entered confirming account, all exceptions dismissed except one and final decree entered, adjudication by BOYLE, P.J. Exceptants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed. Each party to pay own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, life tenants and father, challenged a decision of the Orphans' Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which confirmed the accounting of appellee trustees. The accounting was filed along with the trustees' petition for distribution of the proceeds from stock sales as part of a testamentary trust.


OVERVIEW: The life tenants were entitled by the trust provisions to receive all of the income. The trial court approved the distribution to uniform principal of cash from the sale of rights and the shares of stock received as stock dividends. The allocation was made under the Uniform Principal and Income Act of July 3, 1947 (act), 1947 Pa. Laws 1283, which a recent decision held constitutionally applicable to trusts created prior to the effective date of the act. On appeal, the life tenants argued that the act, as applied to the trust created years prior to the effective date of the act, deprived the life tenants of their property without due process of law. The court affirmed the order confirming the trustees' accounting. In doing so, the court failed to find any constitutional deficiency in the act. The court specifically held that (1) the life tenants had no vested right in a definition of income, (2) the legislature had the power to define income, and (3) the legislature had not acted arbitrarily.


OUTCOME: The order confirming the accounting of the trustees was affirmed.

Butcher v. Bloom


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


415 Pa. 438; 203 A.2d 556; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 469


Argued April 7, 1964  
September 29, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction, Miscellaneous Docket No. 198, in case (originally commenced in Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 151, Commonwealth Docket, 1962) of Harry K. Butcher, Donald C. Rubel, Anne B. McKinley et al. v. George I. Bloom, Secretary of Commonwealth. Jurisdiction retained.

Equity.

Plaintiffs' motion for judgment on the pleadings denied; plaintiffs' petition to Supreme Court to take immediate jurisdiction of the case granted and special writ of certiorari issued; case remanded to common pleas court for hearing; report and findings of fact filed by BOWMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction retained in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers and electors, filed complaints in equity in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Pennsylvania, against defendant, the Secretary of the Commonwealth, alleging that voter redistricting laws violated the Fourteenth Amendment. After lawmakers redrafted the statutes, the taxpayers asked the court to take immediate jurisdiction and determine the constitutionality of 25 P.S. §§ 2221, 2217 (Supp. 1963).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers amended the complaint to include an attack on Pa. Const. art. II, §§ 16, 17 and proposed reapportionment bills pending in the legislature. The court held that seats in both houses of a bicameral state legislature had been apportioned on a population basis. Further, the court found that an individual's right to vote for state legislators was unconstitutionally impaired when that right was substantially diluted when compared with votes of citizens living in other parts of the state. The court held that Pa. Const. art. II, § 16 required that senatorial reapportionment legislation had to maintain the integrity of counties and other political subdivisions whenever possible. The court held, however, that lawmakers had to provide for compact districts of contiguous territory subject to the overriding mandate that all districts shall be "as nearly equal in population" as possible. The court held that Pa. Const. art. II, § 17 required lawmakers to do the same for state representatives' districts. The court held that the Pennsylvania constitutional provisions were in accord with the Fourteenth Amendment and that the statutes, as drafted, were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that both statutes were unconstitutional and found that the legislature was required to enact reapportionment laws that conformed to constitutional requirements. The court retained jurisdiction of the matter pending legislative action.

Pittsburgh R. Co. v. Port of Allegheny County Authority


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


415 Pa. 177; 202 A.2d 816; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 440


Argued March 24, 1964  
July 30, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 164 and 165, March T., 1964, from orders of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1964, Nos. 2580 and 2581, in cases of Pittsburgh Railways Company v. Port of Allegheny County Authority; and petition of Port of Allegheny Authority for appointment of viewers to determine and assess damages re condemnation of Pittsburgh Railways Company's transportation system. Order of court below, appeal No. 164, affirmed and complaint dismissed; orders of court below, appeal No. 165, as modified, affirmed. Petition to recall record and reverse order of court below in No. 165 denied January 15, 1965.

Equity action and condemnation proceedings.

Order entered in equity action refusing to grant preliminary injunction and orders entered in condemnation proceedings appointing viewers and permitting defendant to make payment of certain monies into court, opinions by WEIR, J. Plaintiff in both actions appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below at No. 2581 April Term 1964, appeal No. 164 March Term, 1964, refusing a preliminary injunction is affirmed and the complaint dismissed. Costs to be borne by appellant.

The orders of the court below at No. 2580 April Term,  [***2] 1964, appeal No. 165 March Term, 1964, as modified, are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railway company sought review of two orders from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which refused to grant it a preliminary injunction to enjoin appellee port authority from filing its petition to condemn railway property, appointed viewers to assess the condemnation damages, and granted the port authority permission to pay into court a percentage of damages resulting from its exercise of eminent domain.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the railway company argued that the eminent domain power granted to the port authority by the Second Class Port Authority Act of 1956 (Act), 55 P.S. § 551 et seq., violated the state and federal constitutions; the statutory delegation of sole authority to the condemnor to estimate damages and the determination by the condemnor of what constituted a transportation system as stated in the Act was unconstitutional; and corporate records not related to the operation or maintenance of its system were wrongfully condemned by the port authority. Upon review, the court modified and affirmed the judgment relating to the assessment of damages and payment, and affirmed the judgment denying the railway company's petition for preliminary injunction. Because the trial court did not entertain an application for surety by the port authority in its condemnation of the railway company's property and did not pass on the adequacy of the bond, the court ordered the port authority to give its bond to the railway company, and made it unlimited in amount and secured it by all of the assets of the port authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the railway company's petition for preliminary injunction and dismissed that cause of action, modified and affirmed the judgment relating to the assessment of damages and payment into court, and held that the port authority was to give a bond to the railway company that was unlimited in amount and secured by all port authority assets.

Democratic Cty. Comm. Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


415 Pa. 327; 203 A.2d 212; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 462


Argued July 1, 1964  
July 27, 1964; August 5, 1964


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 329, Jan. T., 1964, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1964, No. 5446, in re petition of Democratic County Committee of Philadelphia on behalf of all its endorsed candidated for nomination at the April 28, 1964 primary election in Wards 23, 25, 33, 35, 36, 41, 45, 53, 54, 55, 56, 57, and 58. Order affirmed. * 


* Reporter's Note: On October 12, 1964, the Supreme Court of the United States denied a petition for a writ of certiorari.

Appeal from decision of County Board of Elections of Philadelphia County which held that votes cast in blank spaces in Row C, marked on the left "Republican", of voting machines in 15 wards in Philadelphia were invalid and void and could not be counted as having been cast in favor of the candidate for the democratic Party nomination for the United State Senate whose name appeared in Row B, marked on the left "Democratic", above or near these blank spaces in Row C.

Order entered affirming Board, by CARROLL, P.J. Democratic County Committee of Philadelphia appealed.

The Jamestown Machine which was involved in 13 wards was set up as shown in the following picture of the voting machine.

 [***2] A diagram of a portion of the face of the voting machine, which is referred to in the opinion of Mr. Justice ROBERTS, is shown in the second picture. This diagram is based on the sample ballots supplied at argument by counsel and on the submitted photographs of the same voting machines.

(Illustration omitted)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.

The record in this case and our applicable law, statutory and decisional, compel me to recognize the intent of the voters. I cannot in good conscience on the facts of this case be a party to the disfranchisement and denial of the constitutional right of these thousands of voters. In my opinion, these voters should be validated; right and justice command that result. I would reverse the order of the court below.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant political committee sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of appellee County Board of Elections of Philadelphia County which held that votes in a so-called blank row were invalid and void.


OVERVIEW: The political committee wanted votes cast in blank spaces, marked on the left of the word "Republican," of voting machines in 15 wards in the county to be counted as having been cast in favor of the political committee's candidate, whose name appeared above or near the blank spaces. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that no one knew or could determine, except by guessing, whether the votes, or indeed any votes in the blank spaces, represented protest votes, non-partisan votes, Republican votes, Democratic votes, votes for the political committee's candidate, or "mistake" votes; but the court found that the votes were illegally cast and were clearly and undoubtedly void votes. The court also found that the only exceptions to cases where votes were inappropriately cast were where there were minor irregularities, especially if committed by election officials, and in cases where a voter voted correctly in the right row and in the right square and in the right space, but then added something which was surplusage. The court found that neither of these exceptions was applicable in this case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in favor of the County Board of Elections of Philadelphia County in the case by the political committee that sought to have votes cast in blank spaces to be counted as having been cast in favor of the political committee's candidate, whose name appeared above or near the blank spaces.

Commonwealth v. Giaccio


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


415 Pa. 139; 202 A.2d 55; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 433


Argued April 22, 1964  
July 6, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 218, Jan. T., 1964, from order of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1963, No. 123, reversing order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Chester County, Sept. T., 1961, No. 225, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Jay Giaccio. Order affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 202 Pa.Super.Ct. 294.

Indictment charging defendant with unlawfully and wantonly pointing and discharging a firearm. Before GAWTHROP, P.J.

Verdict of not guilty; order entered directing defendant to pay costs of prosecution which order was later vacated. Commonwealth appealed to Superior Court which reversed vacating order, opinion by WOODSIDE, J., dissenting opinion by FLOOD, J. Appeal to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Superior Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with pointing a deadly weapon at another person. The jury acquitted him but imposed the costs of prosecution upon him. Defendant moved to be relieved of payment of the costs. The trial court granted the motion and held that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1222 (1860) was unconstitutional and set aside the imposition of costs. The Superior Court of Pennsylvania reversed and reinstated the imposition of costs. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asked the court to declare invalid Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1222 (1860), which permitted the imposition by a jury of costs on defendants acquitted of misdemeanors. The statute was attacked as vague and lacking in sufficient standards. Defendant argued that the Act was an improper delegation of legislative power in contravention of Pa. Const. art. II, § 1. Defendant also contended that the Act violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV because it did not treat those acquitted of felonies or of summary offenses in a similar manner. The court upheld the statute and the imposition of costs. The court found that just as costs in civil cases could be imposed whenever permitted by statute, not as a penalty but rather as compensation to a litigant for expenses, so, too, the costs under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1222 (1860) represented compensation or partial reimbursement to the county for expenses incurred in a prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania

Argued January 7, 1964

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 2, Jan. T., 1964, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, July T., 1962, No. 175, in the matter of appeal of William E. Cleaver, Maira Cleaver, his wife, Joseph H. Engelman et al. v. Board of Adjustment of Tredyffrin Township and Conestoga Enterprises, Inc. Order reversed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Adjustment sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which reversed the decision of the Board that affirmed ex necessitate the issuance to appellee landowners of a building permit for the erection of a garden type of apartment.


OVERVIEW: The Board affirmed ex necessitate the issuance of a building permit for the erection of a garden type of apartment to the landowners. The trial court reversed and held the amendatory ordinance invalid and unconstitutional because it was spot zoning. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that it was error to conclude that the amended ordinance violated the comprehensive plan that the township board of supervisors approved and relied on because the land use plan permitted a defined range of choices in the zoning of the landowner's property and did not command particular requirements of population density or set-back spacing for apartments thereon and thus clearly envisioned and permitted a proper zoning of the property in question for apartments. They topography, location, and characteristics of the property undoubtedly justified the reclassification and rezoning. It was not spot zoning because, among other things, a large part of the surrounding land had the same or virtually the same classification as the tract in question and the uses permitted by the down zoning were substantially similar to those permitted on numerous adjoining properties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which reversed the decision of the Board that affirmed ex necessitate the issuance to the landowners of a building permit for the erection of a garden type of apartment.

Brennan v. Shipe


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


414 Pa. 258; 199 A.2d 467; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 552


Argued October 10, 1963  
April 21, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 2, May T., 1964, from order of Court of Common Pleas of York County, Oct. T., 1962, No. 172, in case of Thomas J. Brennan V. Madge E. Shipe and Burdwell H. Shipe. Order affirmed.

Trespass for personal injuries.

Order entered dismissing defendants' preliminary objections to the complaint, opinion by BUCKINGHAM, J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee pedestrian filed an action in trespass for personal injuries against appellants, a driver and her husband. Appellants filed preliminary objections challenging the substituted service of process under the Pennsylvania Nonresident Motorist Act of May 14, 1929, P.L. 1721, § 1 et seq., as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 75, § 2001 et seq. The Court of Common Pleas, York County (Pennsylvania) dismissed the objections. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The pedestrian alleged that he was injured when struck by a motor vehicle driven by the driver, who at the time of the accident was acting as the agent of her husband. The accident occurred on land that was ceded to the federal government in 1937 by the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. The pedestrian filed suit. The driver and her husband, who lived in Florida, were served under the substituted service provisions of the Nonresident Motorist Act. They filed objections, contending that such service violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 because the federal government had jurisdiction over federal lands. The trial court dismissed the objections and the court affirmed. The Pennsylvania Nonresident Motorist Act was clearly a law of Pennsylvania which by its own terms governed the rights of the parties in an action brought to recover on account of injuries sustained in a federal enclave located within the exterior boundaries of Pennsylvania. The words "within the Commonwealth" in the Act were intended to encompass all territory within the geographical borders of Pennsylvania, including any federal enclave located therein.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Olin Mathieson Chemical Corp. v. White Cross Stores, Inc.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


414 Pa. 95; 199 A.2d 266; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 526


Argued January 16, 1964  
March 26, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 24, March T., 1964, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1963, No. 3464, in case of Olin Mathieson Chemical Corporation v. White Cross Stores, Inc. Nos. 6, 7, 8, 9, 14, 18 and 19. Decree reversed; reargument refused April 24, 1964.

Equity. Before WEISS, J.

Adjudication filed entering preliminary injunction in favor of plaintiff and against defendants upon filing of bond, defendants' exceptions dismissed and final decree entered making injunction permanent. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed. Each party to pay own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) enjoining appellant from selling appellee manufacturer's products below minimum prices, pursuant to the Pennsylvania Fair Trade Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 7 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Pennsylvania Fair Trade Act, appellee manufacturer of pharmaceuticals sought injunctive relief against appellant retailer. Appellee claimed that appellant was not abiding by the price fixing regulations and selling drugs below minimum set prices. Appellee was not a signatory to the agreement. The lower court granted injunctive relief and appellant sought review. On appeal the court reversed. The court held that the Pennsylvania Fair Trade Act, as applied to nonsigners of price maintenance contracts, was unconstitutional. Where price regulation was delegated to a governmental agency, constitutional procedures were mandatory. In the Pennsylvania Fair Trade Act, these procedures were completely absent. Fair hearing and judicial review were not available, even though the fixed price was grossly unfair or completely arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court, finding the legislation unconstitutional because the protective processes of fair hearing and judicial review were absent.

Milk Control Com. v. Battista


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


413 Pa. 652; 198 A.2d 840; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 738


Argued January 7, 1964  
March 24, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 13, Jan. T., 1964, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, No. 62-10954, in equity, in case of Milk Control Commission of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Joseph Battista, Frank DiGiambattista and Albert B. DiGiambattista, trading as Nor-view Farm. Decree reversed.

Equity.

Defendants' preliminary objections sustained and decree entered for defendants and against plaintiff, opinion by FORREST, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed. Each party to bear own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Milk Control Commission (Pennsylvania), sought review of a decision by the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which sustained preliminary objections of appellees, a farm through its owners. The trial court found for appellees. The Commission sought to enjoin, in equity, appellees from selling milk that was removed from the farm before sale to consumers at less than the minimum prices set by the Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellees asserted in their preliminary objections that they were exempt from the licensing and pricing provisions of the Milk Control Law, April 28, 1937, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, §§ 700j-101 to 700j-1302 (Supp. 1963). The court found, however, that all that the Pennsylvania Legislature intended to exempt in § 402 of the Milk Control Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 700j-402 (Supp. 1963), was the family-farm type of producer-dealer operation. The court determined that it would have been in contradiction of the legislative purpose and objective to permit an exempt farm operation to receive its product from a commercial handler or to have its milk processed by such a dealer. The court also found that it could not say that the limitation on the exemption violated the Constitution of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania or the Constitution of the United States of America. The court also determined that it could not hold that the classification bore no reasonable relation to the price structure that the Commission was statutorily empowered to fix and maintain. Therefore, the statute had to stand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decree.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Township of Upper Darby, Pennsylvania challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which reversed the decision of the township's board of adjustment, dismissed the township's exceptions, and ordered that a certificate of occupancy be granted to appellee duplex owners to use their duplex as a real estate office.
