Saulsbury v. Bethlehem Steel Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


413 Pa. 316; 196 A.2d 664; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 674


Argued October 1, 1963  
January 8, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 88 and 89, March T., 1963, from judgments and orders of Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County, June T., 1962, Nos. 2 and 3, in cases of William Saulsbury, William Evans, Frank Slivosky et al. v. Bethlehem Steel Company and City of Johnstown; and George Youngeridge, Edward Feeney, Mike Call et al. v. Bethlehem Steel Company and Borough of Franklin. Judgments and orders affirmed.

Equity actions.

Orders entered granting plaintiffs' motions for judgment on the pleadings and judgments entered, opinion by GRIFFITH, P.J., MCDONALD and SHETTIG, JJ. Defendants, City of Johnstown and Borough of Franklin, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgments and orders affirmed. Costs on appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities filed separate appeals from judgments and orders of Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment on the pleadings for appellee employees who worked within the cities, determined that the ordinances imposing an occupation privilege tax were void, and restrained collection of the tax imposed. The appeals were considered together as the same legal questions were involved.


OVERVIEW: The employees brought separate actions to challenge the validity of ordinances passed in the cities in which they were employed that imposed an occupation privilege tax on those whose gross earnings were $ 600 or more. The trial court determined that the ordinances were void and the court affirmed. It found that the cities had the legal power to levy a true occupational privilege tax, if the power was properly exercised; however the particular ordinances involved presented certain difficulties. Pa. Const. art. IX, §§ 1-2 required that all taxes were to be uniform, upon the same class of subjects, within the territorial limits of the authority levying the tax. Further, while different subjects could be reasonably classified for tax purposes, there must be no lack of uniformity within the class, either on the given subject of the tax or the persons affected as payers. Finally, if a tax was levied on an occupational privilege, it must apply to all who share the privilege. The ordinances in question, however, lacked uniformity as they levied a tax which exempted certain individuals because their incomes did not exceed stated amounts and were therefore void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted judgment in favor of the employees and held that the ordinances passed by the cities imposing an occupation tax on those earning $ 600 or more were invalid.

 

282 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Cheltenham Twp. Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


413 Pa. 379; 196 A.2d 363; 1964 Pa. LEXIS 683


Argued October 10, 1963  
January 7, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 56 and 68, Jan. T., 1964, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, dated June 19, 1963, in re appeal of Gladys Diamond, individually and as chairman of a special committee of Curtis Hills Civic Association. Order reversed; reargument refused February 21, 1964.

Appeal from decision of board of adjustment granting building permit.

Order entered reversing decision of board, order by FORREST, P.J. Property owners and township appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed; the action of the board of adjustment in affirming the issuance of the building permit is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, township and developer, sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which reversed the decision of the township zoning board of adjustment and found two township zoning ordinances invalid in appellee civic association's challenge.


OVERVIEW: The developer presented a detailed plan to develop a tract of land in the township and asked that it be rezoned. A rezoning ordinance was passed after public hearings. A second rezoning request was denied after the association objected. A building permit was issued for an apartment building without objection. When a permit for a store was issued, the association filed an appeal to the board, which upheld the permit. The association brought an action in the trial court, which held the rezoning ordinances invalid. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the association had participated in the planning process for four years and had expressed its satisfaction with the plan, except on one occasion when their objection succeeded. The court ruled that the association was aware that the project was an interdependent complex premised on implementation of the complete plan and its conduct led the developer to believe that the development would proceed as planned. The court concluded that, although a building permit could be challenged within 30 days of its issuance, the association was challenging the entire plan and, thus, it should have appealed the issuance of the first permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and found that the township's zoning ordinances were valid.

 

283 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Philadelphia v. Smith


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


412 Pa. 262; 194 A.2d 177; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 404


Argued May 28, 1963  
October 9, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 3 and 8, May T., 1963, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 555 Commonwealth Docket, 1959, No. 2390, Equity Docket, in case of City of Philadelphia and The United Gas Improvement Company v. Theodore B. Smith, Jr., successor to Charles M. Dougherty, Secretary of Revenue. Decree vacated.

Equity.

Adjudication entered dismissing complaint, plaintiff's exceptions to adjudication overruled and final decree entered, opinion by NEELY, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is vacated and the case remanded to the court below for further proceedings consistent herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a city and the operator of its gas works, sought an injunction restraining defendant, the state secretary of revenue, from collecting the gross receipts tax imposed under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 2181. The Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) entered a decree dismissing plaintiffs' complaint, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under § 23 of the Act of June 1, 1889, P.L. 420 (Pennsylvania), a gross receipts tax was imposed on specified companies, including electric light and power companies. As amended by the Act of May 13, 1925, P.L. 702, the gross receipts of a municipally owned and operated public utility were exempted from the tax. The Act of May 16, 1935, P.L. 200, imposed the tax on the gross receipts of municipal utilities from business done outside the municipality's boundaries, and the Act of November 21, 1959, P.L. 1553, added gas utilities to the list of taxable companies and provided that the tax applied to municipalities, except that receipts other than gas receipts were exempt. The city claimed that the 1959 act was unconstitutional because it arbitrarily subjected municipal gas utilities, but not municipal electric utilities, to the gross receipts tax. In remanding the case for further proceedings, the court found that the parties' stipulation regarding the factors distinguishing gas from electric companies was so lacking in factual data that it was inadequate for the purpose of deciding the constitutional question.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decree and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

284 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Daly v. Hemphill


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


411 Pa. 263; 191 A.2d 835; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 506


Argued April 18, 1963  
June 4, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 208, 209 and 212, Jan. T., 1963, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1962, No. 4994, in equity, and judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1962, No. 4993, in mandamus, in cases of John F. Daly, Chief Magistrate of Philadelphia, v. Alexander Hemphill, Controller, Francis A. Lalley, Finance Director, and Philip Poorman, Treasurer, of City of Philadelphia, and John Reese and Charles Dougherty v. Same. Decree and judgment affirmed; reargument refused July 1, 1963.

Equity action and mandamus consolidated.

Decree entered in equity action enjoining defendants from certain activities, decree by ALESSANDRONI, P.J., and WEINROTT, J.; judgment entered for plaintiffs on the pleadings in mandamus action. Defendants in both actions appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decrees affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city officials sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which enjoined the city officials from certain activities and entered a judgment for appellee chief magistrate in a mandamus action.


OVERVIEW: The court below dismissed the preliminary objections, enjoined the city officials from interfering with the actions of the chief magistrate, and ordered them to pay the salaries of two individuals. On appeal, the court held that there was no violation of the separation of powers or encroachment upon judicial independence in the appointment of a chief magistrate by the governor. The grant of this authority to the governor was well within the law-making sphere of the legislature. The court held that an act of assembly was not to be declared unconstitutional unless it clearly, palpably and plainly violated the constitution. The power of appointment and removal of employees, save those specifically appointable by the individual magistrates, was statutorily vested in the chief magistrate.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court entering a judgment for the chief magistrate in a case brought against the city officials was affirmed.

 

285 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Pew Trust


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


411 Pa. 96; 191 A.2d 399; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 482


Argued January 9, 1963  
May 29, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 23, Jan. T., 1963, from decree of Orphans' Court of Montgomery County, No. 50940, in re trust estate of Mary C. Pew, settlor. Decree reversed.

Audit of account. Before TAXIS, JR., P.J.

Adjudication filed confirming account as modified, exceptions to adjudication dismissed and decree entered. Arthur E. Pew, Jr. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed, case remanded to the Orphans' Court with directions to enter a decree in conformity with this Opinion; costs to be paid out of the principal of the trust.

I would affirm the decree.

DISSENTING OPINION BY MR. JUSTICE COHEN:

I agree with Justice JONES and Judge TAXIS of the court below that the settlor did not "direct" the apportionment between principal and income so as to bring this trust within the proviso clause of section 2 of the Principal and Income Act.

I likewise agree that our decision in Catherwood with respect to the retroactive application of the Act to ordinary stock dividends is entitled to as much weight as our decision with regard to extraordinary stock dividends - a determination which the majority apparently accepts. Moreover, no reason is advanced by the majority why our decision in Catherwood [***2] that ordinary stock dividends are subject to the Principal and Income Act should now be overruled.

I would go further, however, and hold that the retroactive application of the Act to ordinary stock dividends does not violate due process or constitute an impairment of the obligation of contracts, as contended by appellant. As we held in Catherwood, "[there] is no vested property right in a court-made rule of apportionment." [405 Pa. at 77]. Instead of undermining the Act of 1947 and our decision in Catherwood, as the majority does, I would give appellant the opportunity to question the constitutionality of Catherwood before the United States Supreme Court - the obvious purpose of this litigation.

Accordingly, I dissent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant life tenant sought review of the order of the Orphans' Court of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which awarded a six percent stock dividend to the trust's principal. The life tenant contended that the dividend was trust income under res adjudicata, the law of the case, due process of law, and because an award to principal would impair the obligation of the deed of trust in violation of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: When the settlor created the subject trust, the law provided that extraordinary stock dividends up to and including six percent were trust income. The Principal and Income Act of 1945 provided that stock dividends were apportionable. Applying the new law to the six percent stock dividend, the Orphans' Court determined that the six percent stock dividend was deemed principal. The court held that as to wills of persons dying before and inter vivos trusts created prior to the effective date of the Principal and Income Act of 1945, a gift of income or net income included small stock dividends of six percent or less unless the testator or settlor clearly expressed a contrary intent. In light of the facts and circumstances which surrounded the settlor at the time she created the trust and considering the law that existed when she created the trust, the court concluded that she gave and intended to give the life tenant of this trust the small stock dividends of six percent or less, as well as the cash dividends which were paid annually.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Orphans' Court and remanded with directions to enter a decree in conformity with the court's opinion that the six percent stock dividend was trust income payable to the life tenant.

Anstine v. Zoning Board of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


411 Pa. 33; 190 A.2d 712; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 474


Argued November 20, 1962  
April 30, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 4, May T., 1963, from order of Court of Common Pleas of York County, Jan. T., 1962, No. 226, in case of Dale D. Anstine and Vivian D. Anstine v. Zoning Board of Adjustment of York Township. Order reversed.

Appeal from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing to grant variance.

Order entered affirming decision of board, opinion by SHADLE, J. Property owners appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a decision of appellee zoning board of adjustment refusing to grant a variance from the terms of the York Township Zoning Ordinance of 1960.


OVERVIEW: The property owners purchased approximately two acres of land in the township. At the time of purchase, the land was improved with a two-story block building, formerly used as a chicken house and hog pen. The property owners placed on their land a mobile-home or trailer and used it as a dwelling house. On appeal, the court sought to determine whether the zoning ordinance operated in such an arbitrary, capricious, discriminatory or confiscatory manner so as to unconstitutionally deprive the property owners of the use of their property. The burden was on the property owners to show that the maintenance of their mobile home, improved as proposed, would not have been inimical to the health, safety, morals and general welfare of the inhabitants of the township. The court found that the refusal to grant the property owners permission to improve their mobile home was arbitrary and discriminatory. The court concluded that § 704.1 of the Township Zoning Ordinance of 1960 placed an unreasonable, arbitrary and discriminatory restriction on the property owners' use of their property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

 

287 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Philadelphia Life Ins. Co. v. Commonwealth


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


410 Pa. 571; 190 A.2d 111; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 655


Argued November 14, 1962  
April 16, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 19 and 20, May T., 1963, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket, 1961, Nos. 331 and 357, Equity Docket Nos. 2487 and 2492, in cases of Philadelphia Life Insurance Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Charles M. Dougherty, Secretary of Revenue, Thomas Z. Minehart, Auditor General, David Stahl, Attorney General, et al., and Plymouth Mutual Life Insurance Company v. Same. Order affirmed.

Equity.

Order entered overruling defendants' preliminary objections to the complaint, opinion by SWOPE, P.J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Commonwealth and its officers, appealed an order of the Dauphin County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which overruled preliminary objections to the complaint brought by plaintiff taxpayer challenging the constitutionality of 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. § 2270.1 (1961). The trial court found that it had equitable jurisdiction over the suit.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer wished to challenge § 2270.1, which imposed a state tax of two percent on gross premiums obtained by insurance companies. The officials claimed sovereign immunity from suit but the court on appeal disagreed, finding that the suit was not brought to obtain financial relief against the Commonwealth itself, but was brought to prevent the officials from taking unlawful action. Consequently, the court ruled that the name of the Commonwealth must be dropped from the suit. The court next found that equitable jurisdiction always extended to suits brought challenging the very power of the legislature to enact a statute, including a tax statute. Finally, the court held that the taxpayer had no adequate remedy at law because the most that the Fiscal Code provided was review of the tax calculations, which was not sought by the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that overruled the officials' preliminary objections to the taxpayer's complaint, and it allowed the suit to proceed.

Milk Control Com. v. Penn Fruit Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


410 Pa. 242; 188 A.2d 705; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 597


Argued September 25, 1962  
March 19, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 13, May T., 1963, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 2501 Equity Docket 1961, No. 449 Commonwealth Docket 1961, in case of Milk Control Commission of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Penn Fruit Company, Inc., Samuel Cooke, Morris Kaplan et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity. Before NEELY, P.J.

Decree nisi entered dismissing complaint, plaintiff's exception dismissed and final decree entered. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed. Costs on appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commission brought an action against appellee corporation and appellee officers, seeking to enjoin the corporation and the officers from handling milk in the capacity of a milk dealer as defined by the Milk Control Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 700j-101 et seq. The Court of Common Pleas, Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) entered a decree dismissing the complaint. The commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation and the officers operated grocery stores in a multi-state area. In its action, the commission contended that the milk purchased by the corporation from a dairy company at its out-of-state plant was not milk from a licensed dealer. In dismissing the commission's complaint, the trial court found that the Milk Control Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 700j-101 et seq., as construed by the commission, discriminated against interstate commerce, contrary to the provisions of the Commerce Clause. The trial court also found that the corporation was exempt from licensing. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the commission's complaint because the trial court properly held that the corporation in the purchase of milk from a licensed in-state dealer for resale in its stores within the state, was exempt from licensing by virtue of the Milk Control Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 700j-402, and that exemption was not removed by virtue of the fact that the milk was delivered in another state, and transported by the corporation in its trucks for a sale in its stores within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree that dismissed the action brought by the commission against the corporation and the officers.

Tate v. Philadelphia Transp. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


410 Pa. 490; 190 A.2d 316; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 641; 53 L.R.R.M. 2031; 47 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,802


Argued January 30, 1963  
January 31, 1963; April 16, 1963


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 162 and 168, Jan. T., 1963, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 (docketed C.P. No. 4) of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1962, No. 2500, in case of James H. J. Tate, Thomas McIntosh, George X. Schwartz and City of Philadelphia v. Philadelphia Transportation Company. Decree reversed.

Equity. Before MILNER, P.J., and WATERS, J.

Decree entered appointing temporary receiver for Philadelphia Transportation Company. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed; costs to be paid by the City of philadelphia.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant transportation company sought review of the decision of the trial court (Pennsylvania), which granted plaintiff city's request for the appointment of a temporary receiver who was charged with ending the cessation of operation of the transpiration company's transit facilities.


OVERVIEW: The contract between the transportation company and the union representing its employees had expired, and their attempts to negotiate the terms of a new contract had been unsuccessful. The union declared a strike that resulted in a complete cessation of all public transportation in the city causing great hardship to the public. The court determined that the record did not support the appointment of a temporary receiver for the transportation company's solvent business. The court concluded that the trial court appointed the receiver to end the strike. However, in the absence of any justification in the law or in applicable principles of equity for the appointment of a receiver, temporary or otherwise, the trial court abused its discretion. The appointment of a receiver could not be used as a weapon of coercion to force the transportation company to settle a strike, and the court determined that a receiver could not be appointed where receivership was the sole relief asked.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court finding that there was no justification for the appointment of a receiver.

Andress v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


410 Pa. 77; 188 A.2d 709; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 568


Argued November 16, 1962  
January 21, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 340, Jan. T., 1962, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1961, No. 865, in case of George W. Andress, Georginna Andress, his wife, George R. Schultze et al. v. Zoning Board of Adjustment of City of Philadelphia. Order reversed; reargument refused March 28, 1963.

Appeal from decision of zoning board of adjustment granting a variance.

Order entered dismissing appeal, opinion by GOLD, P.J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee construction company obtained a variance to a local ordinance for the erection of an apartment house in an area of single-family residences. The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) affirmed the variance without taking any testimony. Appellants neighboring property owners sought review.


OVERVIEW: The neighboring property owners protested the variance on the grounds that a single-family dwelling could be built and that an apartment would greatly change the character of the neighborhood by increasing congestion, population density, and school taxes, and would be contrary to the public safety and general welfare. The court held that the party seeking a variance was required to show unnecessary hardship and that a variance was not contrary to the public safety, health, morals, or general welfare. The court also held that a variance would not be granted solely on the grounds of economic hardship, particularly where the property was purchased with knowledge of the economic hardship. The court also held that a zoning law and a variance could constitute an unconstitutional taking if it diminished the value of property. Because the evidence was slight, the court reversed without prejudice for the construction company to reapply for a variance and to establish that the erection of buildings that did not require a variance was so impractical as to completely prohibit or substantially destroy the lawful use of the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed without prejudice the lower court's ordered that affirmed the grant of a variance to the construction company. The court also found that the construction company was permitted to reapply for a variance.

Commonwealth v. Smith


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


409 Pa. 521; 187 A.2d 267; 1963 Pa. LEXIS 702


Argued November 26, 1962  
January 8, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 339, Jan. T., 1962, from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Bucks County, Jan. T., 1957, No. 20, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Colon Shaw Smith. Judgment affirmed.

Proceedings on appeal from conviction before justice of the peace. Before FULLAM, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal and directing defendant to pay costs of proceedings and a fine in the amount of $4,350 for operating a tractor-trailer that exceeded the maximum weight permitted under The Vehicle Code. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for operating a tractor-trailer that exceeded the maximum weight permitted under § 903 of the Vehicle Code, codified at Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 75, § 903, entered by the Court of Quarter Sessions of Bucks County (Pennsylvania).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of operating, without a special permit, a tractor-trailer owned by a corporation which was 43,850 pounds over the maximum weight under § 903. Defendant pleaded guilty before a justice of the peace. A fine of $ 4,350 plus costs was imposed under the rising scale of penalties that was set forth in § 903. Defendant posted bond and perfected an appeal to the lower court, which held a trial de novo. At the trial, the corporate owner of the tractor-trailer filed a petition to intervene and for a declaratory judgment that § 903 was unconstitutional. Although the lower court took no action on the petition, the contentions raised as to the constitutionality of § 903 were discussed and dismissed. Defendant was found guilty. On appeal, the court held that defendant had no standing to resist the enforcement of the impounding provision under § 903, noting that the tractor trailer belonged to another. The court also held that the validity of defendant's fine was not dependent upon the constitutionality of the impounding provision, as the provision for the fine was able to be severed from the impounding provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Universal Film Exchanges, Inc. v. Board of Finance & Revenue


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


409 Pa. 180; 185 A.2d 542; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 424


Argued May 22, 1962  
November 13, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 18, 19, 20, 21, 22, 23, 24 and 25, May T., 1962, from orders of Board of Finance and Revenue, Nos. M-16585, M-16586, M-16587, M-16589, M-16590, M-16591, M-16592 and M-16593, in case of Universal Film Exchanges, Inc. v. Board of Finance and Revenue, Allied Artists Distributing Corp. v. Same, RKO General, Inc. v. Same, Paramount Film Distributing Corp. v. Same, Twentieth Century-Fox Film Corp. v. Same, United Artists Corporation v. Same, Columbia Pictures Corp. v. Same, and Loew's Incorporated v. Same. Orders affirmed. * 


* Reporter's Note: On April 1, 1963, the Supreme Court of the United States denied a petition for a writ of certiorari.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant movie distributors sought review of a decision by appellee Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue (Board), which refused the movie distributors' claim for a refund of license fees paid under the Motion Picture Censorship Act for each film.


OVERVIEW: The movie distributors continuously paid to the Pennsylvania State Board of Censors annual license fees for each film, under the Motion Picture Censorship Act, until the Act was declared unconstitutional. The distributors filed petitions for refunds of the license fees which were paid by them, claiming that the license fees were paid under duress and compulsion. The Board denied their petition, and the distributors appealed. The court held that the license-fee payments were not made under legal duress and that there was no violation of due process because the distributors could have paid the fees under protest and with notice of an intent to reclaim and recover the amounts paid. The court noted that the distributors could have brought a timely suit in assumpsit, or a bill in equity to restrain the collection of the tax. The court held that the that the five year statutory period for the recovery under 72 P.S.§ 503(a)(4) was reasonable for the recovery of monies voluntarily, but mistakenly paid to the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania under the Motion Picture Censorship Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the Board and denied the movie distributors' claim for a refund of the license fees paid.

Smith v. Gallagher


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 551; 185 A.2d 135; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 533


Argued September 12, 1962  
October 26, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 424, Jan. T., 1962, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, docketed Court of Common Pleas No. 2, June T., 1962, No. 4588, in case of Beatrice M. Smith v. James A. Gallagher et al. Decree affirmed.

Separate equity action commenced against city officials to enjoin the expenditure of funds in connection with special grand jury; adjudication filed declaring order convening special grand jury and appointing "special prosecutor" to be null and void and decree entered, adjudication by GOLD, P.J., KELLEY and BLANC, JJ. City officials appealed, and "special prosecutor" and others intervened as appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city officials and the district attorney, sought review of various decrees of the Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania). Intervening appellant special prosecutor also challenged the finding that his appointment was null and void. Petitioner citizens originally brought suit against the city officials alleging misconduct on the part of the district attorney. Writs of prohibition were also requested.


OVERVIEW: All these proceedings were predicated on four consolidated appeals regarding certain actions taken in the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, including the following: (1) a special grand jury was ordered, for which there was no warrant in law; (2) an attorney was appointed as special prosecutor, (3) an investigation was directed without limitation as to subject matter or time; and, (4) an elected constitutional officer was displaced from office, without due process. The court found that the judicial actions on the part of the judge went beyond the scope of his jurisdiction. The actions of the judge were found to have lacked legality as the judge was not assigned to the grand jury room when he commandeered the grand jury, and thus abused his discretion. The office of a special prosecutor did not exist, thus such an appointment was unlawful. The investigation ordered was found to have constituted an unwarranted interference with the orderly functioning of the legislative branch, and the court held that an elected official was entitled to due process prior to removal unless misconduct was clear.


OUTCOME: The decrees appealed from were affirmed, and the orders of the lower court which lacked legality were found null and void. A writ of prohibition filed on behalf of the district attorney was ordered issued.

Mayer v. D'Ortona


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 518; 184 A.2d 582; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 531


Argued September 25, 1962  
October 5, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 426, Jan. T., 1962, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1962, No. 2563, in case of William W. Mayer, taxpayer and registered elector, v. Paul D'Ortona, president, Council of City of Philadelphia. Judgment affirmed.

Mandamus.

Finding and judgment for defendant, opinion per curiam. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a taxpayer and registered elector, brought an action in mandamus to compel defendant president of the city council to hold a special election to fill a vacancy in the office of councilman. The Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) concluded that there was no vacancy and entered judgment for the president, and the taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action in mandamus to compel the president of the city council to hold a special election to fill a vacancy in the office of councilman. The lower court refused the writ, and the taxpayer appealed. The court held that when the mayor resigned and the president of council, pursuant to a Philadelphia Home Rule Charter provision, obtained a leave of absence from meetings of the council to serve as acting mayor, the president did not fill the vacancy in the office of mayor and did not vacate either his office of president of council or councilman. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the taxpayer's request for a writ of mandamus to require the president of the city council to hold a special election to fill a vacancy in the office of councilman.

White v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 397; 184 A.2d 266; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 516


Argued January 4, 1962  
September 25, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 346, 368 and 384, Jan. T., 1961, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1959, No. 1894, in equity, in case of Abraham White, South Philadelphia Realty Board, North Philadelphia Realty Board et al. v. City of Philadelphia, Philadelphia Housing Authority, and School District of Philadelphia. Decree reversed.

Equity. Before WEINROTT, J.

Adjudication filed declaring certain ordinances of City Council to be void and restraining defendants from proceeding with certain activities and decree entered. Defendants appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, City of Philadelphia, Philadelphia Housing Authority, and School District of Philadelphia, sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which, in plaintiff homeowner and realty boards' action in equity, declared that a city ordinance enacted under the Pennsylvania Housing Authorities Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 1541 et seq., was void.


OVERVIEW: The City enacted an ordinance known as Philadelphia, Pa., Ordinance No. 2350 that authorized the Authority to purchase and rehabilitate houses in a particular neighborhood and offer them as low-rent housing units. The homeowner and realty boards brought an action against defendants to have the ordinance declared void as unconstitutional. The trial court determined that the ordinance was indeed void and enjoined defendants from proceeding under the ordinance on the ground that defendants had exceeded their authority under the enabling provisions of the Pennsylvania Housing Authorities Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 1541 et seq. Defendants sought review of the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that the resident and realty boards did not claim any interest in their complaint that gave them standing to maintain the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that had declared that the ordinances were void.

297 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Brown Estate


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 214; 183 A.2d 307; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 485


Argued April 19, 1962  
July 6, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 133, Jan. T., 1962, from decree of Orphans' Court of Delaware County, No. 30 of 1940, in re estate of John A. Brown, Jr., deceased. Decree reversed.

Audit of account.

Adjudication filed directing distribution and decree entered, adjudication by VAN RODEN, P.J. Guardian and trustee ad litem appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed, case remanded to the Orphans' Court for such further proceedings as it may deem appropriate or necessary. Costs to be paid out of the principal of the estate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian ad litem, representing minor and unborn contingent remaindermen, sought review of a decree from the Orphans' Court of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), authorizing appellee trustee to invest the trust proceeds in common stocks and various authority bonds.


OVERVIEW: The testator died in 1919, leaving a trust with provisions for the payment of income for many lives in varying proportions and providing the trustee with power to invest in certain mortgages and bonds, including loans of the United States, Pennsylvania, New York, municipalities, townships, school districts, and "similar public divisions." The orphans' court found that the trustee was authorized to invest the trust funds in common stocks and authority bonds. The court reversed, finding that the testator's clear intent was to limit the trustee to exceptionally safe investments. The term "similar public divisions" meant political subdivisions and did not include Pennsylvania turnpike bonds. The Fiduciaries Investment Act of 1949, 20 P.S. § 821 et seq., as amended in 1951, allowing the fiduciary to invest in stocks where not expressly prohibited by the trust instrument, could not be applied to defeat the testator's clear intent. The restrictive investment clause in the testator's will was an express restriction within the meaning of the act. The orphans' court's ruling after the fourth account was not the "law of the case" and was subject to correction in subsequent distributions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the orphans' court.

Breslow v. School Dist.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 121; 182 A.2d 501; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 474


Argued April 24, 1962  
June 28, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction, No. 204, March T., 1962, in case of Ira M. Breslow, Thomas W. McGrew and G. Edward McLellan v. School District of Township of Baldwin. Defendant enjoined.

Original jurisdiction. Petition to enjoin school district bond issue.



DISPOSITION: Costs to be paid by defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a complaint against defendant Baldwin Township School District (Pennsylvania) to enjoin the school district from issuing and selling a proposed issue of general obligation bonds.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers commenced an action against the school district. The taxpayers had sought to enjoin the school district from issuing and selling a proposed issue of general obligation bonds. The court determined that the amendatory Act of July 28, 1961 (Act), 1961 Pa. Laws 917, was unconstitutional, null, and void and enjoined the school district from incurring any indebtedness under the Act. The court held that the definition of market value placed upon the term "assessed valuation" in and by the §§ 201, 203 of the Municipal Borrowing Law of June 25, 1941, 53 P.S. §§ 6201, 6203, as amended by the Act, violated Pa. Const. art. IX, § 8, as plain words in the constitution were given their common or popular meaning and it was a matter of common knowledge that in nearly every township, county, and city in Pennsylvania, property was assessed for tax purposes lower than its market value.


OUTCOME: With respect to the taxpayers' action for injunctive relief, the court held that the amendatory statute was unconstitutional, null, and void and enjoined the school district from incurring any indebtedness under the statute.

Commonwealth ex rel. Hines v. Winfree


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 128; 182 A.2d 698; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 475


Argued November 15, 1961  
June 28, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 117, Jan. T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, June T., 1959, No. 2783, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Harry V. Hines v. Howard Winfree, chief of police. Order affirmed.

Habeas corpus.

Order entered dismissing petition, opinion by TOAL, J. Relator appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed. Costs on Hines.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mayoral candidate appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his habeas corpus petition filed in connection with his arrest and conviction for violating a municipal ordinance.


OVERVIEW: An ordinance of the City of Chester (Pennsylvania) regulated the use of sound amplifying machines, prohibited the making of unnecessary noises, and required a permit for the use of loud speakers in public places. A campaign chairman applied for a permit to use a sound truck during a mayoral campaign. The application was rejected. The candidate proceeded to use a loud speaker and was arrested for violating the ordinance. The candidate filed a writ of habeas corpus, which the trial court dismissed after finding the ordinance was a constitutional exercise of police power and valid. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the trial court and held that the ordinance was not vague or indefinite but clearly expressed the intent of the city council. The court also held that compliance with the ordinance, including its per diem permit requirement, was not onerous or unreasonable and that the permit fee was reasonable absent evidence to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the candidate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus claiming that the he was convicted under an unconstitutional statute.

Delaware River Port Authority v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 169; 182 A.2d 682; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 480


Argued May 3, 1962  
June 28, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 51, May T., 1962, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 309 Commonwealth Docket, 1960, No. 2425, equity docket, certified to the Supreme Court by the Superior Court, in case of Delaware River Port Authority v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Decree affirmed.

Equity.

Decree entered denying plaintiff's motion for judgment on the pleadings and dismissing complaint, opinion by SWOPE, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at appellant's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant river port authority (authority) challenged the decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which denied its motion for judgment on the pleadings and dismissed its complaint against appellee Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission (commission) based on the commission's allocation of the relocation costs of intervenor electric company (company) to the authority.


OVERVIEW: The commission approved the authority's construction of portions of a bridge and allocated as costs the company's expenses in moving its electric lines to accommodate the construction. The authority appealed the allocation of costs, which was thereafter affirmed in a final order. In a separate proceeding, relocation costs for a different area of the bridge were allocated to the authority. However, this allocation was reversed because 66 P.S. § 1181 did not authorize the same. The authority then brought an action to enjoin the commission from certifying the costs that were upheld in the former proceeding. The trial court denied the authority's motion for judgment on the pleadings and, on appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decree. The court held that the opinion in the latter case did not establish the law of the case and render the former adjudication null and void. The former proceeding was entirely separate and distinct from the litigation that gave rise to the present appeal. The doctrine of res judicata also precluded the authority's equity action. The former decision, though it was in error, was allowed to become final and it was binding on all the parties thereto.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree that denied the authority's motion for judgment on the pleadings and that dismissed the authority's complaint against the commission.

 

301 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Key Realty Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


408 Pa. 98; 182 A.2d 187; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 473


Argued January 4, 1962  
June 13, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 22, Jan. T., 1962, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Sept. T., 1959, No. 1981, in re appeal of Key Realty Company from findings and order of Zoning Board of Adjustment of Media Borough. Order affirmed.

Appeal from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing to grant building permit.

Decree nisi entered affirming order of zoning board, exceptions dismissed and final decree entered, opinion by CURRAN, J. Exceptant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner filed an application with the Zoning Board of Adjustment to obtain a permit to erect an apartment house on a residential lot. The property owner had previously constructed a three-unit apartment building on an adjoining lot. The property owner sought review from a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the zoning board's order refusing to grant the building permit.


OVERVIEW: The zoning board initially denied the building permit based on the proposed apartment building's failure to meet the side yard requirements of the borough zoning ordinance. Subsequently, the zoning ordinance was amended to permit only the erection of single-family detached dwellings in the area, and the zoning board rejected another application for the building permit on that basis. On appeal, the court held that the council did not act improperly in passing the prohibitory ordinance. The court found that the property owner acquired no vested right in the continuation of the previous zoning classification, and the second apartment house was not a natural extension of the nonconforming use to which the land was devoted. The court also held that the zoning legislation did not violate the requirement of The Borough Code, 53 P.S. § 48303, that zoning legislation be enacted in accordance with a comprehensive plan. The court found that the ordinance constituted an integral part of a general land program for the county wherein the continued existence of the affected area as one being predominately of single or double homes was contemplated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decree affirming the zoning board's order that refused to grant the property owner's requested building permit.

Edwards Estate


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


407 Pa. 512; 180 A.2d 590; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 614


Argued March 13, 1962  
May 4, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 164, 165, 166, 167, 168, 169, 170, 171, 172 and 173, March T., 1962, from decree of Orphans' Court of Indiana County, Dec. T., 1957, No. 37, in re distribution of funds in hands of The Savings & Trust Company of Indiana, trustee under will of Harry Kelso Edwards, deceased. Decree affirmed.

Audit of account.

Decree entered dismissing exceptions to auditor's report and confirming report, opinion by MORRIS, P.J., specially presiding. Exceptants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; each party to pay own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant exceptants sought review of a decision from the Orphans' Court of Indiana County (Pennsylvania), which entered a decree dismissing the exceptions to an auditor's report and confirming the report.


OVERVIEW: The lower court had affirmed the auditor's report which held that the will in question violated the rule against perpetuities. The testamentary trustee had been directed to distribute the corpus of the estate to the testator's heirs at law. The issue was the correctness of the determination of the lower court that the invalid limitations were so much a part of testator's testamentary scheme of distribution that the intermediate life estates became infected and had to fall. The court held that the life estate as well as the ultimate gifts of corpus were so essential to the testator's scheme, that, being invalid, he would not have wanted the prior valid gifts of income to continue. The lower court had agreed with the auditor that the testator's plan in the relevant paragraph was to delay vesting of his estate until vesting in the great-grandchildren of the named beneficiaries or grandchildren who might be born after lives in being and 21 years thereafter. The court held that the testamentary scheme, the general plan of distribution, and dominant intent of the testator was to tie up his trust estate for a period beyond that permitted by the rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decree.

Bargain City U. S. A., Inc. v. Dilworth


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


407 Pa. 129; 179 A.2d 439; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 555


Argued November 30, 1961  
March 21, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 486, Jan. T., 1961, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1959, No. 1411, in equity, in case of Bargain City U.S.A., Inc. v. Richardson Dilworth, Mayor of City of Philadelphia, Donald Wagner, Managing Director of City of Philadelphia, Victor Blanc, District Attorney of City of Philadelphia, et al. Decree affirmed; reargument refused April 5, 1962.

Equity. Before DOTY, J.

Adjudication filed finding Act of August 10, 1959, P.L. 212 unconstitutional and void, exceptions to adjudication sustained and final decree entered dissolving injunction against defendants and declaring Act to be valid and dismissing complaint. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at appellant's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the exceptions of appellees, mayor of city, managing director of city, district attorney of city, and police commissioner of city, to the retailer's adjudication attacking the validity of P.L. 660, § 1 (1959), 18 P.S. § 4699.10 (act), dissolved the injunction against appellees, and declared the act to be valid.


OVERVIEW: The retailer attacked the validity of the act, which prohibited the retail sale of certain specified commodities on Sundays, on the grounds that the act violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 7 in that it was a local or special law regulating labor or trade, and that the act violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV because enforcement was conducted in a discriminatory manner by appellees. Appellees filed exceptions to the retailer's adjudication, which were sustained, and the trial court declared the act to be valid and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the act did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 7 or the Fourteenth Amendment because the legislative classification bore a reasonable and logical relationship to the end sought, that of an effective enforcement of a valid legislative act in an area particularly subject to violation. The court found that injunctive relief against the district attorney and the police commissioner was not justified because the action against those appellees on the issue of enforcement of the act necessarily abated upon their leaving public office.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment sustaining appellees' exceptions to the retailers' adjudication, dissolving the injunction against appellees, and declaring the act to be valid.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant civic association sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) entered in favor of appellee Lower Merion Township Board of Adjustment (Pennsylvania) finding an ordinance changing the zoning of an area valid.


OVERVIEW: The landowner successfully lobbied to have the zoning for his property changed so that he could build an apartment building. From the issuance of a permit to the owner, the civic association appealed to the Board questioning on substantive grounds the validity of the ordinance allowing the permit. The civic association then appealed to the court of common pleas which directed that the record be remanded to the Board for taking additional testimony. After hearing, the Board again denied the civic association's appeal and, on appeal from that ruling, the court of common pleas, without taking any additional testimony or hearing the matter de novo, upheld the Board's action. The civic association appealed. The court quashed the appeal because the only question the civic association appealed was that of the vague and indefiniteness of the ordinance. Since that issue had not been properly raised in the court of common pleas, it could not be heard on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the civic association's appeal.

Commonwealth v. Bricker


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


406 Pa. 422; 178 A.2d 699; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 697


Argued January 3, 1962  
March 13, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, No. 324, Jan. T., 1961, from order and sentence of Court of Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Philadelphia County, Amy T., 1961, Miscellaneous Docket, and No. 504, Jan. T., 1961, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1961, No. 965, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Glenn W. Bricker. Order and sentence of Court of Quarter Sessions affirmed; order of Court of Common Pleas affirmed; reargument refused March 30, 1962.

Proceedings in court of quarter sessions on appeal from summary conviction by magistrate. Before MILNER, P.J.

Defendant adjudged guilty and judgment of sentence entered. Defendant appealed.

Proceedings in court of common pleas on petition for writ of certiorari.

Order entered quashing writ, opinion by MILNER, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The Order of and the sentence imposed upon the defendant by the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County on May 5, 1961, is affirmed.

The Order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, dated September 29, 1961, is affirmed.

The costs of these appeals shall be paid by the defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order and sentence from the Court of Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) issued after he was convicted of violating local speed ordinances, and from an order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) quashing his writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating a local speed ordinance. Defendant responded with a rule to show cause as to why his conviction should not have been vacated. The court of quarter sessions concluded that the rule was improper, but in the interest of justice considered it as an appeal. The court of quarter sessions concluded that the issues raised in defendant's appeal were without merit, and affirmed his conviction. Defendant then filed an application for a writ of certiorari with the court of common pleas, which the Commonwealth sought to quash. The court of common pleas granted the motion, and defendant appealed both lower courts' orders. The court concluded as an initial matter that defendant's legal and constitutional contentions were devoid of merit. Furthermore, because there was adequate evidence to support his guilt, the sentence was affirmed. As to the order quashing his writ, the court noted that a defendant who had been convicted in a summary proceeding before a magistrate had to have made his election to proceed either by appeal or certiorari. Because defendant had already appealed, he was unable to seek review pursuant to certiorari. That order was also proper.


OUTCOME: The order of the court of quarter sessions convicting and sentencing defendant was affirmed, as was the order of the court of common pleas quashing his application for a writ of certiorari.

Cali v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


406 Pa. 290; 177 A.2d 824; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 678


Argued February 5, 1962  
February 13, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 240 and 241, Jan. T., 1962, from decrees of Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1961, Nos. 2238 and 2366, in cases of Anita Cali v. City of Philadelphia and Thomas P. McHenry, Chairman, and Maurice S. Osser and Louis Menna, City Commissioners; and James B. Burns v. City of Philadelphia and Thomas P. McHenry, Maurice S. Osser, Louis Menna, City Commissioners, et al. Decrees affirmed.

Equity.

Adjudication filed enjoining the holding of an election for the office of mayor in 1962, and decrees entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree in No. 240 affirmed; each party to pay own costs.

Decree in No. 241 affirmed; each party to pay own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the City of Philadelphia and various city officials, appealed a judgment entered in the Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) in favor of plaintiff residents, which enjoined a special election to fill the office of Mayor.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to section 3-500 of the Philadelphia Home Rule Charter, defendants, the city and various officials, upon the resignation of the Mayor, prepared an election to fill the vacancy to be held at the next general election in 1962. Plaintiff residents obtained an order enjoining that election in the common pleas court, and defendants appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the city's power to establish and enforce a charter derived from the legislature, which, in turn, derived the ability to delegate such power from the state constitution. The court found that in granting home rule to Philadelphia, the legislature required its elections to comply with the Pennsylvania Election Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 2600, which required all municipal elections to be held in odd-numbered years. The court found the language mandatory and applicable to special elections.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a lower court judgment, which granted an injunction in favor of plaintiff residents, precluding defendants, the City of Philadelphia and various city officials, from holding an election to fill a vacancy in the office of Mayor in the year 1962, as set forth in the city charter. The court held that the charter could not exceed limitations imposed by the legislature, which required municipal elections to be held in odd years.

The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


406 Pa. 229; 177 A.2d 809; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 672

* Reporter's Note: On May 28, 1962 the Supreme Court of the United States denied a petition for a writ of certiorari.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which reversed the decision of the Superintendent of Public Instruction sustaining the school board's dismissal of appellee teacher and ordered the teacher's reinstatement.

308 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Smith


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


405 Pa. 456; 176 A.2d 619; 1962 Pa. LEXIS 376


Argued November 22, 1961.  
January 2, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 5, Jan. T., 1962, from judgment and sentence of Court of Oyer and Terminer and General Jail Delivery of Adams County, Aug. T., 1960, No. 5, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Elmo Smith. Judgment and sentence affirmed.

Indictment charging defendant with murder. Before SHEELY, P.J.

Verdict entered finding defendant guilty of murder in the first degree, and penalty fixed at death, defendant's motion for new trial refused and judgment of sentence entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Oyer and Terminer and General Jail Delivery of Adams County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, upon a jury verdict, of murder in the first degree. The jury also heard evidence in order to determine the penalty after the conviction, which resulted in a verdict that sentenced defendant to death. He appealed the sentence, contending that the jury abused its discretion in sentencing him to death and that the trial court improperly answered a juror's question concerning the imposition of a life sentence. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that under § 701 of Pa. Penal Code, 1939 P.L. 872, codified at Pa. Stat. Ann. tit.18, § 4701, the jury had the duty of fixing the penalty between death and life imprisonment upon defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree and no discretion was allowed the trial court in sentencing therefore after the penalty was fixed. Neither the trial court nor the court on review had any authority to reverse or reduce the verdict of the jury that lawfully imposed the death sentence. The trial court properly answered a juror's question concerning the possibility of parole if a life sentence was imposed by instructing that such considerations should not be part of the deliberations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree and his death sentence.

Descamp Estate


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


405 Pa. 331; 175 A.2d 827; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 660

December 5, 1961

Audit of account. Before RAHAUSER, J.

Decree entered sustaining exceptions to account. Guardian appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian of the minor challenged the decree of the Orphans' Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the exceptions filed by appellee Veterans' Administration to legal fees charged to the estate in the accounting filed by the guardian after making claims on the minor's behalf to the Veterans' Administration.


OVERVIEW: The minor was the stepchild of a deceased war veteran of the United States. Her guardian was notified by the Veterans' Administration and Social Security Administration that all benefits payable in her behalf by those agencies would cease as of her 18th birthday. The guardian appealed from this decision to the agencies involved. Counsel was engaged to press the claims of the ward. The appeals were successful and counsel charged a fee of $ 1100 for his services. The guardian paid the amount, but at the audit of its account in the Orphans' Court, the Veterans' Administration, as an interested party under the World War Veterans' Act of April 24, 1929, 20 P.S. § 788, filed exceptions to payment of the $ 1100 fee. The lower court sustained the position of the Veterans' Administration and surcharged the guardian in the amount of $ 1090, giving the guardian credit for the $ 10 allowed by the Act of Congress. The guardian appealed and the court affirmed, holding that the limitation of fees applied to all claims administered by the Veterans' Administration, and that there was no question that Congress had the authority to impose such limitation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.

Rockwell v. York County Retirement Board


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


405 Pa. 406; 175 A.2d 831; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 671


Argued September 25, 1961.  
December 5, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 1, May T., 1962, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of York County, April T., 1960, No. 476, in case of Mary C. Rockwell, executrix of estate of Ella May Rockwell, deceased, v. York County Retirement Board. Judgment affirmed.

Mandamus. Before ATKINS, P.J., SHADLE and LIVERANT, JJ.

Opinion filed finding for plaintiff and judgment entered, opinion by ATKINS, P.J., LIVERANT, J., dissenting in part. Retirement board appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county retirement board sought review of the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania), which in a mandamus action awarded retirement benefits to appellee executrix of the estate of the deceased county employee.


OVERVIEW: The deceased county employee, a court stenographer, died four days subsequent to the effective date of the county's retirement system. Thirteen years earlier the employee had retired from another county and was receiving retirement benefits from that county during the period that she had worked for the most recent county. On appeal, three issues were raised: (1) whether the estate of a deceased county employee who was employed on the effective date of the retirement system but died before contributing to the retirement fund and before making application for retirement was entitled to the benefits of the retirement fund so long as her personal representative tendered the contribution based upon the compensation earned between the effective date of the system and the date of death; (2) whether folio and transcript fees paid to a court stenographer was to be included in computing the retirement benefits of such court stenographer; (3) whether a county employee was barred from receiving retirement benefits from two different and separate political subdivisions? The court determined issues (1) and (2) in the affirmative, and issue (3) in the negative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

312 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Catherwood Trust


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


405 Pa. 61; 173 A.2d 86; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 622


Argued April 25, 1961.  
July 26, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 184 and 185, Jan. T., 1961, from decree of Orphans' Court of Philadelphia County, No. 3263 of 1931, in re trust of Daniel B. Cummins Catherwood. Decree, as modified, affirmed; reargument refused August 11, 1961.

Audit of third account. Before KLEIN, P.J.

Adjudication filed confirming account, exceptions to adjudication dismissed and decree entered, before KLEIN, P.J., BOLGER, LEFEVER, SAYLOR and SHOYER, JJ., opinion by LEFEVER, J., concurring opinions by SHOYER and BOLGER, JJ. Exceptants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree, as modified, affirmed. Each party pay own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, in three separate actions, sought review of a judgment from the Orphans' Court of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which made a ruling adverse to appellants with respect to the Pennsylvania rule of apportionment.


OVERVIEW: The consolidated appeals presented three problems arising under Pennsylvania's rule of apportionment. The underlying facts involved the creation of an inter vivos trust, wherein the settlor's two children were to collect the income for life and, at their deaths, the res was to be distributed to the children's descendants per stirpes. The court analyzed the various rules of apportionment and concluded that the court below had erred with respect to the second problem presented in the case at bar--whether small stock dividends belonged to the life tenants or whether they should be apportioned. The court opined that it had never held that ordinary small stock dividends should be considered as income payable to the life tenant; it had also never held to the contrary. The court ruled that if a total stock distribution for the current year was payable at the rate of 6 percent or less of the corporation's outstanding shares before such distributions were made, such distribution in stock of the distributing corporation should be treated as income.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court concerning the state's rule of apportionment was modified and, as modified, affirmed.

 

313 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Schlesinger


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


404 Pa. 584; 172 A.2d 835; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 613


Argued March 17, 1961.  
July 18, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 208, March T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1957, No. 1608, in the matter of Hymen Schlesinger. Order reversed; reargument refused July 31, 1961.

Disbarment proceedings.

Exceptions to recommendation of Committee on Offenses dismissed and order of disbarment entered, order by MCNAUGHER, P.J. Attorney appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of disbarment is reversed and the record remanded with directions that the complaint be dismissed.

Mr. Justice MUSMANNO did not participate in the decision in this case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney was charged with violating his oath as an attorney by being a member of the Communist Party. The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) entered an order disbarring the attorney, based on the report and recommendation of a bar committee that the attorney was guilty of unprofessional conduct. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was a member of the Communist Party from 1946 to 1950. The court held that the attorney was deprived of his constitutional right to practice his profession without due process of law by the order of disbarment entered by the trial court. The bar committee acted, directly and through its subcommittee, which consisted of three of its own members, as prosecutor, judge, and jury at the hearing on the committee's own complaint against the attorney. The subcommittee's proceedings were legally incapable of supporting the trial court's order of disbarment, which was entered solely on the basis of the committee's report and recommendation. The court also held that the evidence before the subcommittee was insufficient, as a matter of law, to convict the attorney of professional misconduct because findings that the attorney was a member and functionary of the Communist Party did not justify an inference that he (1) lacked good moral character, (2) was not attached to the tenets of the United States Constitution, (3) advocated the forcible and violent overthrow of the government, or (4) engaged in or was associated with any unlawful activity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order disbarring the attorney.

Commonwealth v. McCoy


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


405 Pa. 23; 172 A.2d 795; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 619


Argued April 18, 1961.  
July 18, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 199, Jan. T., 1961, from judgment of Court of Oyer and Terminer and General Jail Delivery and Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Philadelphia County, July T., 1957, No. 351, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Frank McCoy. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused August 9, 1961.

Indictment charging defendant with murder. Before KELLEY, J.

Verdict entered finding defendant guilty of murder in the first degree; defendant's motion for new trial refused and judgment of sentence of death entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of sentence is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of sentence of the Court of Oyer and Terminer and General Jail Delivery and Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which was entered upon a jury verdict after the hearing required by the Split-Verdict Act of December 1, 1959, P.L. 1621, amending § 701 of the Penal Code of June 24, 1939, P.L. 872, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4701 (Pocket Part).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed a grocery store owner during an armed robbery. Defendant was indicted for murder and was tried under the Split-Verdict Act. At the trial of the issue of defendant's guilt or innocence, the jury returned a verdict of guilty of murder in the first degree. As required by the Split-Verdict Act, the trial court then entered upon a hearing with respect to the penalty to be imposed on the verdict, at which hearing the jury received additional evidence on the question of the penalty to be imposed on the convict, as between death and life imprisonment. The jury fixed the penalty at death. On review, defendant contended that the trial court erroneously permitted a victim of a prior armed robbery to testify at the penalty hearing. Affirming, the court held that it required a stretch of the imagination beyond all reason to say that the testimony of the victim of the prior unassociated robbery played any essential part in the fixing of the penalty by the jury, which had just heard all of the Commonwealth's evidence against defendant at the trial on the question of his guilt or innocence of the murder and which had found him guilty of that murder in the first degree.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentence.

Susquehanna Collieries Div. v. Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


404 Pa. 527; 172 A.2d 807; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 608


Argued May 31, 1961.  
July 10, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 99, 100 and 101, Jan. T., 1961, from decisions of Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, Nos. B-50175, B-50240, and B-50239, in case of Susquehanna Collieries Division, The M. A. Hanna Company v. Unemployment Compensation Board of Review. Decisions affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 193 Pa. Super. Ct. 242.



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the Board of Review which sustained the Bureau's determinations in each case are affirmed.

Mr. Justice BENJAMIN R. JONES took no part in the consideration or decision of this case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) which affirmed appellee unemployment board's decision granting unemployment compensation to various appellee employees during a period of partially paid plant shutdown pursuant to their collective bargaining agreement.


OVERVIEW: Under their collective bargaining agreement, employees were partially paid by the employer during a two-week plant shutdown. They applied for, and received, partial unemployment benefits for this period. The employer sought review of the decision of the unemployment compensation board, arguing they did not meet the eligibility requirements, in part based upon the claim they were not available for work as required by the law. On appeal, the court stated that an employee cannot be considered ineligible for benefits simply because the plant has shutdown for a vacation period as agreed to by him or his union. The court held that his eligibility may still be questioned if he is, in fact, individually unavailable for work; but this is, as stated, a determination aimed at his personal status, not one acquired by an agreement with the employer. The court found nothing in the record or in the briefs or arguments to indicate that claimants were unavailable for work, finding in fact, the determination of eligibility could only lead to the contrary conclusion that they were available.


OUTCOME: Based upon its determination that the employees were eligible for partial employment benefits, the court affirmed the decision of the unemployment compensation board.

Ejectment.

Pennsylvania Game Commission's preliminary objections overruled in part and sustained in part and order entered, opinion by PENTZ, P.J. Game commission and corporation appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, commonwealth and gas company, sought review of orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Clearfield County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the commonwealth's objection to the trial court's personal jurisdiction over it in an ejectment proceeding concerning land in which the commonwealth was the lessor and the gas company was lessee. The trial court also overruled the commonwealth's objection to its jurisdiction over the gas company.


OVERVIEW: An ejectment action was filed against a gas company as the lessee of land that was owned by the commonwealth. The commonwealth intervened in the action but subsequently filed objections to the trial court's jurisdiction over it and over the gas company. The trial court sustained the commonwealth's objection to the assertion of jurisdiction over it but overruled the objection to its jurisdiction over the gas company. On appeal, the court affirmed in part but reversed in part the trial court's orders. The court held that the trial court had correctly asserted jurisdiction over the action pursuant to 17 P.S. § 251. The court also held that the trial court had correctly asserted jurisdiction over the gas company because it was the necessary party to the action. The court further held that although the commonwealth held title to the property, the action sought to dispossess the gas company of the property Finally, the court held that the trial court had jurisdiction over the commonwealth despite its contentions of sovereign immunity because once the commonwealth had intervened in the action pursuant to 12 P.S. § 145, it waived its immunity to suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part but reversed in part orders of the trial court, which sustained the commonwealth's objection to the trial court's jurisdiction over it in an ejectment proceeding concerning land in which the commonwealth was the lessor and a gas company was lessee. The trial court also overruled the commonwealth's objection to its jurisdiction over the gas company.
