Heuchert v. State Harness Racing Com.


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


403 Pa. 440; 170 A.2d 332; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 485


Argued April 17, 1961.  
May 2, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 38, May T., 1961, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 214, Commonwealth Dcdket, 1960, No. 2414, in equity, in case of William P. Heuchert et al. v. State Harness Racing Commission et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity.

Decree entered sustaining preliminary objections in nature of demurrer and complaint dismissed, adjudication by RICHARDS, P.J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at appellants' costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision by the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which confirmed a chancellor's decree for appellees, the Pennsylvania Harness Racing Commission and the Pennsylvania Secretary of Agriculture, in a suit to enjoin appellees from issuing a license for a harness racing track under the provisions of the Pennsylvania State Harness Racing Act of 1959, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 4, § 301 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers instituted a suit to enjoin appellees from issuing a license to conduct a harness racing track to any person or corporation under the provisions of the Act. Appellees filed preliminary objections to the complaint in the nature of a demurrer and a chancellor entered a decree dismissing the complaint. The trial court confirmed the chancellor's adjudication. On appeal, the court held that the act did not constitute a local or special law regulating the affairs of counties or granting special or exclusive privileges in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 7. The Act required a petition to be signed by at least 5,000 registered electors before the subject of harness racing could be submitted to the voters. The court stated that nothing in the Act prevented counties from becoming members of the class having more than 5,000 registered electors and determined, therefore, that such a classification was not lacking in uniformity. The court found that a classification based on a certain number of registered electors was reasonable and founded on a genuine distinction. The court concluded that the Act did not grant any special and exclusive privileges to the licensees thereunder.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the taxpayers' assignments of error and affirmed the decree of the trial court.

 

319 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Griggs v. County of Allegheny


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


402 Pa. 411; 168 A.2d 123; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 377


Argued September 29, 1960.  
January 16, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 155 and 158, March T., 1960, from orders of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1958, No. 2384, in case of Thomas N. Griggs v. County of Allegheny. Order in appeal No. 155 reversed with directions; appeal No. 158 dismissed; reargument refused February 15, 1961.

Proceedings on exceptions to report of board of viewers awarding damages.

Opinion filed dismissing county's exceptions and orders entered, opinion by SOFFEL, J. Supplemental opinion filed dismissing plaintiff's exceptions and order entered, opinion per curiam. Plaintiff and county, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: I would affirm the Orders of the lower Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner and defendant municipality challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed all exceptions of both parties to the board of view that it had appointed. Plaintiff protested the damages that the board awarded to it for interference with the use and enjoyment of his land caused by flights of aircraft. Defendant contended that it was not liable for any damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner brought an action to recover damages from defendant municipality because of a substantial interference with the use and enjoyment of land caused by flights of aircraft at low altitudes. A board of viewers assessed damages and the trial court dismissed the exceptions of both parties to the board's decision. Both parties appealed. The court found that the navigable air space that Congress placed in the public domain did not include the path of glide for an airplane's take-off or landing. However, there was no evidence that defendant exercised any control over aircraft. Thus, plaintiff was precluded from recovering against defendant. The relief that plaintiff sought appeared to be contemplated by Section 403 of the Aeronautical Code of May 25, 1933, 2 P.S. § 1469, which placed liability on the owners or operators of the aircraft. Because the owners or operators were not clothed with the power of eminent domain, plaintiff could not proceed against them through a viewer's proceeding. The order dismissing defendant's exceptions to the viewers' report was reversed with directions that the viewers' report be vacated and set aside. Plaintiff's appeal was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court dismissing defendant municipality's exceptions to the viewers' report was reversed with directions that the report be vacated and set aside. There was no taking of plaintiff property owner's land by defendant because it did not control the aircraft. Plaintiff's appeal was dismissed because the owners of the aircraft had no power of eminent domain and a viewer's proceeding was not an available remedy.

Bowers v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Bd.


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


402 Pa. 542; 167 A.2d 480; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 396; 41 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,130


Argued April 18, 1960.  
January 16, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 31, May T., 1960, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket, 1957, No. 406, in case of Clarence P. Bowers v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board et al. Judgment affirmed.

Mandamus.

Adjudication filed finding for plaintiff and against defendants, and judgment entered, opinion by RICHARDS, P.J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board (board) sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee aggrieved party the relief he sought regarding his position on the board.


OVERVIEW: The aggrieved party instituted a mandamus action to compel the members of the board and the secretary of labor and industry to recognize him as a member of the board. The aggrieved party also sought to have the parties continue to certify to the auditor general the amount of salary due him. The aggrieved party was granted the relief he sought, and the board sought review. The board contended that the aggrieved party's term was an indefinite term. The court determined the attempted removal of the aggrieved party was without warrant of law and that he had to be restored to his position. The court concluded that duly confirmed members of board possessed tenure for the fixed terms they served. The court further determined that the governor did not have the constitutional power to remove a member of the board at his pleasure. Thus, the order granting the aggrieved party mandamus relief was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court granting the aggrieved party mandamus relief regarding his removal from the board.

 

321 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


YMCA v. City of Reading


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


402 Pa. 592; 167 A.2d 469; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 397


Argued April 26, 1960.  
January 16, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 164, Jan. T., 1960, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, No. 2783 Equity Docket, 1958, in case of Young Men's Christian Association of the City of Reading v. City of Reading et al. Decree affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Equity. Before HESS, J.

Adjudication filed finding for plaintiff, exceptions to adjudication dismissed and decree entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Record remanded for further proceeding in accordance with this opinion. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed an action in equity to enjoin defendant city form collecting real estate taxes on the taxpayer's building. The trial court entered its ruling. The Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania) ruled in favor of the taxpayer and the city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a charitable organization. It sought to enjoin the city from collecting real estate taxes on the portions of the taxpayer's building used for dormitories, a coffee shop, and rented by other charitable organizations. The taxpayer argue that its building was entirely exempt from taxation. Section 204(i) of the General County Assessment Law, 72 P.S. § 5020-204 exempted from taxation real property owned by a charity and used or occupied jointly by it and another charity. The court noted that a statutory procedure existed for challenging tax assessments. Equity only had jurisdiction over such challenges where there was a total want of power to tax or where the mode of assessment violated a constitutional right. Absent a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute or of official action thereunder, equity had no jurisdiction to restrain the collection of taxes. But the court nonetheless addressed the issues. The court held that § 204(i) did not apply to cases where the owner charity realized a rental income from the leasing of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's ruling relative to the building's dormitory and coffee shop but reversed with respect to the office rental.

Box Office Pictures, Inc. v. Board of Finance & Revenue


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


402 Pa. 511; 166 A.2d 656; 1961 Pa. LEXIS 391


Argued April 18, 1960; reargued November 22, 1960.  
January 4, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 15 and 16, May T., 1960, from judgments of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket, 1958, Nos. 355 and 356, in cases of Box Office Pictures, Inc. v. Board of Finance and Revenue of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Screen Guild Productions of Philadelphia v. Same. Judgments affirmed.

Mandamus.

Opinion filed sustaining defendants' preliminary objection and dismissing complaint, and judgments entered, opinion by KREIDER, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sued to recover fees paid under the Motion Picture Censorship Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 4, § 41 et seq., which had been declared void. Appellee Board of Finance and Revenue of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania objected on the ground that refund petitions were not timely filed. The taxpayers challenged the judgments of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the Board's objections.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers as distributors of motion pictures were required by the Motion Picture Censorship Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 4, § 41 et seq., to remit to the Pennsylvania State Board of Censors a certain sum for the examination of each film, reel or set of views of 1,200 lineal feet or less and a certain sum for each duplicate or print thereof. The taxpayers brought suit to recover the fees paid on the ground that the Act was rendered void ab initio by a prior Supreme Court of Pennsylvania case. The Board of Finance and Revenue contended that the taxpayers failed to file petitions for refund within the statutory period. The trial court sustained the Board of Finance and Revenue's objection. On appeal, the court held that the trial court, in the absence of an averment of payment under duress or protest, justly assumed the fees were voluntarily paid, and thus, the Board of Finance and Revenue had no power to entertain the taxpayers' petitions because they were not filed in conformance with statutory procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

 

323 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


1621, Inc. v. Wilson


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


402 Pa. 94; 166 A.2d 271; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 402; 93 A.L.R.2d 1274


Argued April 25, 1960.  
November 15, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 144, Jan. T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1959, No. 3537, in case of 1621, Inc. v. Morris Wilson et al. Order affirmed; reargument refused January 11, 1961.

Equity. Before GRIFFITHS, J.

Adjudication filed refusing to grant injunctive relief, and order entered. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner of a taproom-restaurant (owner) challenged the interim order from the trial court (Pennsylvania), which denied his request for a preliminary injunction enjoining appellee picketers from picketing and boycotting the owner's duly licensed establishment.


OVERVIEW: The owner of a taproom-restaurant in Philadelphia obtained a liquor license in an area that was zoned for both commercial and residential use. Within days, the picketers, Philadelphia residents who had protested the license, began picketing the taproom everyday except Sunday, bringing their children and carrying signs saying, "Less taprooms, more classrooms, more playrooms," and "We don't need another taproom." The owner sought a preliminary injunction against the picketers, and the chancellor entered what he termed an Interim Order reserving decision on the preliminary injunction, but limiting the pickets to three in number and otherwise regulating them. On appeal, the court affirmed, first finding that the order was appealable because even though the order was termed an "interim order," the chancellor's edict in practical effect denied the owner's requested relief. The court then found that the objective of the picketing, to persuade people not to patronize the taproom so that its owner would move to another location, did not violate a legitimate, clearly defined law or public policy of the state; thus it was protected free speech under U.S. Const. amend I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the interim order which denied the owner's request for a preliminary injunction against the picketers.

 

324 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


McGinley v. Scott


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


401 Pa. 310; 164 A.2d 424; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 528


Argued September 26, 1960  
October 11, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 392 and 393, Jan. T., 1960, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1960, No. 3718, in case of John P. McGinley v. William Z. Scott et al. Decree vacated and complaint dismissed.

Equity.

Adjudication filed dismissing defendants' preliminary objections and decree entered granting preliminary injunction, opinion by MCCLANAGHAN, J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree vacated and complaint dismissed; the parties to pay their respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant legislative committee members (members) appealed a decree of the Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania, which dismissed the members' preliminary objections and granted plaintiff taxpayer a preliminary injunction, in the taxpayer's action seeking to restrain the members from taking any action authorized by a certain Senate resolution, and to enjoin any expenditures of funds of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought the instant action against the members to prohibit the Pennsylvania State Senate from adopting a resolution at a regular session in an even-numbered year creating a committee of its members for the purpose of making certain specified investigations unrelated to either revenue or appropriations. The lower court ordered the members to show cause why a preliminary injunction should not issue, overruled their preliminary objections, and enjoined them preliminarily from performing the duties imposed upon them by the resolution. On the members' appeal, the court reversed, holding that the members' objection that the venue of the controversy was exclusively in Dauphin County pursuant to Pa. R. Civ. P. 1503(c) was well taken. Moreover, contrary to the lower court's findings, the Senate resolution involved was not a "law" within the purview of Pa. Const. art. II, § 4, and the adoption of the resolution at the 1960 regular session was not thereby prohibited. However, the Senate was without constitutional power to investigate the conduct of a particular district attorney as provided by the resolution involved. The court vacated the decree and dismissed the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's decree and dismissed the taxpayer's complaint seeking to prohibit action on a particular state Senate resolution.

 

325 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Eves v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


401 Pa. 211; 164 A.2d 7; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 519


Argued April 20, 1960  
September 26, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 167, 168 and 169, Jan. T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, April T., 1959, No. 5, in case of Schuyler Eves et al. v. Zoning Board of Adjustment of Lower Gwynedd Township. Order reversed.

Proceedings on appeal by protestants from decision of zoning board of adjustment which granted building permits.

Adjudication filed affirming decision of zoning board, and order entered, opinion by GERBER, J. Protestants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbors, citing 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 67003 of the Second Class Township Code, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) affirming a decision of appellee zoning board granting building permits to appellee landowner under ordinances creating a limited industrial zone for the landowner.


OVERVIEW: The neighbors contended on appeal that the ordinances failed to conform to enabling legislation. The zoning board and landowner argued that the ordinances were part of a comprehensive development plan. The court reversed the order. The court determined that the ordinances were at variance with legislative directives because they were not enacted in accordance with a comprehensive plan and devolved upon township supervisors duties beyond those outlined in the enabling legislation. The court concluded that the ordinances were invalid and that the permits were improperly issued. The court pointed out that the adoption of a procedure whereby it was decided which areas would eventually be zoned limited industrial on a case by case basis patently admitted that at the point of enactment of the ordinances there was no orderly plan of particular land use for the community and that the development itself would become the plan, which was the antithesis of zoning in accordance with a comprehensive plan under 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 67003.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court denying the appeal of the neighbors and affirming the zoning board's grant of building permits to the landowner.

Hazle Twp. Appeal


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


400 Pa. 194; 161 A.2d 600; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 333


Argued May 3, 1960.  
June 6, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 204, Jan. T., 1960, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Luzerne County, Feb. T., 1959, No. 231, in re annexation of a portion of Hazle Township and Sugarloaf Township to the Borough of West Hazleton. Order affirmed.

Proceedings on petition to annex property to borough.

Order entered allowing annexation of property, order by FLANNERY, J. Township supervisors appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order of annexation affirmed, costs to be borne by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township challenged a decision of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), which, in proceedings on a petition to annex property to a borough, entered judgment for appellee citizens allowing annexation of the property in question.


OVERVIEW: Under the Act of July 20, 1953, 1953 P.L. 550 a trial court approved the annexation by a borough of approximately 550 acres of land lying mostly in a township. The township appealed. It claimed that § 2 of the Act of July 20, 1953 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that, under Pa. Act of July 20, 1953, 1953 P.L. 550, § 2, the petition, after its approval by council was to be certified to a trial court by the secretary of the borough or township or clerk of the city. If, within 30 days thereafter, no person aggrieved by the ordinance complained, asking for the appointment of a board of commissioners as a fact finding body, the court was to determine the question, and, if it was satisfied as to the legality of the proceeding and the propriety of the annexation as serving public interests, would affirm the annexation. The court found that the annexation proceeding was a legislative and not a judicial proceeding and, therefore, was not subject to procedural due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of annexation.

Whitehall v. Oswald


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


400 Pa. 65; 161 A.2d 348; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 320


Argued April 22, 1960.  
June 3, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 4 and5, Jan. T., 1960, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County, Jan. T., 1959, No. 194, in cases of Township of Whitehall v. Gerald Oswald, and Same v. John Reiss. Judgment vacated.

Declaratory judgment action.

Opinion filed holding township ordinance valid, and judgment entered, opinion by HENNINGER, P.J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and petition dismissed at the plaintiff's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant trailer owners appealed an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County (Pennsylvania), which validated plaintiff township's ordinance prohibiting the occupation of a trailer for living quarters outside a duly permitted trailer park.


OVERVIEW: The township enacted an ordinance, which provided, inter alia, that no person could occupy any trailer for living quarters outside a duly permitted trailer park. Without any effort to enforce the provision against the trailer owners for violating the same, the township filed a petition in the lower court praying for a declaratory judgment affirming the constitutionality of the ordinance. The lower court adjudged that the ordinance was constitutional and the trailer owners appealed. The court held that the township was without standing to invoke the jurisdiction of the lower court for the purpose of having the constitutionality of its ordinance adjudicated in a declaratory judgment proceeding. The court found that if a question concerning the constitutionality of an ordinance was to have been passed upon, it could have been done properly only as a sequence of an actual controversy based upon a sufficient allegation by a complainant of being harmed or threatened with imminent harm in violation of constitutionally protected rights and that the Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act did not extend such a right to a political subdivision with legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court vacated a judgment declaring the township's ordinance valid.

In reversing, the court held that the jury was left with the impression that the landowner's title was impaired and thus that its property was worth only a fraction of the value attributed to it by the landowner's witness. The court further held that the admission by counsel for the county and the judge's affirmance of the landowner's point for charge that it had access at the date of taking were not sufficient to overcome the strong potential prejudice of the extended inquiry concerning the federal suit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the lower court that awarded a sum of money to the landowner in the condemnation proceedings and granted a new trial.

 

329 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Syme v. Bankers Nat'l Life Ins. Co.


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


400 Pa. 74; 161 A.2d 29; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 321


Argued April 20, 1960.  
May 23, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 194, Jan. T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1957, No. 7883, in case of Kathie V. Syme et al. v. Bankers National Life Insurance Company. Order affirmed.

Proceedings on petition for attorneys' charging lien.

Order entered discharging petition, opinion by SPORKIN, J. Attorneys appealed.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the lower Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which discharged their petition for a lien against the proceeds of a life insurance policy that were payable to appellee beneficiary.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys filed a petition to establish an attorney's charging lien upon the proceeds of the life insurance policy that were payable to the beneficiary. The lower court dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that an attorney had no lien upon a judgment recovered by him for a client in a common law action. Indeed, the court noted that the statute that attempted to establish such a lien had been declared unconstitutional. The court held that the rule that an attorney could claim his fees as a preference out of money raised by his services when it had come within the grasp of the court, on the principle that he was the equitable owner thereof to the extent of the value of his services, applied only to a court of equity or to a proceeding in the orphans' court. Moreover, the court noted that the imposition of a charging lien in a case such as the instant one was prohibited both by the terms of the insurance policy and by statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which dismissed the attorney's petition for a charging lien against the proceeds of a life insurance policy that the beneficiary was to collect.

Robinson v. Philadelphia


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


400 Pa. 80; 161 A.2d 1; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 322; 46 L.R.R.M. 2922; 1 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 14; 1 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 478; 40 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P66,539


Argued April 18, 1960.  
May 23, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 300, Jan. T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1959, No. 659, in case of Charles H. Robinson v. City of Philadelphia et al. Order affirmed.

Equity.

Adjudication filed sustaining defendants' preliminary objections and dismissing complaint, and order entered, opinion by ALESSANDRONI, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) sustained preliminary objections filed by defendants, city, city agency, and hospital board, and dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's suit in equity to enjoin defendants from carrying out a contract. The taxpayer appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: Defendants signed a contract with two private universities related to the operation, management, and control of a city hospital. The taxpayer alleged that the allocation of money under the contract was for an illegal purpose and was wasteful. The court affirmed the order denying the taxpayer's request for an injunction to stop defendants from carrying out the contract. The city's powers and responsibilities were not unlawfully delegated to a private party because the contract provided that the hospital board would continue to operate the hospital. Defendants were presumed to have acted lawfully and in good faith because the taxpayer failed to allege any facts to support his claim of waste and because the courts would not review defendants' determination of need in the absence of bad faith. The court also rejected the taxpayer's argument that the private universities' policies were discriminatory, thus making the contract contrary to public policy. Again, the taxpayer failed to state any facts to support his argument. Further, the contract specifically provided that the parties would not discriminate because of race, color, religion or national origin.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the taxpayer's suit in equity to enjoin defendants from carrying out a contract was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Scoleri


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


399 Pa. 110; 160 A.2d 215; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 433


Argued October 15, 1959.  
April 4, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 282, Jan. T., 1959, from judgment of Court of Oyer and Terminer and General Jail Delivery of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1958, No. 839, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Anthony Scoleri. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused April 19, 1960.

Indictment charging defendant with murder. Before CARROLL, P.J.

Verdict of murder in the first degree returned with penalty fixed at death; defendant's motion for new trial dismissed and judgment of sentence entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Oyer and Terminer of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction, defendant argued that the trial court erred in resuming defendant's trial after defendant attempted to commit suicide. On review, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion under the circumstances in resuming the trial after defendant's suicide attempt. The court then held that, while excerpts from the trial court's jury instructions were misleading, the instructions as a whole did not require reversal of the judgment. The court also held that caselaw subsequent to defendant's conviction that removed an accused's burden of proving alibi was not retroactive and thus did not apply to the case at issue. Additionally, the court held that the passage of the state's split-verdict statute, which worked to abolish a rule allowing the introduction of evidence of prior crimes in the guilt phase of capital criminal cases, did not apply retroactively to defendant's case. In denying a subsequent motion to reargue, the court held that defendant incorrectly deduced the court's vote on the issues involved in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and his death sentence. The court then denied the petition for reargument.

Cooper v. McDermott


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


399 Pa. 160; 159 A.2d 486; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 436


Argued January 13, 1960.  
March 22, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 103, Jan. T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1959, No. 1327, in case of George Cooper et al. v. Thomas F. McDermott. Order affirmed.

Equity. Before DOTY, J.

Opinion filed denying injunctive relief, and order entered. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the lower court is affirmed at the appellant's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied their petition to enjoin defendant police chief from taking any action in furtherance of the execution of extradition warrants.


OVERVIEW: The citizens, who were all from California, stood indicted, charged with the violation of, or conspiracy to violate, the state's anti-pornography laws. The citizens sought injunctive relief to halt the execution of extradition warrants issued pursuant to the 19 P.S. § 191.1 et seq. The trial court denied injunctive relief and the citizens appealed. The court affirmed the order that denied relief. The court ruled that no injunction should be granted except in a case reasonably free from doubt and when necessary to prevent great and irreparable injury. The court found that the only resulting harm to the citizens under indictment would be the inconvenience, personal expense, and embarrassment incident to the extradition and prosecution. The court ruled that such harm was insufficient to invoke the equitable jurisdiction of the court. The court noted that the citizens' harm was entirely of their own making and in no way attributable to any act of the state or its people.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court the denied injunctive relief to the citizens.

Pew Trust


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


398 Pa. 523; 158 A.2d 552; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 617


Argued November 11, 1959  
March 15, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 79, Jan. T., 1959, from decree of Orphans' Court of Montgomery County, No. 50,940 of 1958, in re deed of trust of Mary C. Pew. Decree affirmed.

Audit of second account.

Adjudication filed directing distribution of principal, certain exceptions to adjudication sustained and decree entered, opinion by TAXIS, JR., P.J. Life tenant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed 10 at appellant's costs.



10 Appellant has urged that the equities favor the life tenant and that the basic aim of the Pennsylvania Rule has been to make available to life tenants - usually the primary objects of the settlor's bounty - the earnings accumulated on corporate stock held by a trust. From 1933 through 1954 the Company's total earnings with respect to the shares held by this trust were $1,720,326. The cash dividends ($507,049) and the market value of the stock dividends ($2,111,220) received by the appellant totalled $2,618,268 or $897,942 more than the Company earned on the trust shares. If appellant sold the stocks distributed to him immediately he would have realized this amount; if he retained them, including subsequent stock dividends thereon, he has received from this trust 93,156 shares of the Company's stock which would have been worth as of December 31, 1954, $6,520,920, absolutely tax free.

 [***2]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant life tenant sought review from a decree entered in the Orphans' Court of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed his exception to an adjudication of the distribution of trust principal and the refusal of the apportionment of certain shares of stock that comprised the trust fund between the life tenant and appellee remaindermen.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the life tenant was not entitled to apportion the value of certain shares of stock that comprised the trust fund because the "stock split" of those shares did not comprise a division of earnings, profits, or accumulations of the shares that constituted the trust fund. The life tenant argued that the "stock split" was in reality a stock dividend, and as such, was a proper subject for apportionment. The court rejected the life tenant's argument. The court noted that there was a hybrid situation but regardless of how it was described, the "stock split" involved in the case did not constitute either a division of corporate earnings or profits and was, therefore, not a recognized apportionable event. Thus, the increase in the shares of stock that resulted from the stock split did not entitle the life tenant to apportionment because no division of corporate earnings or profits had taken place.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree.

Rubin v. Bailey


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


398 Pa. 271; 157 A.2d 882; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 585; 39 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P66,151


Argued January 14, 1960  
January 22, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 142, Jan. T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Nov. T., 1959, No. 28, in case of Albert Rubin et al. v. Bruce H. Bailey, Jr., Chief of Police, Montgomery Township, Montgomery County et al. Order affirmed.

Decree entered granting preliminary injunction; order entered, after hearing, dissolving preliminary injunction. Plaintiff appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retail merchants and intervenor retail merchants appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which dissolved a preliminary injunction restraining defendants, the chief of police and the district attorney, from arresting or threatening to arrest plaintiffs for alleged violations of the Penal Code of June 24, 1939, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4699.4, as amended by the Act of August 10, 1959, P.L. 660.


OVERVIEW: The amendatory Act of August 10, 1959, P.L. 660, proscribed the selling of certain personal property on Sunday and prescribed fines and penalties for violations. On appeal, the court affirmed the order, which dissolved the preliminary injunction against defendants. The question before the court was whether the trial court had reasonable grounds for its action. The court held that an act could not be declared unconstitutional unless it violated the constitution clearly, palpably, plainly, and in such manner as to leave no doubt or hesitation in the court. The court held that the constitutionality of the amendatory Act of 1959 was not so doubtful as to render unreasonable the trial court's conclusion that the presumption of the statute's constitutional validity had not been sufficiently impugned to warrant the continuance of the preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Booz v. Reed


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


398 Pa. 172; 157 A.2d 170; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 575


Argued November 17, 1959  
January 18, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 56, Jan. T., 1960, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Dec. T., 1956, No. 1618, in case of Elmer H. Booz v. Howard F. Reed, Jr. Judgment vacated.

Mandamus.

Order entered denying petition for writ of mandamus and judgment entered for defendant, order by OLMSTED, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and complaint dismissed.

I would reverse the judgment which the lower Court entered for defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tort claimant challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of appellee prothonotary in the claimant's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the prothonotary to accept the filing of the claimant's appeal of a judgment by a justice of the peace without the claimant's compliance with the Act of May 17, 1956, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 42, § 913a.


OVERVIEW: The Act provided that, when the judgment did not exceed $ 100, the judgment of the magistrate, alderman, or justice of the peace was final except by petition to the court of common pleas for special allowance. The prothonotary refused to accept the claimant's transcript because of the claimant's failure to comply with the Act. The claimant then sought a writ of mandamus to compel the prothonotary to accept the transcript and alleged that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the Act was constitutional. On appeal, the court found that the claimant could not raise the question of the Act's constitutionality because he failed to show that he was or would be denied a right of trial by jury on his appeal from the judgment by the justice of the peace. The claimant had no standing to question the constitutionality of the Act unless he showed that his constitutional right was or would be violated by the Act's enforcement. Compliance with the Act would not deprive the claimant of his constitutional right to a jury trial, and until a court of common pleas denied him leave to file his appeal, he sustained no harm to his constitutional right.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and dismissed the claimant's complaint.

46 South 52nd Street Corp. v. Manlin


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


398 Pa. 304; 157 A.2d 381; 1960 Pa. LEXIS 586


Argued April 30, 1959  
January 18, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 121 and 185, Jan. T., 1959, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1956, No. 6780, in case of 46 South 52nd Street Corporation et al. v. Oscar Manlin et al. Decree reversed.

Adjudication filed dismissing complaint, exceptions to adjudication dismissed, and final decree entered, opinion by GRIFFITHS, J.; HAGAN, P.J., dissenting. Plaintiffs and defendant, respectively, appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newsstand owner and appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, (Pennsylvania), in a dispute regarding the operation of a newsstand.


OVERVIEW: The corporation had instituted this action in equity to enjoin newsstand owners from operating a newsstand for the sale of newspapers, magazines, pocket books and comic books on the sidewalk of a public street in Philadelphia. The corporation had request the newsstand owner relocate to another sidewalk. The newsstand owner sought review of the lower court's order. The corporation contended that the operation of the newsstand constituted both a trespass and nuisance. The court determined that the sale and distribution of newspapers and other printed materials were such a public use it had to be permitted on sidewalks. The court concluded that the corporation as fee owner of the sidewalk was entitled to possession free and clear of any encroachments. The court held that because the newsstand owner did not have permission to maintain the newsstand either from the city or from the fee owner, the maintenance of such a newsstand constituted a trespass upon the corporation's property and could be enjoined.

338 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Eastern Motor Express, Inc.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


398 Pa. 279; 157 A.2d 79; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 419


Argued April 28, 1959  
December 30, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 20 and 21, May T., 1958, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 242 Commonwealth Docket, 1954, and No. 133 Commonwealth Docket, 1955, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Eastern Motor Express, Inc., and Same v. Riss & Company, Inc. Judgment reversed in each case.

Proceedings on appeal from decision of Board of Finance and Revenue refusing to review tax settlement.

Adjudication entered against Commonwealth and in favor of taxpayers; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and judgment entered for taxpayers, opinion by NEELY, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment in each case is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commonwealth of Pennsylvania sought review of decisions by the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which held that the Corporation Income Tax Law of 1951, 1951 Pa. Laws 1763, was unconstitutional and, therefore, the tax imposed on defendant companies thereunder was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth imposed a tax on the companies under the Corporation Income Tax Law of 1951, 1951 Pa. Laws 17639 (Act). The commonwealth brought an action to collect the tax. The lower court determined that the Act was in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 and that the imposition of the tax on the companies was invalid as being imposed on the companies' privilege of engaging in interstate commerce. Upon appeal, the court reversed the decision. The court found that the Act was intended to include and tax only foreign corporations which were engaged solely in interstate commerce in the commonwealth and which employed property or carried on local activities in the commonwealth in connection with interstate commerce. The court held that the levies under the Act were not privilege taxes based on the right to carry on business in commonwealth. The commonwealth was to collect only through ordinary means. The tax, therefore, was not open to the objection that it compelled the companies to pay for the privilege of engaging in interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the companies.

Brown v. Dickey


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 454; 155 A.2d 836; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 477


Argued September 29, 1959  
November 25, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 124, March T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1958, No. 3544, in case of John W. Brown, Jr. Equipment Rental Corporation v. Robert J. Dickey, trading as R. J. Dickey Company, et al. Order affirmed.

Proceedings on attachment execution.

Garnishee's preliminary objections sustained and order entered dissolving writ of attachment, opinion by ELLENBOGEN, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff equipment lessor sought review of the order of the trial court (Pennsylvania) which dissolved a writ of attachment execution sur judgment against defendant employer.


OVERVIEW: After the decedent's representative obtained a judgment on the verdict equally against the equipment lessor and the employer based on negligence, the equipment lessor discharged the judgment by payment of the full sum. The equipment lessor then issued a writ of attachment execution sur judgment against the employer and named the workmen's compensation carrier as garnishee. The court below ordered the writ of attachment execution dissolved upon the payment of $ 342, the balance of the amount due to the representative under the workmen's compensation award. The equipment lessor sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's holding that the writ was to be discharged upon payment of the balance of the compensation award. The court held that the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act was inapplicable because of the lack of a joint liability. The court found that the limited right of contribution was based on the equitable principle that the moving party was not entitled to recover twice for the same wrong.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dissolving a writ of attachment execution sur judgment against the employer.

341 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Koppers Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 523; 156 A.2d 328; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 485


Argued May 25, 1959  
November 24, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 56, May T., 1959, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 454 Commonwealth Docket, 1956, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Koppers Company, Inc. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused December 31, 1959.

Proceedings on appeal by taxpayer from decision of Board of Finance and Revenue refusing to review tax resettlements. Before RICHARDS, P.J., without a jury.

Adjudication filed dismissing appeal, defendant's exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign corporation sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which upheld the Corporate Net Income Tax Act's (Act) constitutionality and appellee commonwealth's inclusion of dividends, interest, proceeds from security sales, and proceeds from asset conversions in the Act's gross receipts fraction that was used to determine the foreign corporation's net income in the commonwealth.


OVERVIEW: In order to determine the net income of the foreign corporation, which transacted part of its business inside the commonwealth, the commonwealth used three fractions under the Act: 1) tangible property; 2) wages and salaries; and 3) gross receipts. When the commonwealth included dividends, interest, proceeds from security sales, and proceeds from asset conversions in the gross receipts fraction, the foreign corporation brought an action challenging the inclusions and the Act's constitutionality. Following an unfavorable judgment, the foreign corporation sought review, and the court affirmed. After finding the security sales had been properly included in the fraction, the court held the proceeds from the asset conversions had been includable under the ordinary definition of gross receipts, the term having not been statutorily defined. Furthermore, the court held the exemption of dividends and interest from taxation had not excluded those items from the foreign corporation's gross receipts. Finally, the court held the Act's imprecise measurement of income was not constitutionally fatal and that its misapplication had not violated the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment which upheld the Act's constitutionality and the commonwealth's inclusion of dividends, interest, proceeds from security sales, and proceeds from asset conversions in the Act's gross receipts fraction that was used to determine the foreign corporation's net income in the commonwealth.

Locust Club v. Hotel & Club Employees' Union


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 357; 155 A.2d 27; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 465; 45 L.R.R.M. 2091; 38 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P65,843


Argued May 5, 1959  
October 21, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 190, Jan. T., 1959, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1957, No. 2822, in case of Locust Club v. Hotel and Club Employees' Union, Local No. 568, AFL-CIO et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity. Before GRIFFITHS, J.

Adjudication filed dismissing complaint; plaintiff's exceptions to adjudication dismissed and decree entered, dissenting opinion by HAGAN, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is affirmed, costs on appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), denying its motion for a preliminary injunction restraining appellee union from picketing pursuant to the Labor Anti-Injunction Act, 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 206a et seq.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court was correct in holding that it was without jurisdiction to impose an injunction. The court held that, because the word "employer" in the Labor Anti-Injunction Act, 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 206c, specifically included corporations not for profit, the club was an employer within the meaning of the Act. The court held that it was clear that the request for an injunction was a labor dispute that was included within the Act, and thus to grant the injunction would violate the public policy declared by the Act. Moreover, the court noted that the trial court also was justified in refusing to impose the heavy hand of injunction under the circumstances of the case as a court of equity, where it found that the picketing was constitutionally protected because it did not have an unlawful object, was not forbidden by law, and did not contravene public policy. The court upheld these findings because they were in accordance in the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of a preliminary injunction for club.

 

343 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Ayers v. Morgan


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 282; 154 A.2d 788; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 451


Argued May 27, 1959  
October 21, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 106, Jan. T., 1959, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, July T., 1958, No. 897, in case of Chester A. Ayers v. Dr. Philip J. Morgan. Judgment reversed.

Trespass for personal injuries.

Defendant's motion for judgment on the pleadings granted and judgment entered for defendant, opinion by LEWIS, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the court below is reversed with a venire facias de novo.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania) granting appellee doctor's motion for judgment on the pleadings stating that the statute of limitations under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 12, § 34 had run on appellant's claim. Appellant alleged that appellee committed a trespass resulting in personal injuries when he failed to remove a surgical sponge from appellant's abdomen after surgery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient underwent surgery in 1948 for an ulcer. He continued to experience pain and, in 1957, discovered that a surgical sponge had been left in his abdomen after the surgery. Appellant filed an action against appellee doctor for trespass causing personal injuries. The trial court granted appellee's motion for judgment on the pleadings based on the running of Pennsylvania's two-year statute of limitations under § 34, and appellant sought review. The court reversed. The court found that appellee's negligence was not in the use of the sponge, but in his failure to remove it. The court held that the statute could not have started to run when appellee failed to remove the sponge because, at that time, appellant had suffered no damages. Thus, the court held that the statute of limitations on appellant's injury began running when appellant discovered that the sponge had been left in his abdomen. Therefore, appellant's action was timely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that granted appellee doctor's motion for judgment on the pleadings on the basis that the statute of limitations had run on appellant patient's claim for trespass that resulted in personal injuries. The court held that the statute of limitations had not begun to run on appellant's claims until he discovered that a sponge left in his abdomen by appellee after surgery had caused his injuries.

Grimaldi v. Local No. 9


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 1; 153 A.2d 214; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 425; 44 L.R.R.M. 2445; 37 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P65,583


Argued April 21, 1959  
July 2, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 298, Jan. T., 1958, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1956, No. 6964, in equity, in case of Louis J. Grimaldi v. Local No. 9, Journeymen Barbers, Hairdressers and Cosmetologists International Union et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity. Before WEINROTT, J.

Adjudication filed granting injunction against defendants; defendants' exceptions to adjudication dismissed and decree entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Local 9 was given every opportunity to present its case fully in the lower court and we are satisfied that the findings of fact and conclusions of law are justified by the record. We therefore affirm the decree entered in the Court of Common Pleas, and place the cost on the appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant union sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that granted plaintiff business owner's petition for an injunction preventing the union from picketing his shop, from interfering with his business, and from intimidating or attempting to intimidate him to join the union.


OVERVIEW: The owner was the proprietor of a barbershop in which he had no employees. Several union men appeared outside his barbershop with signs attempting to force the owner to join the union. The union was made up of barbers, hairdressers and cosmetologists who are employees in barber and beauty shops owned by others. The owner successfully petitioned to restrain and enjoin the union, with its officers and members, from picketing his shop, from interfering with his business, and from intimidating or attempting to intimidate him to join the union. The court noted that the owner was not qualified for membership in this union because he was not an employee. The court held that the picketing of a one-man establishment by a union was an invasion of an American's freedom to determine his own economic destiny when he stood alone in an enterprise of his own. The court opined, however, that labor unions had the right to picket for organizational purposes, such as to persuade non-union employees of an establishment to join a union.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the injunction in the owner's favor preventing the union from picketing the owner's shop, from interfering with the owner's business, and from intimidating or attempting to intimidate the owner to join the union.

Commonwealth v. Blumenstein


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


396 Pa. 417; 153 A.2d 227; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 567


Argued January 14, 1958; reargued April 22, 1959  
July 2, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 139, Jan. T., 1958, from judgment of Superior Court, Feb. T., 1958, No. 1, affirming judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lackawanna County, Dec. T., 1956, No. 8, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Martin Blumenstein. Judgment reversed.

Same case in Superior Court: 184 Pa.Super.Ct. 83.

Indictment charging defendant with giving and permitting exhibition of moving picture of lascivious, obscene, indecent and immoral character and tending to corrupt morals. Before EAGEN, J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence entered thereon, defendant appealed to Superior Court which affirmed judgment. Appeal by defendant to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and defendant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant theater manager appealed an order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed his conviction of unlawfully exhibiting obscene motion pictures under 18 P.S. § 4528.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with the giving and permitting exhibition of motion pictures of a lascivious, sacrilegious, obscene, indecent, or immoral character under § 4528. Upon his conviction, defendant appealed to the trial court, which affirmed his conviction and sentence. On further appeal, the court reversed and discharged defendant. The court held that federal court decisions were conclusive and that the word sacrilegious was held unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court, the test of being lascivious, indecent, immoral or impure was rejected by the same court, and that the words lascivious, indecent, and obscene were synonymous, thus leaving the single term obscene to consider. The court held that the proper standard for judging obscenity was whether to the average person, applying contemporary community standards, the dominant theme of the material taken as a whole, appealed to prurient interest. The court found that § 4528 could not pass this test and thus, defendant's conviction was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of unlawfully exhibiting obscene motion pictures.

Kingsley International Pictures Corp. v. Blanc


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


396 Pa. 448; 153 A.2d 243; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 568

July 2, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 206 and 235, Jan. T., 1958, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1957, No. 2390, in case of Kingsley International Pictures Corporation v. Victor Blanc, District Attorney. Decree reversed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, film distributor, sought review of the decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which sustained defendant district attorney's preliminary objections, denied the distributor's motion for preliminary injunction, and dismissed the complaint in the equity action brought by the distributor to permit the exhibit of a film in Philadelphia.


OVERVIEW: The film distributor had an exclusive agreement to release a film in America. Butcher v. Rice


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 158; 153 A.2d 869; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 440


Argued May 6, 1959  
June 30, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 27, May T., 1959, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket, 1958, No. 313, Equity Docket No. 2319, in case of Harry K. Butcher et al. v. John S. Rice, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Decree affirmed; reargument refused August 10, 1959.

Equity.

Adjudication filed dismissing complaint and decree entered, opinion by SOHN, J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at appellants' costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the complaint brought by the taxpayers for relief in equity where the taxpayers claimed that defendant Secretary of the Commonwealth should have been enjoined from certifying candidates or holding elections.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers challenged the trial court's dismissal of their action for the enjoinment of the Secretary's ability to certify candidates or to hold an election. The taxpayers claimed that the Apportionment Act of May 10, 1921, P.L. 449 was unconstitutional and that the General Assembly should have divided the state into senatorial districts. The Secretary claimed that the action should have been dismissed for failure to join the General Assembly as a necessary party. The court affirmed the dismissal of the case, as the court was without the power to grant the relief that the taxpayers sought. The court held that the General Assembly's failure to divide the state into senatorial districts raised a purely political question. Whether the aforementioned act required such division into districts that were as nearly equal as was possible was within the discretion of the General Assembly. Additionally, an election of senators at large, as suggested by the taxpayers was not legal. Pa. Const. art II, § 16 provided that each district was only entitled to elect one senator. The election could not be at large because by law they had to be elected by districts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint brought by the taxpayers for equitable relief to enjoin the certification of candidates or the holding of elections by the Secretary, as the court was without the power to grant the relief sought by the taxpayers.

Costello v. Rice


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


397 Pa. 198; 153 A.2d 888; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 441


Argued May 6, 1959  
June 30, 1959; August 10, 1959


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 4, May T., 1960, from order on special writ of certiorari to Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, April 24, 1959, in case of Daniel T. Costello v. John S. Rice, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Bill dismissed; reargument refused August 10, 1959.



DISPOSITION: Petition for reargument denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner filed a petition for a special writ of certiorari to the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) for disposition of questions of law in an action against appellee Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, challenging the constitutionality of the Apportionment Act of May 10, 1921, P.L. 449, as amended by the Act of July 26, 1923, P.L. 106. The court dismissed the bill and appellant moved for reargument.


OVERVIEW: Appellant moved for reargument on the grounds that the court in its previous opinion dismissing appellant's bill did not expressly pass upon his contention that the Pennsylvania Senatorial Apportionment Act of May 10, 1921, P.L. 449, was unconstitutional for its failure to conform to Pa. Const. art. II, § 16, which required two senators for a county with a one and three-fifths population ratio. The court denied appellant's petition for reargument. The court held that the Act was a valid statutory enactment that conformed to the Pennsylvania Constitution when enacted and that a mere change in the population of a county that required reapportioning of a senate district under the Pennsylvania Constitution did not render the Act invalid. The Act would be rendered invalid only if the legislature reapportioned the district pursuant to the Act in violation of the applicable constitutional provisions. The court concluded that the courts were without authority to compel the legislature to reapportion the legislative districts of the state and that the legislature's failure to reapportion state legislative districts was a political and not a justiciable question.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's petition for reargument.

Angle v. Commonwealth


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


396 Pa. 514; 153 A.2d 912; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 575


Argued May 25, 1959  
June 30, 1959

Proceedings on exceptions by Commonwealth to findings of board of viewers in condemnation.

Order entered dismissing Commonwealth's exceptions, opinion by DEPUY, P.J. Commonwealth appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth challenged the order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Franklin County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed its exceptions to an award of damages made to appellee farmers in their action seeking the same after a swath of their land was condemned for use in a road-widening project.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth approved plans for the reconstruction and improvement of a road that was near the lands held by the farmers. Appearing on the Commonwealth's plans, but otherwise unnoted, were pencilled lines suggesting that, at a future time, the Commonwealth may have desired to further widen the road. Thirty-two years after improving the road, the Commonwealth implemented its plan to widen it. The farmers sued the Commonwealth, seeking damages for the encroachment of their land. The farmers were awarded damages, to which the Commonwealth excepted. The exceptions were dismissed and the Commonwealth appealed. The court affirmed, holding that when the Commonwealth's department of highways filed its original plans, it made no effort to advise the farmers, directly or indirectly, that some day it would cut a swath 50 feet wide through the farm, and that there was no prior indication, either by word or symbol, that the Commonwealth had intended to condemn a 50-foot belt of land. The court noted that there was nothing more fundamental in representative government than that no one may have been deprived of life, liberty, or property without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court.

Transamerican Freight Lines v. Commonwealth


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


396 Pa. 64; 151 A.2d 630; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 515


Argued April 21, 1959  
May 28, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 18, May T., 1959, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 372 Commonwealth Docket, 1957, in case of Transamerican Freight Lines, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Order affirmed. * 


* Reporter's Note: On November 11, 1959 the Supreme Court of the United States denied a petition for a writ of certiorari.

Proceedings on appeal by taxpayer from refusal of Board of Finance and Revenue to review tax settlement. Before NEELY, J., without a jury.

Adjudication filed dismissing appeal and directing judgment for Commonwealth, exceptions dismissed and judgment entered. Taxpayer appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a decree and order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) dismissing the taxpayer's appeal from the refusal of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania) to review the tax settlement made by defendant Commonwealth's (Pennsylvania) fiscal officers. The tax was imposed under the Act of June 22, 1931, as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 2183 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a foreign corporation that was engaged in Pennsylvania exclusively in interstate commerce as a common carrier. It owned two freight terminals within the Commonwealth. The taxpayer disagreed with tax that was imposed on the taxpayer's mileage traveled over the Pennsylvania Turnpike. The taxpayer claimed that the tax violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err when dismissed the appeal because the Commerce Clause was not violated. A State could, consistent with the Commerce Clause, impose upon vehicles engaged in interstate commerce a reasonable, nondiscriminatory excise tax as compensation for the use of its highways. The taxpayer did not show that the tax plus the toll exceeded fair compensation for its use of the Turnpike, or that there was a lack of uniformity in the operation of the tax. The court rejected the taxpayer's contention that Turnpike mileage could not be used in the taxing formula. The Act and its supplements indicated that the Turnpike was intended by the Legislature to be part of the State highway system.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the taxpayer's appeal was affirmed.

Pennsylvania R. Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


396 Pa. 34; 152 A.2d 422; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 510


Argued April 28, 1959  
May 18, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 182 and 183, Jan. T., 1959, from order of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1958, No. 313, reversing in part the order of Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, March 24, 1958, in case of The Pennsylvania Railroad Company v. The Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission et al. Order vacated and set aside; reargument refused June 3, 1959.

Same case in Superior Court: 187 Pa.Super.Ct. 590.

Proceedings before Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission upon exception by railroad to rule proposed by commission.

Order entered by commission adopting new rule in revised form. Railroad appealed to Superior Court, which reversed order in part, opinion by WRIGHT, J. Appeal to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Superior Court, entered November 14, 1958, is hereby vacated and set aside.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad excepted to a rule proposed by appellee Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. The railroad appealed the order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which reversed the part of the commission's rule that required application to and approval by the commission prior to the removal, elimination, or substantial change in the schedule of any passenger train.


OVERVIEW: The railroad challenged a rule that promulgated by the public utility commission. The superior court issued an order that abrogated the part of the rule that required the railroad to obtain the commission's approval prior to the removal, elimination, or substantial change in any passenger train schedule. The railroad appealed. The court vacated the order and held that the superior court was without jurisdiction to review the commission's rule because the rule had not yet been applied to the railroad. There was no justiciable controversy and the superior court did not have the authority to render an advisory opinion. The superior court's jurisdiction rested exclusively in express statutory authorization provided by § 1101 of the Public Utility Law, 66 P.S. §§ 1431(a), 1391 (1937). Under those statutes, only parties "affected" by a commission order or who had been required to observe or carry into effect a commission regulation or order had standing to appeal to the district court or otherwise complain. Because there was no commission order directing the railroad to comply with the challenged rule, there was no statutory authority for the railroad's appeal to the superior court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and set aside the superior court's order that reversed the part of the commission's rule that required application to and approval by the commission prior to the removal, elimination, or substantial change in the schedule of any passenger train.

In re Tahiti Bar, Inc.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. 355; 150 A.2d 112; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 625


Argued January 15, 1959  
March 25, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Same cases in Superior Court: 186 Pa.Super.Ct. 214 and 186 Pa.Super.Ct. 223.

Appeal, No. 355, Jan. T., 1958, from order of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1957, No. 268, affirming order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, Nov. T., 1956, No. 1122, in the matter of Tahiti Bar, Incorporated. Order affirmed.

Appeal by licensee from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board suspending restaurant liquor license and amusement permit.

Order entered dismissing appeal, opinion by SLOANE, J. Licensee appealed to Superior Court which affirmed order. Appeal to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed. Costs on appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensees challenged a ruling from appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board (board), which suspended the licensees' liquor licenses and amusement permits because the licensees permitted lewd, immoral, or improper entertainment on their premises in violation of 47 P.S. § 4-493. The suspensions had been affirmed on separate appeals to the Court of Quarter Sessions for the County of Philadelphia and the Superior Court.


OVERVIEW: The suspensions were imposed after board officers visited the licensees' premises on four occasions and witnessed "strip acts," which involved the removal of substantially all of the female performers' apparel, accompanied with "bumps and grinds." The licensees argued that § 4-493 violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the U.S. Constitutions in that it abridged freedom of speech and expression and that the terms of § 4-493 were void for vagueness under the Fourteenth Amendment. The decisions had been affirmed by two lower appellate courts and went to the next appellate level on allocatur. The court affirmed the suspensions, holding that § 4-493 and Pa. Liquor Control Bd. Reg. 110 (regulation) were valid and constitutional. The terms "lewd and immoral," as used in 47 P. S. § 4-493 were sufficiently precise to conform to Fourteenth Amendment due process. The regulation was directed against a well-defined group, and its purpose was the abolition of certain well-recognized and prevalent evils historically associated with the consumption of alcohol on licensed premises. The board's action in suspending the licenses was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rulings from the two lower appellate courts sustaining the board's action in suspending the licensees' alcohol licenses and amusement permits and found that the underlying statute and regulation were constitutional.

Tidewater Oil Co. v. Poore


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. 89; 149 A.2d 636; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 590


Argued January 7, 1959  
March 16, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 54 and 59, Jan. T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Sept. T., 1957, No. 383, in case of Tidewater Oil Company v. F. S. Poore et al. Order reversed; reargument refused April 13, 1959.

Proceedings on appeal by property owners from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing to grant building permit. Before TOAL, J.

Adjudication entered sustaining appeal, exceptions dismissed and final order entered. Township and intervening defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; costs on the appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a township and intervening landowners, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which reversed a zoning board decision and awarded to appellee oil company a permit to build a "tank farm" on farmland that it owned and was zoned "A Residential."


OVERVIEW: The company attempted to have the zoning of its land changed from residential to industrial so that it could build a tank farm on which large tanks for storing gasoline and petroleum products would have been installed. The township refused to change the zoning or to issue a permit to allow the tank farm. The trial court reversed the zoning board's decision on the ground that refusal to allow the tank farm was unconstitutional, arbitrary, and unreasonable because the land was about the geographical center of a supposed industrialized area. Reversing, the court held that the record did not bear out the conclusion about the geographical center. Further, the court found that the trial court's jurisdiction was limited to determining whether there was substantial evidence to support the board's findings, whether there was any mistake of law, and whether there was any abuse of discretion. However, the court found that the trial court failed to limit itself to such scope of review. The court found that the township had the right to take whatever measures the situation demanded to prevent foreseeable harm and to limit an encroaching imperilment in its residential district.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

 

355 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Philadelphia v. Northwood Textile Mills, Inc.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. 112; 149 A.2d 60; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 593


Argued November 24, 1958  
March 16, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 340, Jan. T., 1958, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1957, No. 5586, in case of City of Philadelphia v. Northwood Textile Mills, Inc. Judgment affirmed.

Proceedings on municipal lien.

Adjudication filed granting plaintiff's motion for judgment for want of sufficient defense and judgment entered for plaintiff, opinion by DOTY, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding on a municipal lien for excess water and sewer rents pursuant to the Act of May 16, 1923, 1923 Pa. Laws 207, as amended, 53 P.S. § 7107, defendant property owner appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the motion of plaintiff city for judgment for want of sufficient affidavit of defense and its preliminary objections to the property owner's counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: Services were supplied by the city, the property owner's tenant failed to pay water charges, and a lien was filed against the premises. An amended writ of sci. fa. was served on the property owner, who filed an affidavit of defense and counterclaim. The trial court entered judgment for the city and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected the contention that the purpose of Philadelphia, Pa., Code of General Ordinances tit. 19, § 1606(3) was to impose on the city a requirement of due notice before it could can either shut off the water or assert a statutory lien. The failure of the city to shut off the water did not affect the enforcement of the lien under the Act of May 16, 1923, 1923 Pa. Laws 207. The court rejected the property owner's contention that the city could not enforce a statutory lien for excess water and sewer rent because the city negotiated and agreed with the tenant alone for the payment of delinquent water and sewer rent, and hence, was estopped from enforcing the lien.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which sustained the city's motion for judgment for want of sufficient affidavit of defense and its preliminary objections to the property owner's counterclaim in a proceeding on a municipal lien for excess water and sewer rents.
