Department of Licenses & Inspections v. Weber


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


394 Pa. 466; 147 A.2d 326; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 366


Argued November 21, 1958.  
January 12, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 294, Jan. T., 1958, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1957, No. 2878, in case of Department of Licenses and Inspections et al. v. Nancy Weber. Order reversed.

Appeal by beauty shop proprietress from decision of the Board of License and Inspection Review.

Adjudication sustaining appeal and reversing adjudication of the Board and order entered, opinion by GLEESON, J. City of Philadelphia appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed, the ordinance is sustained, and the adjudication of the City's Board of Licenses and Inspection Review is re-instated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city licensing department (department) sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which reversed the department's decision requiring appellee beauty shop owner to obtain a city license and to introduce certain features into her shop so that she could meet the city's safety and sanitation standards.


OVERVIEW: The department issued a decision that required the beauty shop owner to obtain a city license and to introduce certain features into her shop so that she could meet the city's safety and sanitation standards. On appeal by the beauty shop owner, the trial court issued an order that reversed the department's decision, and it appealed. On further appeal, the court reversed the trial court and reinstated the department's decision. The trial court found the state had preempted the field of beauty culture regulation, and that no municipality could step into that area of supervision and control. The court disagreed. The Barber Act, 1935 Pa. Laws 158, § 2, had provided that nothing contained in this act could be construed as prohibiting any municipality from adopting appropriate ordinances that were not inconsistent with this act. The court concluded that there was nothing in Beauty Culture Act, 1933 Pa. Laws 242, 62 P.S. § 507, which prevented the city from issuing its ordinance regulating the operation of a beauty shop.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, and reinstated the city licensing department's decision requiring the beauty shop owner to obtain a city license and to introduce certain features into her shop so that she could meet the city's safety and sanitation standards.

Prichard v. School Dist.


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


394 Pa. 489; 147 A.2d 380; 1959 Pa. LEXIS 369


Argued November 24, 1958.  
January 5, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 10, Jan. T., 1959, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Misc. No. 11401 of 1957, in case of Edwin C. Prichard v. School District of Willistown Township. Judgment reversed.

Proceedings under Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act.

Judgment entered declaring that § 677.1 of the School Code of 1949 is unconstitutional as applied to certain properties of petitioner, opinion by HARVEY, P.J. Township appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas, Chester County (Pennsylvania), which entered a judgment that the School Code of 1949, codified at 24 P.S. § 6-677.1 (1952), was unconstitutional as applied to appellee property owner.


OVERVIEW: The property owner built on his property after September 1, which would have had the effect of delaying increased taxation because of the improvement for a period of almost two years. In order to remedy that situation the legislature enacted a law, 24 P.S. § 6-677.1 (1952), which provided for the reassessment of property after the regular assessment period had passed. The property owner challenged the constitutionality of § 6-677.1. The trial court held that § 6-677.1 was unconstitutional because there was no right of appeal and the statute was too indefinite and vague. On appeal, the court reversed because the time provisions in § 6-677.1 were directory and not mandatory, which meant that the property owner had a right of appeal from a reassessment. The court also held that § 6-677.1 was not a new tax levy; that it was not discriminatory because it was applied uniformly; and that it was not vague, indefinite, or ambiguous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that a property tax reassessment statute was unconstitutional as applied to the property owner.

 

358 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Water & Power Resources Board v. Green Springs Co.


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


394 Pa. 1; 145 A.2d 178; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 276


Argued May 28, 1958.  
October 9, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 195, Jan. T., 1958, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, March T., 1957, No. 2, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania Water and Power Resources Board v. Green Spring Company, Inc. Order reversed; reargument refused November 5, 1958.

Equity.

Adjudication entered sustaining preliminary objections and dismissing complaint and final order entered, opinion by SHEELY, P.J., specially presiding. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and the matter remanded to the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Costs to abide the event. 8 



8 The record indicates that, in addition to this equity action, the Commonwealth instituted a criminal action against the defendant and its president for violation of Section 7 of the Act, that both defendants were indicted and motions to quash the indictments were filed on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. While the Court below in its opinion stated that its action would determine not only the preliminary objections filed in the equity action but also the motions to quash the indictments in the criminal action, yet in its order the Court simply sustained the preliminary objections in the equity action. The motions to quash the indictments are not before this Court.

 [***2]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Water and Power Resources Board of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania (board) challenged the decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the preliminary objections by defendant company, a fish hatchery, and ruled the Water Obstruction Act (Act), 32 P.S. § 681 et seq., violated Pa. Const. art. II, § 1, in that it constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative authority.


OVERVIEW: The board instituted an equity action alleging the company, without the board's consent or permit, increased by 17 inches the height of a pre-existing water obstruction dam across a non-navigable stream flowing through its land. The board sought injunctive relief. The Act was the basic authority for the board's action. The trial court was of the opinion the act lacked definite standards, policies, and limitations by which the action of the board could be governed. The trial court stated the purpose of the Act was not indicated. On review, the court reversed and remanded holding that (1) the Act's title was declarative of its object, (2) both the statutory language and the circumstances surrounding the passage of the act indicated the legislative purpose and why the regulation of water obstructions was necessary, (3) the board was not granted the power to determine what the law should be, but simply to apply the law as enunciated by the legislative body to particular circumstances, (4) the board's authority to act was not subject to its whim or caprice, it was circumscribed by a definite standard, and (5) the definite standards were neither vague nor indefinite.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that the act constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative authority and remanded for further proceedings. The court held the act did not present a clear, palpable, and plain violation of the Pennsylvania Constitution, but on the contrary a reading of the statute in its entirety was convincing of its validity.

Barth v. School Dist.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 557; 143 A.2d 909; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 392


Argued June 2, 1958  
July 25, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 276 and 277, Jan. T., 1958, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1957, No. 2262, in case of Frederic H. Barth v. School District of Philadelphia et al. Decree affirmed; reargument refused August 15, 1958.

Equity.

Adjudication entered dismissing defendants' preliminary objections; defendants' exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered granting an injunction, opinion by OLIVER, P.J., dissenting opinion by SLOANE, J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school district sought review of a final decree of the Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted plaintiff taxpayer's motion for an injunction restraining the school district from expending funds on a program to curb juvenile delinquency.


OVERVIEW: The school district entered into an agreement with the City of Philadelphia to institute a program to curb juvenile delinquency. The taxpayer filed a complaint in equity on behalf of himself and other taxpayers to enjoin the school from making any expenditure in performance of the agreement. The trial court issued a final decree granting the injunction. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's final decree and declared the agreement illegal and void. The court held that the school district was an agency of the legislature and had only the powers granted to it by statute. The court held that the school district had no statutory authority to enter into an agreement to fund a juvenile delinquency program. The court held that the agreement was illegal pursuant to art. VI, § 610 of the Pennsylvania Public School Code (Act), 1949 Pa. Laws 30, 24 P.S. § 610, which provided that the use or payment of public school funds by a school district for any purpose not provided in the Act was illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's final decree enjoining the school from expending funds on the juvenile delinquency program. The court declared the agreement between the school district and the city illegal and void.

Commonwealth v. Voci


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 404; 143 A.2d 652; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 365


Argued April 25, 1958  
July 1, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 242, Jan. T., 1958, from judgment of Superior Court of Pennsylvania, Oct. T., 1957, No. 242, affirming judgment of Court of Oyer and Terminer and Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Lancaster County, June Sessions, 1954, No. 161, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Tony Voci. Judgment affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 185 Pa.Super.Ct. 563.

Indictment charging defendant with bookmaking and pool selling. Before JOHNSTONE, J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence thereon. Defendant appealed to Superior Court, which affirmed the judgment. Appeal to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Superior Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania, which affirmed a trial court's judgment convicting him of bookmaking and pool selling, a violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4607, and refusing his motions for a new trial and in arrest of judgment. Among the issues raised was the admissibility of telephone conversations intercepted in violation of § 605 of the Federal Telecommunications Act of 1934, 47 U.S.C.S. § 605.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of bookmaking and pool selling. The superior court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Defendant argued that the "best evidence" rule required that the contents of a tape recording be proven by the playing of the recording itself, that there was no evidence of venue, and that the conviction could not stand because it was based solely upon unauthorized interception and divulgence of telephone conversations in violation of § 605. The court stated that the superior court correctly held that the best evidence of the intercepted conversations was the testimony of a detective who had actually heard the conversations as they occurred. There was sufficient evidence of record to establish that defendant was in the county in which venue was laid at the time he committed the offense. Even though wiretapping by state officials violated § 605, a state rule of evidence allowing admission of such evidence in state courts would not be overturned. The wiretapping evidence was admissible at the time of defendant's conviction and was sufficient in nature and quality to support the conviction because it established that defendant had illegally accepted some 11 bets.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

Home Life Ins. Co. v. Board of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 447; 143 A.2d 21; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 373


Argued April 30, 1958  
June 30, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 44, Jan. T., 1958, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Nov. T., 1956, No. 24, in case of Home Life Insurance Company of America v. Board of Adjustment of Lower Merion Township. Order affirmed.

Proceedings on appeal by property owner from decision of board of adjustment.

Final order entered dismissing appeal for lack of jurisdiction, opinion by KNIGHT, P.J. Property owner appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed at appellant's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) dismissing the owner's appeal from a decision of appellee, a board of adjustment, which quashed the owner's appeal from the refusal of the zoning officer to entertain the owner's petition for a variance that would allow it to erect an apartment house on its land. The board filed a motion to quash the owner's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed with the zoning officer a petition requesting a variance that would allow it to erect an apartment house on its land. It did not apply for a building permit and did not submit any plans with its request. The zoning officer refused to entertain the owner's petition. The owner appealed to the board to contest the validity of a zoning ordinance as it applied to his property. The board quashed the owner's appeal. The owner then appealed to the trial court, which determined that the sole question before it was whether the owner adopted the proper procedure to have the constitutionality of the ordinance determined. The trial court dismissed the owner's appeal, and the owner sought review. The court first refused to quash the appeal, finding that the owner had a right to appeal from the trial court's decision. The court then determined that the owner failed to follow the prescribed procedure for questioning the constitutionality of the ordinance. The court held that the owner had to first apply for a building permit, accompanied by plans of a proposed structure, and only upon the refusal of such a permit, could the owner challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

United States v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 537; 143 A.2d 341; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 389


Argued April 24, 1958  
June 30, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 253, Jan. T., 1958, from judgment of Superior Court of Pennsylvania, Oct. T., 1955, No. 27, affirming orders of Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission at Investigation Docket No. 24, in case of United States of America v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Judgment reversed.

Same case in Superior Court: 184 Pa.Super.Ct. 380.

Proceedings before Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission following institution by commission on its own motion, of investigation to determine whether railroad was transporting property at charges other than as provided in its officially filed tariff.

Order entered affirming prior order of commission, asserting jurisdiction over matter and enjoining railroad from charging rates other than those in its tariff filed with commission. United States appealed to Superior Court, which affirmed order. Appeal to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Superior Court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the United States of America, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Pennsylvania, which affirmed an order of respondent, the state public utility commission, enjoining a railroad from charging the United States rates other than those in the railroad's tariff with the public utility commission.


OVERVIEW: The Commission instituted proceedings against the United States and determined a state-regulated railroad was transporting or offering to transport property for federal agencies at special rates in violation of §§ 303 and 304 of the Public Utility Law of Pennsylvania, 66 P.S. §§ 1142, 1143. The Commission affirmed its prior order, which asserted jurisdiction over the matter and enjoined the railroad from charging the United States discounted rates. On appeal, the trial court affirmed the Commission's order. On further appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court found that application of the Act to federal government would have imposed an unreasonable burden. The court relied upon common law, which held the exemption of the United States' procurement services from the discretionary authority of a state agency was not violative of the mandate of state statutory law. The court ruled that common law holding that state regulation imposed no prohibition on the federal government was distinguishable. The court further decided that regulations authorized by 10 U.S.C.S. §§ 2301-2314 sanctioned the policy of negotiating rates for shipment of federal property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which affirmed the order of the public utility commission enjoining the railroad from charging the United States rates other than those in the railroad's tariff with the public utility commission.

Board of Zoning Appeals v. Silas


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 10; 142 A.2d 24; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 319


Argued May 1, 1958  
May 26, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 185, Jan. T., 1958, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, Sept. T., 1957, No. 822, in case of Board of Zoning appeals of the City of Scranton et al. v. Alex Silas et al. Order affirmed.

Proceedings on appeal by protestants from the decision of the Board of Zoning Appeals.

Adjudication entered sustaining appeal and final order entered directing board to revoke use permit, opinion by HOBAN, P.J. Property owners and board appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, permit applicants and a zoning board, challenged a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which entered a verdict in favor of appellee neighboring property owners after the neighbors argued that the applicants were not entitled to a certificate of use for a store from the board because the business at issue violated Scranton, Pa., Zoning Ordinance § 3 (1924).


OVERVIEW: The applicants, landlords and tenants of a building, sought a certificate of use in order to turn the building at issue into a store. Initially, the request for a certificate was refused, but after a full hearing before the board, the certificate was issued. Thereafter, the neighbors appealed the board's decision to the trial court, which concluded that the applicants were not entitled to the certificate. On appeal, the court upheld the trial court's judgment in favor of the neighbors. Specifically, the court held that the record clearly indicated that the board abused its discretion when it awarded the certificate to the applicants since the commercial enterprise did not remotely qualify under the provisions of the zoning ordinance. In addition, the court emphasized that it was clear from the record that the operation of the commercial enterprise, considering its size and scope, would have had a very definite bearing on the public health, safety, and general welfare of the community. Lastly, the court concluded that the limitations in the zoning ordinance, directed at businesses "for neighborhood use" only, constituted a proper constitutional exercise of police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Ullom v. Boehm


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. 643; 142 A.2d 19; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 484


Argued April 23, 1958  
May 26, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 2, May T., 1958, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket of 1956, No. 264, Equity Docket, No. 2202, in case of George A. Ullom, trading as Price Optical Company v. Charles H. Boehm et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity.

Adjudication entered dismissing complaint; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered, opinion by NEELY, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, each party to hear own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant optician sought review of a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which dissolved an injunction prohibiting the enforcement of the Act of 1956, 63 P.S. § 237, and dismissed his complaint.


OVERVIEW: The optician asserted that that the enforcement of the Act of 1956, 63 P.S. § 237, which prohibited advertising the price of products used for ophthalmic purposes, impaired his right of freedom of speech and constituted an unauthorized exercise of police power. He obtained a temporary injunction in the trial court against the enforcement of the Act. The trial court later dissolved the injunction and dismissed the complaint. The optician appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that as the state's regulation of the practice of optometry was already found to be a valid exercise of its police power, the state could regulate the sale of glasses. As the fitting of the glasses into suitable frames was part of the operation of preparing glasses to make them usable, the state could regulate the sale of frames. As advertising could have a direct bearing on the quality of lenses and frames, the state could regulate that too. The court found that the amendment of 1956 was germane to the original Act of 1917, and promoted but a single objective, the protection of the eyesight of the public. Thus, it did not introduce a new subject in violation of constitutional prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree dissolving the injunction and dismissing the optician's complaint.

Reargument granted October 10, 1957. Reargued November 18, 1957. Before JONES, C.J., BELL, CHIDSEY, MUSMANNO, ARNOLD, JONES and COHEN, JJ. Order of reversal entered on June 28, 1957 vacated and opinion withdrawn April 21, 1958. Order of court below affirmed; reargument refused May 27, 1958.

Final order entered affirming the decision of the zoning board and dismissing the appeal. Construction company and its transferee appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the action of appellee zoning board in refusing the developer's application for a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought permission from the zoning board to erect a dwelling on a subdivision lot that was a portion of the developer's tract of unimproved land. The zoning board denied permission because the developer's plan did not comply with zoning requirements that the lots be of a minimum size. The developer alleged that the zoning regulations were unconstitutional because they were arbitrary and capricious and they had no substantial relation to public health, safety, morals, or general welfare. The developer appealed from the trial court's judgment in favor of the zoning board. On appeal, the court held that the burden of proving clearly and unmistakably the unconstitutionality of a legislative enactment was upon the person so asserting. The court stated that in a case such as this one, it was to presume that the zoning board acted with purpose to serve the public welfare and even when there was room for difference of opinion as to whether the ordinance was designed to serve a proper public purpose, the court would not substitute its judgment for the zoning board. The court found that the zoning requirement bore a reasonable relation to the promotion of the general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the zoning board.

Commonwealth v. Rockwell Mfg. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. 339; 140 A.2d 854; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 462


Argued January 14, 1958  
May 2, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 24, May T., 1958, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1956, Commonwealth Docket No. 489, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Rockwell Manufacturing Company. Judgment affirmed.

Proceedings on taxpayer's appeal from decision of Board of Finance and Revenue refusing to review corporate net income tax resettlement.

Adjudication entered dismissing appeal; defendant's exceptions overruled, and judgment entered for Commonwealth, opinion by RICHARDS, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a corporate taxpayer, challenged a decision from appellee, the Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue, which refused to review a resettlement of its corporate net income taxes for the tax year 1953. The taxpayer argued that an amendment to the Pennsylvania Corporate Net Income Tax Act, excluding proceeds from securities sales from the definition of gross receipts, applied retroactively to the resettlement.


OVERVIEW: When the Department of Revenue learned that the taxpayer had not included the proceeds from securities sales in its gross receipts, the Department resettled the taxpayer's 1953 corporate net income taxes. Before the resettlement was approved, the Pennsylvania Corporate Net Income Tax Act was amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 3420b, to exclude such proceeds from the definition of gross receipts. The taxpayer argued that the use of the term "heretofore" should be construed to mean that proceeds from securities transactions could not be included in gross receipts regardless of the taxable year in which they occurred. On appeal, the court explained that the legislature had broad taxing powers, including the power to tax retroactively, but that it had to clearly express an intent to do so in light of the rule favoring prospective statutory construction. Nothing in the Act suggested an intent for retroactive application. The proposed construction was contrary to the Pennsylvania Statutory Construction Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 46, §§ 573, 574, and 581. It would also impose different tax burdens on corporations with offices located inside and outside the Commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Board.

 

367 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Best v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 106; 141 A.2d 606; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 330


Argued October 9, 1957  
May 2, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 177, March T., 1957, from order of County Court of Allegheny County, 1953, No. A 1317, in case of Pauline G. Best v. Zoning Board of Adjustment of the City of Pittsburgh. Order affirmed; reargument refused June 3, 1958.

Appeal by property owner from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing to grant variance. Before KAUFMAN, J.

Order entered sustaining the decision of the zoning board of adjustment. Property owner appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of an order from a trial court (Pennsylvania), which sustained the decision of appellee zoning board of adjustment (board) refusing to grant a variance.


OVERVIEW: The property owner had a home, which contained 22 rooms and 7 baths, located in a single-family district. The trial court sustained the board's refusal to grant a variance. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court determined that when the property owner purchased the house she knew or should have known of the provisions of the zoning ordinance restricting the property to use as a one-family dwelling and of the large expenditures required to maintain and keep up the property. Thus, the property owner took the property with the conditions of economic hardship staring her in the face, and she could not be heard to complain. The city's undertaking to control the density of its population in accordance with a comprehensive plan drawn to promote the welfare of the community was neither arbitrary nor unreasonable. The court was unable to say that requiring the property owner to use her property in conformance with the provisions of the zoning ordinance would not preserve the attractive characteristics of the community and the property values therein. Therefore, the attack upon the reasonableness of the application of the ordinance to the property failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which sustained the board's decision refusing to grant a variance to the property owner.

Commonwealth ex rel. Hendrickson v. Myers


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. 224; 144 A.2d 367; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 341


Argued November 11, 1957  
March 24, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 36, Jan. T., 1958, from judgment of Superior Court of Pennsylvania, Oct. T., 1956, No. 283, affirming order of Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, March T., 1956, No. 136, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Robert E. Hendrickson v. David Myers, Warden. Judgment affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 182 Pa.Super.Ct. 169.

Habeas corpus.

Order entered discharging rule and refusing petition, opinion by SATTERTHWAITE, J. Relator appealed to Superior Court which affirmed order. Appeal by relator to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Superior Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania that affirmed an order denying inmate's petition of habeas corpus in an action against appellee prison warden.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pressed only one issue in seeking review in 1957, namely, that the sentence imposed in 1946 on him was illegal and void because the sentencing judge was informed of and considered his juvenile court record in imposing sentence. The inmate had been found delinquent when he was approximately 17 years of age as the result of a burglary then committed by him. The inmate contended in his writ of petition for habeas corpus that the use of his juvenile court record in the consideration of the sentence was in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 11, § 261. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court. The court found that the inmate's juvenile court record was not introduced or presented as evidence in the 1946 trial. It further found that the inmate's juvenile court record was not considered, even after the trial, to determine a factual issue, that is, his guilt or innocence of the crime with which he had been charged. The court determined that the juvenile record was taken into consideration by the trial judge in 1946 after the inmate had pleaded guilty and then only for the purpose of imposing a fair, proper, and just sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court that had upheld the denial of the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, holding that a trial court on sentencing could consider the inmate's juvenile court record.

 

369 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Dwyer v. Dilworth


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. 123; 139 A.2d 653; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 427


Argued January 15, 1958  
March 17, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 364, Jan. T., 1957, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1956, No. 2969, in case of Cynthia Dwyer v. Richardson Dilworth, Mayor of the City of Philadelphia et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity. Before CARROLL, J.

Decree entered ordering that preliminary injunction issue against defendants; defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings granted, and final decree entered for defendants. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from a decree of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted a motion for judgment on the pleadings filed by defendants, a mayor and others. The taxpayer had sought to enjoin a competitive examination for the position of clerk of quarter sessions court.


OVERVIEW: In a prior decision, the court had held that the office of the clerk of the courts of oyer and terminer and quarter sessions of the peace had become a city office, upon consolidation of the city and county, and was subject to the civil service provisions of the Home Rule Charter. A qualifying examination was prepared for the employees appointed to their posts prior to the effective date of the charter. In effect, the taxpayer was seeking to have the court reconsider that portion of its prior opinion which dealt with the office of clerk of quarter sessions. The taxpayer contended that subjecting the employees of the clerk's office to municipal civil service would threaten the principals of separation of powers. However, the court held that only a person who was affected could raise the constitutional question. That the taxpayer paid tax monies to the city treasury did not establish her standing to maintain the suit, unless she could also demonstrate that her pecuniary interest in the proper use of such funds would be jeopardized, and no such interest was alleged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree.

 

370 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Sleighter v. Banmiller


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. 133; 139 A.2d 918; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 429


Submitted November 13, 1957  
March 17, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 99, Jan. T., 1958, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County, Oct. T., 1957, No. 142, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Sleighter v. William J. Banmiller, Superintendent. Order affirmed.

Habeas corpus.

Order entered denying petition, opinion by DEPUY, P.J. Relator appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator inmate sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate contended that he was denied due process of law at his trial because his involuntary confession was received in evidence, mob hysteria influenced the trial court and the jury, and he was denied the effective assistance of legal counsel.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of first-degree murder in the death of his six-year-old foster child based mainly upon his confession. The inmate contended that police pressure and promises induced his written confession. The court determined that the trial court properly charged the jury and left to them the determination of whether the confession was voluntarily given without inducements. Additionally, the inmate confirmed the correctness of the contents of his confession in a sworn application to the Board of Pardons. His confession was not rendered constitutionally objectionable by reason of being made in custody unless the detention induced the confession. The court also determined that the inmate failed to establish that he was denied a fair trial because the public was beset by hysteria or passion because he failed to show that the jury was influenced and because there was no evidence that the trial was conducted under other than peaceable and orderly circumstances. The court found that the trial record refuted the inmate's claim that his attorneys were ineffective and that it could not consider de novo the merits of their decision to refrain from presenting any evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order.

Pennsylvania R. Co. v. Schwartz


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. 619; 139 A.2d 525; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 544


Argued October 7, 1957  
March 17, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 8, May T., 1958, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1956, No. 2215 Equity Docket, No. 401 Commonwealth Docket, in case of The Pennsylvania Railroad Company v. Leon Schwartz et al. Decree reversed.

Equity.

Adjudication filed finding for defendants and dismissing complaint; final decree entered, opinion by SOHN, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree is reversed, and the record is remanded with direction to enter an appropriate decree enjoining defendants therein from further proceeding in the Commission's inquiry and investigation. Each party to pay its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Pennsylvania, which dismissed the railroad's complaint against appellees, Public Utility Commission and others, in which the railroad sought to enjoin the Commission's inquiry and investigation to determine whether the railroad was violating §§ 3, 9, and 10 of the Full Crew Act of June 1, 1937, P.L. 1120, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 67, § 461a et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Act had been declared unconstitutional. Sixteen years later, the Attorney General filed a bill of review to amend or modify the final decree declaring that the Act was unconstitutional and restraining the enforcement of the entire Act against the railroad on the ground that only those sections of the Act at issue in the prior proceeding should have been declared unconstitutional rather than the entire Act. The court discharged the bill without prejudice to the right of the Attorney General to proceed through the Commission for the enforcement of §§ 3, 9, and 10 of the Act nor to the right of the railroad to plead any and all defenses. The Commission instituted the inquiry and investigation at issue in the case at bar. On appeal, the court determined that its ruling on the Attorney General's bill was misunderstood by the lower court in that the court did not intend to declare or intimate that §§ 3, 9, and 10 had survived the earlier ruling that the Act was unconstitutional but that the Attorney General had the right to test the enforceability of those sections by proceedings before the Commission. The court found that those sections were not severable and were invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decree, and remanded the record with direction to enter an appropriate decree enjoining appellees from further proceeding in the Commission's inquiry and investigation.

 

372 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Universal Trades


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. 323; 141 A.2d 204; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 461


Argued November 20, 1957  
March 17, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 19, May T., 1957, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1954, Commonwealth Docket No. 154, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Universal Trades, Inc. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused May 23, 1958.

Appeal by taxpayer from determination of capital stock tax by state taxing officials. Before RICHARDS, P.J. and NEELY, SOHN and KREIDER, JJ.

Adjudication filed dismissing appeal; defendant's exceptions dismissed and judgment entered, opinion by RICHARDS, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which allowed appellee state to impose a capital stock tax based in part upon intangible assets which were located outside the state.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a domestic corporation with a registered office in the state and its principal office in Florida. The taxpayer's business engaged exclusively in construction work outside the United States. All of its contracts were negotiated and effected by its officers working out of the Florida office, and the taxpayer exercised complete jurisdiction, control, supervision, and management of its assets and business at its Florida office. Regardless, the trial court allowed the state to impose a capital stock tax against the taxpayer based in part by intangible assets located outside the state. The taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed the judgment. There was no constitutional rule of immunity from taxation of intangibles by more than one state. The fact that the intangible property at issue acquired a commercial or business situs in Florida did not bar the state's power to impose a capital stock tax. Since the taxpayer was incorporated in the state, the state gave the taxpayer its existence and defined its powers. Thus, the state's laws governed the taxpayer and under that law, the situs of intangible property for taxation was the taxpayer's domicile.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment allowing the state to impose a capital stock tax against the taxpayer based in part on intangible assets located outside the state.

Girard College Trusteeship


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. 434; 138 A.2d 844; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 535


Argued November 21, 1957  
January 24, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 109 to 121, inclusive, Jan. T., 1958, from decrees of the Orphans' Court of Philadelphia County, July T., 1885, No. 10, in re estate of Stephen Girard, deceased. Decrees affirmed; reargument refused February 12, 1958.

Cause remanded to Orphans' Court by Supreme Court of Pennsylvania for proceedings not inconsistent with opinion of Supreme Court of the United States.

Adjudication and decrees filed dismissing applicants' petitions for admission to Girard College, removing trustee effective upon appointment of substituted trustees, and directing an accounting; petitions for reconsideration, vacation or modification of decrees denied and final decrees entered; before KLEIN, P.J., BOLGER, HUNTER, LEFEVER, SAYLOR and SHOYER, JJ., opinion by KLEIN, P.J. Commonwealth, City and applicants appealed.
Pennsylvania v. Bd. of Dir. of City Trusts, 353 U.S. 230, 77 S. Ct. 806, 1 L. Ed. 2d 792, 1957 U.S. LEXIS 1001 (1957)



DISPOSITION: The decrees are affirmed at the cost of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the City of Philadelphia.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the Orphans' Court (Pennsylvania), which, on remand from the supreme court, vacated its prior judgment denying admission of two minor orphan Negro applicants to a school established by a benefactor's will, and, instead, appointed new, private trustees who could legally administer the trust pursuant to the benefactor's wishes. The city contended that it was denied procedural due process.


OVERVIEW: A testamentary benefactor had established a trust for the financing of a school for "white orphan boys." The trust had been administered by the city for over 100 years at the time two orphan Negro boys made application for admission to the school. The decision not to admit the boys as violative of the trustor's intent was reversed by the Supreme Court of the United States as violative of the Fourteenth Amendment right to equal protection, because the decision had been made by a government entity. On remand to the orphans' court, the court ordered the removal of the city trustees and substituted a board of private individuals for administration of the trust. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the orphans' court had found a satisfactory solution because there was nothing in the testator's will or in any legislation by the commonwealth or the city that served to make the school a public charity or that required it to be publicly administered. Thus, the board of private trustees could refuse admittance to the boys without violating the Fourteenth Amendment because there was no government action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the orphans' court appointing new trustees to administer the testator's trust.

Wright Estate


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. 405; 138 A.2d 102; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 534


Argued June 3, 1957  
January 22, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 254, 255 and 279, Jan. T., 1957, from the decree of Orphans' Court of Clearfield County, estate No. 21090, in re estate of Abram K. Wright, deceased. Decree, as modified, affirmed.

Proceedings upon exceptions of legatees to decision of auditor dismissing exceptions to his report.

Adjudication entered confirming report of auditor, exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered, opinion by MCKENRICK, P.J., specially presiding. Legatees appealed.



DISPOSITION: I would affirm the decree of the Orphans' Court of Clearfield County as to No. 279, which imposed the Pennsylvania Inheritance tax on each legatee, and reverse the decree as to Nos. 254 and 255, which held that all of the Federal Estate tax should be borne by the residuary legatees (the charities).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Residuary legatees, two charities, pre-residuary legatees, and individuals, appealed from the decree of the Orphans' Court of Clearfield County (Pennsylvania), which confirmed an auditor's report that imposed state inheritance tax on all of the legatees but imposed federal estate taxes only on the residuary legatees.


OVERVIEW: The pre-residuary legatees were a number of individuals, including a long-time secretary to the decedent, that the decedent's will left specific bequests of cash and stock to. The residual legatees, two charities, were left the residual of the decedent's estate. The trial court affirmed an auditor's conclusion that all of the legatees would bear deduction for state inheritance taxes, but only the residuary legatees would bear the federal estate tax burden. On appeal by the pre-residuary and the residuary legatees, the court modified the decree of the trial court. The court found that the testator's intent, as expressed in his will, overcame the presumption that state inheritance taxes would be borne by each of the legatees. The court found that his specific bequests exhibited his desire that the pre-residuary legatees not bear any deduction for state inheritance taxes . Likewise, the court found that the testator intended that the specific bequests to the pre-residuary legatees be without any deduction for federal estate taxes, as provided in the Estate Tax Apportionment Act of 1951, 1951 Pa. Laws 1405.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decree of the trial court so that the residual estate would be charged with the state inheritance taxes, and as so modified, affirmed.

Hertrick Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. 148; 137 A.2d 310; 1958 Pa. LEXIS 508


Argued October 8, 1957  
January 6, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 168, March T., 1957, from order of County Court of Allegheny County, 1956, No. A 1916, in re appeal of Theodore Hertrick, Secretary and W. J. Dunbar, Building Inspector of the Borough of Greentree. Order affirmed.

Appeal by borough from decision of zoning board of adjustment granting building permit. Before KAUFMAN, J.

Order entered sustaining the decision of the zoning board of adjustment and directing that building permit be issued. Borough appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borough sought review of the order of the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) directing the building inspector to issue to appellee applicant a building permit for a gas station, thus sustaining the decision of the zoning board of adjustment to issue the permit.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a building permit for a gas station under an ordinance that required the consent of the majority of owners of property within 100 feet. Two of three owners within 100 feet of the main building consented. Within 100 feet of the perimeter of the parcel, there were seven owners. The inspector refused the application. The board of adjustment granted the permit. The county court sustained the board's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. While the appeal was pending, the zoning ordinance was amended to require the consent of 80 per cent of the owners. The court held that the amendment did not upgrade the use to which the land could be put, but merely changed the procedure necessary to obtain a building permit. Thus, it did not affect the pending application. The distance within which property owners' consents were required was to be measured from the main structure, rather than the perimeter of the area of the installation. Thus, the applicant had obtained the consent of the requisite number of property owners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the county court sustaining the decision of the zoning board of adjustment and directing that a building permit be issued to the applicant for the construction of a gas station, over the objection of the borough.

Parente Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


390 Pa. 249; 135 A.2d 62; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 285


Argued September 30, 1957  
October 7, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 239, March T., 1957, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Apr. T., 1957, No. 520, in re decision of County Election Board. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon appeal from decision of county election board refusing to cumulate write-in ballots.

Order entered sustaining the appeal and directing that write-in ballots be cumulated; exceptions dismissed and final order entered, before LAIRD, P.J., O'CONNELL, J. and COPELAND, P.J., specially presiding, opinion by LAIRD, P.J., O'CONNELL, J., dissenting. Defeated candidate appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his exceptions to an order requiring that certain write-in votes cast in a local primary election be cumulated and adopted the opinion and decree of the hearing judge as its final order.


OVERVIEW: A primary election was held for the mayor's office for a certain city. No candidates for the office were placed on the Republican ticket. Accordingly, an extensive write-in campaign was conducted to obtain a candidate. Appellant and appellee were the principal contenders for the nomination following the write-in campaign. Appellee duly requested that the county election board cumulate all of the votes cast in his name as written in on the voting machines and to declare him the Republican nominee. The board credited the two candidates with only such votes as were written in with their full names. As a result, appellant was certified as the Republican nominee. However, the trial court ordered that all of the write-in votes be cumulated and, as a result, appellee was certified as the nominee. The trial court's order was adopted by the trial court en banc. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the trial court had the authority under the Election Code of June 3, 1937, P.L. 1333 to order that all of the write-in votes be cumulated in order to effectuate the will of the voters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

L. J. W. Realty Corp. v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


390 Pa. 197; 134 A.2d 878; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 280


Argued April 23, 1957  
September 30, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 218, 225, 222, Jan. T., 1957, from orders of Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1956, No. 6485; Court of Common Pleas No. 4, June T., 1956, No. 7828, transferred to Court of Common Pleas No. 7; Court of Common Pleas No. 2, June T., 1956, No. 7787, transferred to Court of Common Pleas No. 7, in cases of L.J.W. Realty Corp. v. City of Philadelphia; Tax Review Board v. Lit Brothers, Inc.; and Tax Review Board v. American Stores Company. Judgments affirmed.

Appeals to court of common pleas by taxpayers from decisions of Tax Review Board sustaining decisions of Revenue Commissioner refusing claims for refunds.

Judgments entered sustaining decisions of Board. Plaintiffs, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxpayers, sought review from orders entered in the Court of Common Pleas No. 7 for Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that sustained decisions of the Tax Review Board that sustained decisions of appellee revenue commissioner that refused the taxpayers' claims for refunds for taxes imposed on them by the Sterling Act, Act of August 5, 1932, P.L. 45, § 1, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 4613.


OVERVIEW: The lower court upheld a local ordinance enacted pursuant to the Sterling Act and denied the taxpayers' claims for refunds for taxes paid to record certain documents that transferred real estate. On appeal, the taxpayers argued that the tax imposed by the Sterling Act was invalid because it constituted a duplication of existing state taxes imposed pursuant to the Act of April 6, 1830, P.L. 272, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 3171. The court rejected this argument and noted that the tax imposed in this case was not imposed on a transaction but was imposed on the presentation of a document for recording. Thus, it was not a duplication of an existing state tax. The court also noted that the State Realty Transfer Act of December 27, 1951, P.L. 1742, as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 3283-3292 did not prohibit the tax imposed in this situation, as this act contained an exception for local ordinances that imposed taxes like the one in this case. The court found that the State Realty Transfer Act did not violate Pa. Const., art. III, § 6, as the constitution did not require every act recite all other acts that its operation might incidentally affect by repeal, modification or extension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the lower court.

Grote Trust


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


390 Pa. 261; 135 A.2d 383; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 288

September 30, 1957

Audit of account of surviving trustee. Before BOYLE, P.J.

Adjudication filed holding trust had terminated and claimants had released their rights to require an accounting; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered, before BOYLE, P.J., COX and RAHAUSER, JJ., opinion by BOYLE, P.J. Successor trustee and exceptants, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree dismissing the exceptions to the account of the Executors of Frederick C. Grote, deceased, filed for the deceased as Surviving Trustee under the trust indenture of Conrad H. Grote and his wife, dated October 29, 1917, and confirming said account, is modified by striking therefrom so much thereof as (1) terminated the trust, (2) directed distribution to Dorothy Grote Voss, Meta Christine Grote Uber, and Union National Bank, Guardian for Esther Grote Siegert, an incompetent, as the remaindermen, of the corpus of the trust estate, and (3) revoked the appointment of Potter Bank and Trust [***2] Company as Successor Trustee under the said trust indenture. As so modified, the decree is affirmed and the record remanded to the Court below for further proceedings consonant with this opinion; each party to pay their respective costs, except that the cost of printing the record shall be equally apportioned among the appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, successor trustee and exceptants, sought review of a decision of Orphans' Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which held that a trust had terminated and that claimants had released their rights to require an accounting. The lower court had dismissed exceptions to adjudication and entered a final decree.


OVERVIEW: This case involved a trust indenture in which a husband and wife conveyed 19 parcels of real estate to their three sons, as trustees, for the purposes set forth in the trust indenture. In this case, the court held that all the individual claimants, grandchildren, were barred from all claims for further accounting and for surcharge by estoppel, waiver and laches. The court held that the successor trustee was barred by laches. The court held that the exceptions and claims for surcharges were properly dismissed by the lower court. However, the court held that the lower Court was in error in holding that a resigned trustee's sale of his right to future spendthrift trust income created an acceleration of the remainder interests and justified a termination of the trust estate. The court held that the rights of the great grandchildren, which were clearly and specifically given them in the trust indenture of 1917, could not possibly be extinguished or altered by a resigned trustee's sale in 1940 of his share of future spendthrift trust income.


OUTCOME: The court held that the exceptions and claims for surcharges were properly dismissed by the lower court. The court also held that the lower court was in error in holding that a resigned trustee's sale of his right to future spendthrift trust income created an acceleration of the remainder interests and justified a termination of the trust estate.

Pittsburgh Outdoor Advertising Co. v. Clairton


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


390 Pa. 1; 133 A.2d 542; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 257


Argued May 27, 1957  
June 28, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 180, March T., 1957, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Oct. T., 1954, No. 1676, in case of Pittsburgh Outdoor Advertising Company v. City of Clairton. Order reversed.

Equity.

Order entered refusing defendant's motion to dismiss, opinion by O'BRIEN, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and bill dismissed at the appellee's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied the city's motion to dismiss an action filed by appellee advertising company, which alleged that City of Clairton, Pa., Zoning Ordinance 654 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The advertising company had signboards erected on properties within the city prior to enactment of City of Clairton, Pa., Zoning Ordinance 654, § 1507-2-7(a) (July 21, 1948). The ordinance required removal of signboards other than those bearing the name of the person, firm, or corporation operating the enterprise and a general description of the enterprise within five years of the date of the ordinance. The city solicitor sent a letter to the advertising company seeking compliance with the ordinance. The advertising company then filed a bill in equity, alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The advertising company sought an injunction restraining enforcement of the ordinance. The city filed a motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court reversed and dismissed the bill. The court held that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the advertising company's action was one challenging the constitutionality of a zoning ordinance. The court explained that the zoning ordinance provided an adequate statutory remedy, and, therefore, a bill in equity raising the same question could not lie.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied the city's motion to dismiss the advertising company's bill against it for the declaration that a zoning ordinance was unconstitutional, and dismissed the bill.

381 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Progress Mfg. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


389 Pa. 600; 133 A.2d 814; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 406


Argued May 28, 1957  
June 28, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 26, May T., 1957, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket No. 180, 1955, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Progress Manufacturing Company, Inc. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused August 1, 1957.

Appeal by taxpayer from decision of the Board of Finance and Revenue refusing to review its action resettling and increasing taxpayer's capital stock tax. Before NEELY, J. without a jury.

Adjudication filed finding for Commonwealth; defendant's exceptions to adjudication overruled and final judgment entered. Opinion by RICHARDS, P.J. Defendant appealed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer requested review from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket (Pennsylvania) that affirmed an adjudication of a resettlement of the taxpayer's capital stock tax.


OVERVIEW: The department of revenue accepted the taxpayer's capital stock report and settled the capital stock tax based on the report. However, the department later found the stock's value to be higher and resettled the tax for a higher amount. The taxpayer contended that that § 1105 of the Fiscal Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 1105 (1929) improperly delegated legislative power. The taxpayer also contended that granting that the department had the right to make a resettlement, it could not have increased the tax except for clerical or mathematical errors, unless it has in its possession accounts and information which it did not have at the time of the original settlement. The court held that § 1105 did not delegate legislative power, it assigned administrative duties. The court stated that the valuation of the property to be taxed was left, of necessity, to the administrative officers. The court also stated that as the fixing of the original assessment could not be regarded as the performance of a legislative function, so also the re-assessment could not be so designated. The court also held that the commonwealth reserved for two years the unlimited right to resettle the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Cano


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


389 Pa. 639; 133 A.2d 800; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 414


Submitted June 4, 1957  
June 28, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 26 and 27, Jan. T., 1958, from judgments of Superior Court, Appeals, Nos. 52 and 53 Oct. T., 1957, affirming judgments of sentence of Court of Quarter Sessions of Schuylkill County, Sept. T., 1953, No. 553, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Aurelio Cano et al. Judgments affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 182 Pa.Super.Ct. 524.

Proceedings upon informations charging violations of the Anthracite Mine Law. Before DALTON, J.

Demurrer sustained as to corporate defendant; verdicts of guilty as to some counts and not guilty as to others; defendants' motions for new trial refused as to all counts, but motion in arrest of judgment sustained on one count; judgments of sentence entered on remaining counts. Defendants appealed to the Superior Court which affirmed the judgments of the court below. Appeal by defendants to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of the Superior Court affirming the judgments and sentences of the Quarter Sessions of Schuylkill County, are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the decision of a Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed defendants' convictions for violations of the Anthracite Mine Law. Defendants were charged and tried under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 52, § 511, for having been negligently guilty of an offense against the provisions of this act, whereby a dangerous accident had resulted or might have resulted to any person or persons employed in such mine.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution arose out of an occurrence in defendants' mine, in which five miners lost their lives. Defendants contended that the procedure that was followed, which included the filing of an affidavit and the issuance of a warrant, violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 10. This provision stated that no person, for any indictable offense, could have been proceeded against criminally by information. Defendants alleged that the absence of a bill of indictment by the grand jury rendered the statutory procedure invalid. The court rejected defendants' contention that the charges against them, in the absence of the statute, would have been indictable as common law offenses. The court held that the offenses charged did not offend against the public peace, morals, or economy, or the due regulation and domestic order of the Commonwealth. Although the legislature regulated the business of mining for the safety of miners, it was only by virtue of the statute that the failure to act in accordance therewith was made a punishable offense. The fact that the legislature declared the violations to have been misdemeanors, did not make them indictable offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

383 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Thompson


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


389 Pa. 382; 133 A.2d 207; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 382


Argued April 25, 1957  
June 6, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 124, March T., 1957, from judgment and sentence of Court of Oyer and Terminer of Allegheny County, Nov. T., 1949, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Cleveland Thompson. Judgment and sentence affirmed.

Indictment charging defendant with murder. Before SOHN, J., specially presiding.

Verdict of guilty, with penalty fixed at death, and judgment of sentence entered thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed and the record is remitted to the court below for the purpose of execution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and sentence of Court of Oyer and Terminer of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied defendant's motion for a new trial after he was found guilty of murder in the first degree with the death penalty affixed.


OVERVIEW: Witnesses testified that defendant shot and killed a bartender during a robbery. Defendant claimed that the bartender, who had a gun, attacked him and that if he shot the gun, it was in self-defense. Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree and sentenced to death. The court affirmed and determined that the jury was properly instructed both on self-defense and voluntary manslaughter. There was no evidence produced at trial to show that defendant was placed in any fear or that he shot the victim while under the influence of such fear, and therefore the trial court was not required to instruct the jury on this issue. Evidence of prior offenses committed by defendant, including his court-martial record, were admissible to enable the jury to decide what penalty was appropriate for defendant. The court had no authority to inquire into or review defendant's court-martial record, which was res judicata and conclusive on the court. Defendant's conviction of three separate offenses of violence was properly admitted into evidence. Even if erroneous, the introduction of this evidence was harmless where defendant had testified that he shot three soldiers while in military service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree with the death penalty affixed.

 

384 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Archbishop O'Hara's Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


389 Pa. 35; 131 A.2d 587; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 337


Argued January 14, 1957  
April 26, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 118, Jan. T., 1957, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Nov. T., 1954, No. 28, in the matter of the appeal of His Excellency, Most Reverend John F. O'Hara, C.S.C., Archbishop of Philadelphia. Order reversed.

Appeal by applicant from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing special exception to use premises for school purposes. Before DANNEHOWER, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal; exceptions to findings and order dismissed in part and final order entered. Applicant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed. Costs are placed on the appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant archbishop sought relief from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which denied his application to build a school on the property he owned, contending that the local ordinance that the denial was based on was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant archbishop's application to build a school on land that he owned pursuant to a local ordinance, which stated that educational, religious, or philanthropic use by and with the consent of the board, was denied by a hearing judge, and affirmed by the lower court. The court held that any traffic increase with its attendant noise, dirt, danger and hazards was unpleasant, yet, such increase was one of the inevitable accompaniments of suburban progress and of the constantly expanding population which, standing alone, did not constitute a sufficient reason to refuse a property owner the legitimate use of his land, and there was nothing in the contemplated use of that site of land by appellant that would depreciate or change the character of the neighborhood anymore than would the establishment of any other school, church or philanthropic institution in the district. The court noted that any use of the site would affect, consequently, the township, in that it would require the widening of streets, and the fact that appellant owned another site that in the lower court's opinion was more suitable was irrelevant, thus, the judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision because the denial of appellant archbishop's application would be an unnecessary, unwarranted, and unreasonable intermeddling with appellant's ownership of the property under the label of the preservation of the health and safety of the community.

 

385 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Dauphin Deposit Trust Co. v. Myers


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


388 Pa. 444; 130 A.2d 686; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 465


Argued January 14, 1957  
March 29, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 21, May T., 1957 from order of Secretary of Banking and Department of Banking of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, dated September 12, 1956, disapproving merger of banking institutions. Order reversed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed. The Department of Banking is directed to approve the Articles of Merger and promptly notify the Department of State of its action approving said articles.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, banking institutions in contiguous counties, challenged the order of Secretary of Banking and Department of Banking of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania that disapproved the proposed merger of appellants, stating that there was no need for a merger since the banking facilities and services in one of the counties were adequate, and the merger would result in over-banking which would be detrimental and possibly disastrous to the community.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were banking institutions in contiguous counties. Articles of Merger were filed by appellants and approved by the Department of State. The Articles were transmitted to the Department of Banking (Department) for approval or disapproval. One of the appellants had its principal and sole place of business in one county. The other appellant had its principal place of business, together with three branches, in another county. Appellants challenged the order that disapproved the proposed merger stating that there was no need for a merger since the banking facilities and services in one of the counties were adequate, and a merger would result in over-banking and would be detrimental to the community. On appeal, the court examined the Act of December 30, 1955, Pa. Laws 920, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 7, § 819-204.1, which repealed an earlier act; specifically, the court looked at § 204.1 A and B. Department misinterpreted § 204.1 A. Yet, the appeal, pursuant to 7 P.S. § 819-1406 C, was permissible only in the nature of a narrow certiorari; the proceedings by Department were regular and it had jurisdiction. Still the order was reversed due to an exercise of excess of powers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and directed the Department of Banking to approve the Articles of Merger and notify the Department of State of its action because the court was not precluded from reversing an order of an administrative agency where an excess of powers, powers beyond those granted or possessed, was exercised by such an agency, like in the case here.
