Land Holding Corp. v. Board of Finance & Revenue


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


388 Pa. 61; 130 A.2d 700; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 421


Argued November 13, 1956  
March 18, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 18, May T., 1957, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket 1955, No. 226, in case of Land Holding Corporation v. Board of Finance and Revenue. Order affirmed.

Mandamus.

Order entered sustaining defendant's preliminary objections and granting judgment for defendant, opinion by SOHN, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grantee of deed challenged an order by the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) that sustained respondent board of finance and revenue's (board) preliminary objections and granted judgment for the board in an action by the grantee seeking a refund of the taxes paid.


OVERVIEW: The grantee deeded certain property to the grantor. However, when the deed was presented for recording, the deed was refused on the ground that the deed required stamps under The Realty Transfer Tax Act of December 27, 1951, P.L. 1742, as amended by the Act of May 29, 1953, P.L. 257. The grantee paid the taxes under protest and filed a request for a refund with the board. The request was denied by the board, and the grantee filed a complaint in mandamus contending that there was no tax due on the transaction and the retention of the tax was unconstitutional. The court stated that the action of the board could not be reviewed unless the board had acted fraudulently, arbitrarily or in excess of the powers and duties vested in it. It was not claimed that the board acted fraudulently, and it could not be said that the board acted arbitrarily or beyond the powers and duties conferred upon it. Therefore, the action was properly found not subject to review by mandamus.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

387 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Stotesbury Estate


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


387 Pa. 591; 128 A.2d 587; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 494


Argued November 21, 1956  
January 24, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 85, Jan. T., 1957, from decree of Orphans' Court of Montgomery County, May T., 1956, No. 44897, in re Estate of Edward T. Stotesbury, deceased. Decree reversed.

Proceeding upon petition for review of adjudication of account previously confirmed.

Final decree entered dismissing petition, opinion by TAXIS, P.J. Petitioners appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed and record remanded with directions that the petition be reinstated and a decree entered granting the review prayed for; costs on the appeal to be borne by the trust estates equally.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, life beneficiaries, sought review of a decree entered in the Orphans' Court, Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their petition for review of an adjudication and schedule of distribution previously confirmed by the trial court. Appellees, a guardian and trustee ad litem, denied the beneficiaries had the right of the review sought. The beneficiaries claimed that the trial court erred in dismissing their petition.


OVERVIEW: The beneficiaries claimed that since the time the schedule of distribution had been entered they learned that stock dividends, stock exchanges, and stock rights, which were included in the principal account, was an error of law and that the same should have been apportioned and included in income rather than in principal. The trial court refused the review because it deemed unmeritorious the reason offered by the beneficiaries for not having raised at the time of the audit their right to apportionment as income the receipts in question. The court reversed. The right of any party in interest to a review of a fiduciary's account, auditor's report, adjudication, or decree of distribution within five years after the final confirmation of the account was allowed by § 721 of the Fiduciaries Act of 1949, P.L. 512, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 20, § 320.721. The petition was filed within the five-year time limitation. No part of the property erroneously allocated in the account to principal had been distributed. The action of the trial court was in disregard of the plain intent of the Fiduciaries Act and constituted a manifest abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the record was remanded with directions that the petition be reinstated and a decree entered that granted the review prayed for.

 

388 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Landau Advertising Co. v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


387 Pa. 552; 128 A.2d 559; 1957 Pa. LEXIS 491


Argued November 14, 1956  
January 17, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 215, Jan. T., 1956, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1954, No. 7540, in case of Landau Advertising Co., Inc. v. Zoning Board of Adjustment. Order reversed.

Appeal by applicant from decision of Zoning Board of Adjustment refusing permit for advertising sign.

Order entered directing permit to issue, opinion by KUN, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee advertiser applied for a permit to erect a billboard on leased premises. Appellant Zoning Board of Adjustment (board) denied the request. The advertiser then filed an action in the Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) which, without taking additional testimony reversed the action of the board. The board appealed and the city was substituted as appellant.


OVERVIEW: The city alleged that the erection of a billboard on leased premises was not an accessory use and was not permitted by the zoning ordinance. The advertiser alleged that its billboard was an accessory use and that a refusal to permit such a sign by a lessee was a restriction that bore no substantial relation to public health, safety, morals, or general welfare and was unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The only signs expressly permitted by the zoning ordinance were those specifically enumerated or those that could have been classified as an accessory use. A billboard devoted to general advertising without reference to the businesses situated in the immediate community was not an accessory use. The contemplated use of the leased premises bore no relationship to the occupancy of the building on the subject premises, was not one incidental to the operation of the business and was, therefore, forbidden by the ordinance. There was no illegal discrimination in the ordinance. The unique nature of outdoor advertising justified the separate classification of such structures for the purposes of governmental regulation and restriction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which reversed the action of the board denying a permit to the advertiser, was reversed.

 

389 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Robinson Twp. Sch. Dist. v. Houghton


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


387 Pa. 236; 128 A.2d 58; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 349


Argued October 3, 1956  
December 29, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 127, March T., 1956, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1955, No. 605, in case of School District of Robinson Township v. Vernon Houghton and Ola Gordon, individually and as trustees ad litem for the Taxpayers' League of Robinson Township. Order of supersedeas vacated and appeal quashed.

Proceeding upon petition for declaratory judgment upon case stated.

Order entered finding transportation of non-public school children in public school buses ultra vires, before MARSHALL, MONTGOMERY and LEWIS, JJ., opinion by MARSHALL, J., concurring opinion by LEWIS, J.; petition to intervene on behalf of non-public school children granted. Intervenors appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of supersedeas is vacated and the appeal quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which held that respondent school district was without power, discretionary or otherwise, to transport non-public school pupils in public school buses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant intervened on behalf of non-public school children and asserted that the school board possessed discretionary power to permit non-public school pupils to be transported in public school buses. The court determined that Pa. Const. art. X, § 2, which provided that no money raised for the support of the public schools of the commonwealth could have been appropriated to or used for the support of any sectarian school, was a negative restraint and not a positive authorization to anyone to do anything. The court explained that whether a school district's transportation of non-public school pupils to and from its public school in public school buses would have constituted a violation of art. X, § 2 could not have properly come before the court until the legislature authorized or permitted such a practice. The court concluded that, in any event, the appeal had to be quashed because appellant lacked standing to appeal. The court explained that the litigation initiated by the declaratory judgment petition was conclusively determined by the lower court and a final judgment entered therein before the petition for intervention was ever filed, so intervention was no longer allowable.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the appeal of the order of the trial court, which held that the school district was without power, discretionary or otherwise, to transport non-public school pupils in public school buses. The court vacated the order of supersedeas.

Janney v. Philadelphia Transp. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


387 Pa. 282; 128 A.2d 76; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 354


Argued November 15, 1956  
December 29, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, no. 251, Jan. T., 1956, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1955, No. 7561, in case of Joseph N. Janney v. Philadelphia Transportation Company et al. Decree affirmed; reargument refused January 18, 1957.

Declaratory judgment proceeding.

Final decree entered finding Acts permitting stagered elections of corporate directors constitutional, opinion by OLIVER, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree is affirmed at the cost od appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff stockholder appealed a decree from the Court of Common Pleas No. 7 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which declared that 1887 Pa. Laws 411, § 1 and defendant company's by-laws were not in conflict with, nor in violation of, Pa. Const. art. XVI, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The sole question presented on review was whether the right granted by statute to classify corporate directors and stagger their terms violated the right conferred by the state constitution upon the stockholders to cumulate their votes in all elections for directors. The stockholder contended that the company's by-law and § 1 of 1887 Pa. Laws 411, by which it was authorized, were invalid because they conflicted with the state constitution. The decree was affirmed. The court concluded that constitution granted the right of cumulative voting, but it did not purport to insure the maximum effectiveness of the exercise of that right to obtain minority representation on the board of directors. The constitution was silent as to how many candidates there should be at the election, whether they must consist of all the directors of the corporation, or whether they could not be classified and their elections staggered. The court concluded that to write into the constitution any such limiting or qualifying provisions as contended for by the stockholder would be an extreme exercise of judicial legislation.


OUTCOME: The decree declaring that the company's by-law was not in conflict with the state constitution was affirmed.

 

391 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


387 Pa. 362; 127 A.2d 703; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 363


Argued November 27, 1956  
December 10, 1956; December 29, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 131, Jan. T., 1957, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1955, No. 7857, in case of John Warren et al. v. City of Philadelphia. Decree affirmed; reargument refused December 29, 1956.

Bill in Equity. Before ALESSANDRONI, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding rent control ordinance invalid; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The final order heretofore entered on the above appeal is confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a decree of the Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which found in favor of plaintiff taxpayers in their action to find invalid a rent control ordinance enacted by the city.


OVERVIEW: The city had imposed temporary controls over rents and evictions in rental housing and when it expired, the city extended the imposition of the controls. The taxpayers claimed that no emergency existed that would have justified the imposition of the ordinance. The court agreed and affirmed the decree that adjudged the amended ordinance invalid, arbitrary, and void and restrained its enforcement. The court held that a law that purported to be an exercise of a city's police power must not have been unreasonable, unduly oppressive, or patently beyond the necessities of the case. In addition, the means employed must have had a real and substantial relation to the objects sought to have been attained. The court stated that a city did have the power to control rents and evictions by ordinance when an emergency existed. The question was whether such emergency existed. The court found that the evidence presented at trial was credible and that it showed that there was no emergency that would have justified the enactment of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the final order.

In re Appeal of Obradovich


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 342; 126 A.2d 435; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 397


Argued September 24, 1956  
November 12, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 128, March T., 1956, from decision of Superior Court, April T., 1955, No. 169, affirming order of County Court of Allegheny County, 1955, No. C-343, in re: appeal of Louis Obradovich, from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board. Order reversed.

Same case in Superior Court: 180 Pa. Superior Ct. 383.

Appeal by applicant from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board refusing transfer of liquor license. Before KAUFMAN, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal; exceptions to order dismissed and final order entered, before LENCHER, P.J., BROWN and KAUFMAN, JJ., opinion by KAUFMAN, J. Applicant appealed to the Superior Court, which affirmed the order of the court below. Appeal by applicant to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Superior Court affirming the order of the County Court of Allegheny County is reversed, and it is directed that the Liquor Control Board approve appellant's transfer application; each party to bear his, its, or their own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant challenged the affirmance by the Superior Court, April Term (Pennsylvania) of an order by the county court that sustained a decision of appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board refusing to transfer a liquor license and dismissed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The applicant applied to the Board for the transfer to him of a restaurant liquor licensed owned by two individuals. The Board found that the applicant was a reputable person and the establishment met the requirements prescribed by law, but refused the application. The county sustained the action, and the trial court affirmed. The court granted the applicant's petition for the allowance of an appeal. The court reversed and directed the Board to approve the transfer application. The court reasoned that the Board did not have discretion to refuse the application based on protests by the neighbors. The Board was only entitled to refuse an application based on grounds embraced in § 404 of the Liquor Code of April 12, 1951, P.L. 90. The only matters to have been considered by the Board were the fitness of the application, whether he alone was pecuniarily interested, and whether the premises met the requirements of the Code. The court also determined that the Board was not vested with a greater measure of discretion in the case of an application for the transfer of a liquor license than it possessed in the case of the original issuance of such a license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and directed the Board to approve the applicant's transfer application.

Knup v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 350; 126 A.2d 399; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 398


Argued October 1, 1956  
November 12, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 258, Jan. T., 1956, from final decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1955, No. 6090, in case of Jacob Knup, Jr. et al. v. City of Philadelphia et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity.

Defendants' preliminary objections sustained and decree entered dismissing complaint, opinion by REIMEL, J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree is affirmed at appellants' costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of the decree from Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the objections of defendant City of Philadelphia and dismissed the property owners' complaint in equity on the ground of lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The property owners instituted an action, seeking to enjoin the City from issuing any permit under a city ordinance that rezoned an adjoining tract of land to allow the erection of apartment buildings. The property owners alleged that the ordinance was invalid because the construction of an apartment building would create a nuisance, would aggravate traffic congestion and overcrowding, and because the ordinance was not enacted by the vote of three-fourths of the city council. The trial court dismissed the complaint for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision, holding that the proper procedure for challenging the validity of the zoning ordinance was to await an application for a permit and then file a complaint with the zoning board. An appeal to the court could then be had. Because the remedy provided in 1806 Pa. Laws § 13 was the exclusive remedy, and it had to be strictly followed, the court dismissed the complaint. Moreover, the court found that the property owners had no standing to pursue their claim because their rights had not been affected by the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the property owners' complaint.

Schade v. Allegheny County Institution Dist.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 507; 126 A.2d 911; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 419


Argued September 27, 1956  
November 12, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 28, March T., 1956, from final decree of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Jan. T., 1952, No. 1171, in case of Fred A. Schade et al. v. Allegheny County Institution District et al. Decree affirmed; reargument refused December 5, 1956.

Equity. Before THOMPSON, J.

Adjudication filed enjoining county institution district from making payments out of appropriations to charitable and religious institutions for support and maintenance of dependent children; exceptions to adjudication sustained in part and decree entered dismissing bill, before THOMPSON, ELLENBOGEN and KENNEDY, JJ., opinion by ELLENBOGEN, J., concurring opinion by KENNEDY, J., dissenting opinion by THOMPSON, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at appellant's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which found in favor of appellees, commissioners of Allegheny County and institution district, in the taxpayer's action to enjoin the commissioners from paying out funds of the institution district for the support, care and maintenance of delinquent children placed in sectarian or denominational homes and institutions.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers brought a suit against the commissioners, seeking to enjoin the commissioners from paying out funds to the institution district for the support, care, and maintenance of delinquent, neglected, or dependent children placed in sectarian or denominational homes. The taxpayers alleged that the paying of funds was unconstitutional under Penn. Const. art. III, § 18, which prohibited appropriations for charitable purposes or to any denominational or sectarian institution. The trial court entered a decree enjoining the institution district from paying the sectarian and denominational institutions, and enjoining each institution from receiving payment from the institution district. An appellate court reversed the trial court's decision, and one taxpayer sought review. On appeal, the court held that payments made by the institution district for the support and maintenance of neglected or dependent children were not appropriations within the meaning of that term as employed in § 18. The court affirmed the appellate court's holding and found that the payments by the institution district to the sectarian homes did not violate the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's holding, which held that the commissioner's actions in paying of funds to the institution district for the support of children in sectarian homes were not unconstitutional.

In re Girard Will Case


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 548; 127 A.2d 287; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 425


Argued April 26, 1956  
November 12, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by, Sub nomine at Pennsylvania v. Bd. of Dir. of City Trusts, 353 U.S. 230, 1 L. Ed. 2d 792, 77 S. Ct. 806, 1957 U.S. LEXIS 1001 (1957)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 167, 168, 175, 176, 177, 178, 179, 180, 202 and 203, Jan. T., 1956, from decrees of Orphans' Court of Philadelphia County, July T., 1885, No. 10, in re estate of Stephen Girard, deceased. Decrees affirmed; reargument refused December 20, 1956.

Proceeding upon petitions of rejected applicants and City for citation upon Board of City Trusts to show cause why applicants should not be admitted to Girard College. Before BOLGER, J.

Adjudication filed denying admission to applicants; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered, opinion by LEFEVER, J. Applicants, City and Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decrees affirmed, each of the parties to bear his or its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city, state, and two black applicants (city), filed petitions for a citation on appellee board of directors (board) to show cause why the applicants were not admitted to a college established under the decedent's will for white orphans. The city sought review of the order of the Orphans' Court of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the board's refusal of the applications and dismissed the city's petitions.


OVERVIEW: Decedent's will made a devise and bequest to a city for the erection of a college for the benefit of poor, male, white, orphan children between the ages of 6 and 10 years. The city was named as trustee and provided for the administration of the college through a city board of directors. The city claimed that the Fourteenth Amendment made the restriction to white children unconstitutional. The court held: 1) that the decedent was entitled to prescribe a method of selection for admission to the college unless there was a violation of an affirmative provision of law; 2) that private trusts for charitable purposes, not subject to or controlled by state action, were beyond the scope of the Fourteenth Amendment; 3) that the city's fiduciary duties were separate from its ordinary governmental functions; 4) that the administration of the trust by the city did not represent state action; 5) that even if the city were deemed to have engaged in state action, the trust did not fail, and the remedy was the substitution of another trustee; and 6) that the doctrine of cy pres was inapplicable because the objects of the trust were capable of being enforced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decrees of the trial court.

In re Mack


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 251; 126 A.2d 679; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 394


Argued January 13, 1956  
October 5, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 144-45, 154-58, March T., 1955, from judgment and sentences of Court of Quarter Sessions of the Peace and Court of Oyer and Terminer of Westmoreland County, No. 1, January T., 1955, in re attachment for contempt of David W. Mack. Judgment and sentences, as modified, affirmed.

Contempt proceeding. Before LAIRD, P.J., BAUER and O'CONNELL, JJ.

Defendants adjudged guilty of direct criminal contempt and sentenced. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: With the determination that the rules, so far as involved here, are reasonable, and not an abuse of the court's discretion, the judgment and sentences, as so modified, are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a judgment from the Court of Quarter Sessions of the Peace and Court of Oyer and Terminer of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which found defendants guilty of direct criminal contempt and sentenced them to a term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants took pictures of a criminal defendant who was being brought into the courtroom for sentencing, in violation of Westmoreland County Ct. R. 6084. The trial court found them guilty of criminal contempt, imposed a fine, and sentenced them to five days in custody. The court determined that Rule 6084 did not violate the First Amendment right to freedom of the press. The court found that Rule 6084 was imposed to regulate public order and was valid if it was a reasonable regulation. The court reasoned that the essential rights of the First Amendment were subject to the elemental need for order and were not absolute. The court determined that Rule 6084's regulation of the area outside of the courtroom was reasonable. The freedom of the press was not abridged by an order prohibiting newspapermen from seeing and hearing what transpired in a courtroom because they had no special right or privilege not possessed by other members of the public. Finally, the court noted that the trial court had the duty to protect the prisoner's right to privacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendants' convictions for contempt of court. The court modified defendants' sentences by striking the provision of imprisonment and leaving only the imposition of a fine and costs.

 

397 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania State Chamber of Commerce v. Torquato


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 306; 125 A.2d 755; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 395


Argued June 25, 1956  
October 1, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 10, 11 and 12, May T., 1957, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1956, No. 2192 Equity Docket, No. 136 Commonwealth Docket, 1956, in case of Pennsylvania State Chamber of Commerce et al. v. John R. Torquato, Secretary of the Department of Labor and Industry et al. Decree affirmed; reargument refused October 19, 1956.

Equity. Before RICHARDS, P.J., NEELY, SOHN and KREIDER, JJ.

Decree entered granting special injunction, opinion by NEELY, J. Plaintiffs and defendants, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; each party to pay its, his and their respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employer and unemployment compensation fund contributors (collectively contributors), and defendant state officials appealed a decision by the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) granting an injunction restraining the payment of unemployment compensation funds until an appeal of an underlying matter was heard. At issue was the constitutionality of § 501(e) of the Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 821.


OVERVIEW: The employer's employees went on strike. The employer refused to participate in binding arbitration and locked out the employees. The contributors appealed the award of unemployment benefits to the employees. However, the appeal did not act as a supersedeas to the payment of benefits. The contributors filed an action claiming that § 821 was unconstitutional because the appeal should have acted as a supersedeas. The lower court granted an injunction and the court affirmed the decision. The court held that the contributors were proper parties to the action as taxpayers and because of the potential loss to their funds. The court held that the payment of the benefits without judicial review violated due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, and Pa. Const. art. I, § 9. Because payment of benefits under 43 P.S. §§ 822, 824 would have resulted in irreparable harm to the contributors because retrieval of the funds would have been from the employees, equitable relief was appropriate. However, the Department of Labor and Industry's determinations of benefits was to continue consistent with the Unemployment Compensation Law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision, which was partially in favor of the contributors and state officials in the contributors' equitable and injunctive action regarding the state officials' payment of unemployment compensation benefits on the basis of whether such payment was constitutional.

 

398 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Lened Homes, Inc. v. Department of Licenses & Inspections


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 50; 123 A.2d 406; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 380


Argued May 25, 1956  
June 25, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 216, Jan. T., 1956, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1955, No. 6466, in the case of Lened Homes, Inc. v. Department of Licenses and Inspections of the City of Philadelphia. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon petition of city and rule to show cause why summary judgment entered in mandamus directing issuance of zoning use and building permits should not be opened.

Order entered denying petition, opinion by LEWIS, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, each party to pay its own respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a department of licenses and inspections of a city, appealed from an order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) dismissing the department's petition to open a summary judgment entered in favor of plaintiff builder in a dispute regarding the issuance of a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The builder purchased land when the city zoning ordinance permitted the construction of row houses. Two months later, the city amended the zoning ordinance to prohibit row house in the type of district that included the builder's land. The builder applied for a permit to erect row houses, but the application was refused, The builder challenged the refusal, and the court below declared the amendatory ordinance invalid. The case was remanded for disposition in accordance with the original ordinance. The builder again requested a permit, but another ordinance was enacted prohibiting row houses in the district in question. The builder filed a complaint in mandamus to compel the issuance of a permit, and the court below entered summary judgment in the builder's favor. The lower court denied the department's petition to open the summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that the court below did not abuse its discretion in refusing to open the judgment. It stated that the facts in the case fell within the principles enunciated in a case in which it was held that a zoning ordinance, when applied retroactively to the plaintiff's property, was special legislation and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

399 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Watson v. Pennsylvania Turnpike Com.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


386 Pa. 117; 125 A.2d 354; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 385


Argued May 21, 1956  
June 25, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction, No. 22, May T., 1956, sur special certiorari to Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, in case of David E. Wtson v. Pennsylvania Turnpike Commission et al. Record remanded for entry of judgment; reargument refused October 5, 1956.



DISPOSITION: The defendant members of the Pennsylvania Turnpike Commission are ordered and directed to accord forthwith to David E. Watson, the plaintiff, the duties, rights, privileges and emoluments of a member of the Commission for the term expiring June 4, 1961, and the Commission is ordered and directed to pay to the plaintiff so much of his salary from December 1, 1955, as remains unpaid at the time of his restoration to office; the costs of this proceeding to be borne by the Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On special certiorari to the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Pennsylvania, plaintiff appointee filed an action in mandamus to compel defendants, members of a state turnpike commission, to restore him to office as a member of the commission. The appointee argued that the governor lacked the power to remove him from office at his pleasure and that he could only be removed as provided in Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 36, § 652a et seq. (1937).


OVERVIEW: The governor appointed the appointee to serve as a member of a state turnpike commission. The appointee served in office until the members excluded him from meetings and divested him of authority to perform official acts on the grounds that the governor had removed the appointee by written notice. The appointee filed an action in mandamus to compel the members to accord him the rights and privileges of his appointed office, and, because of the evident issue of public importance involved, the court accepted certiorari. The court held that the attempted removal of the appointee from his office was without warrant of law. Accordingly, it found that the appointee was to be restored to the position. The governor lacked the power under Pa. Const. art. VI, § 4 to remove at his pleasure a member of the commission during his fixed term of office. Pa. Const. art. VI, § 4 had to be read in connection with Pa. Const. art. XII, § 1, which permitted the Pennsylvania Legislature the power to annex conditions of tenure. The legislatively annexed conditions of tenure provided in Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 36, § 652a et seq. (1937) determined the method by which the appointee could be removed from office.


OUTCOME: The court ordered and directed the members to accord the appointee the duties, rights, privileges, and emoluments of a member of the commission, and it ordered that the appointee be paid the salary he was due.

 

400 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Eastman Kodak Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


385 Pa. 607; 124 A.2d 100; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 511


Argued May 21, 1956  
June 25, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 21, May T., 1956, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Commonwealth Docket, 1953, No. 215, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Eastman Kodak Company. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused August 13, 1956.

Appeal by defendant from decision of Board of Finance and Revenue. Before NEELY, J.

Order entered sustaining appeal and judgment entered for defendant. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth of Pennsylvania challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Pennsylvania, which found in favor of appellee corporate taxpayer in the Commonwealth's action to collect taxes under Pennsylvania Corporation Income Tax Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 3420n (1951). The Commonwealth argued that the imposition of the tax did not violate the Interstate Commerce Clause.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a business corporation organized under the laws of another state, and it owned a manufacturing plant in a second state. The taxpayer was engaged in interstate commerce, and it manufactured and sold photographic equipment and supplies in many states. The taxpayer did not maintain an office in Pennsylvania and was not registered to do business in Pennsylvania, but some of its salesmen solicited business in Pennsylvania, and automobiles owned by the taxpayer were regularly used by its salesmen in Pennsylvania. The Commonwealth sought to impose a tax on the taxpayer's net income, and the taxpayer argued that the imposition of the tax violated the Interstate Commerce Clause. The trial court found in favor of the taxpayer, and the Commonwealth appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the tax was an attempted excise tax on the taxpayer's interstate commerce business out of which there were no local activities which could be considered as not an integral or realistically inseparable part of interstate commerce. Accordingly, the Law in its application to the taxpayer was a violation of the Interstate Commerce Clause and was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
